/techniques/T1588/006===========================
APT19 performed a watering hole attack on forbes.com in 2014 to compromise targets.[3]
APT32 has infected victims by tricking them into visiting compromised watering hole websites.[4][5]
APT37 has used strategic web compromises, particularly of South Korean websites, to distribute malware. The group has also used torrent file-sharing sites to more indiscriminately disseminate malware to victims. As part of their compromises, the group has used a Javascript based profiler called RICECURRY to profile a victim's web browser and deliver malicious code accordingly.[6][7]
APT38 has conducted watering holes schemes to gain initial access to victims.[8]
BRONZE BUTLER compromised three Japanese websites using a Flash exploit to perform watering hole attacks.[9]
Bundlore has been spread through malicious advertisements on websites.[10]
Dark Caracal leveraged a watering hole to serve up malicious code.[11]
Darkhotel used embedded iframes on hotel login portals to redirect selected victims to download malware.[12]
Dragonfly has has compromised targets via strategic web compromise (SWC) utilizing a custom exploit kit.[13]
Dragonfly 2.0 compromised legitimate organizations' websites to create watering holes to compromise victims.[14]
Elderwood has delivered zero-day exploits and malware to victims by injecting malicious code into specific public Web pages visited by targets within a particular sector.[15][16][17]
Grandoreiro has used compromised websites and Google Ads to bait victims into downloading its installer.[18][19]
KARAE was distributed through torrent file-sharing websites to South Korean victims, using a YouTube video downloader application as a lure.[7]
Lazarus Group delivered RATANKBA to victims via a compromised legitimate website.[20]
Leafminer has infected victims using watering holes.[21]
LoudMiner is typically bundled with pirated copies of Virtual Studio Technology (VST) for Windows and macOS.[22]
Machete has distributed Machete through a fake blog website.[23]
Patchwork has used watering holes to deliver files with exploits to initial victims.[24][25]
PLATINUM has sometimes used drive-by attacks against vulnerable browser plugins.[26]
POORAIM has been delivered through compromised sites acting as watering holes.[7]
PROMETHIUM has used watering hole attacks to deliver malicious versions of legitimate installers.[27]
REvil has infected victim machines through compromised websites and exploit kits.[28][29][30][31]
RTM has distributed its malware via the RIG and SUNDOWN exploit kits, as well as online advertising network Yandex.Direct.[32][33]
Threat Group-3390 has extensively used strategic web compromises to target victims.[34][35]
Turla has infected victims using watering holes.[36]
Windigo has distributed Windows malware via drive-by downloads.[37]
Windshift has used compromised websites to register custom URL schemes on a remote system.[38]
/techniques/T1189===========================
APT28 has conducted SQL injection attacks against organizations' external websites.[8] 
APT29 has exploited CVE-2019-19781 for Citrix, CVE-2019-11510 for Pulse Secure VPNs, CVE-2018-13379 for FortiGate VPNs, and CVE-2019-9670 in Zimbra software to gain access. They have also exploited CVE-2020-0688 against the Microsoft Exchange Control Panel to regain access to a network.[9][10]
APT39 has used SQL injection for initial compromise.[11]
APT41 exploited CVE-2020-10189 against Zoho ManageEngine Desktop Central, and CVE-2019-19781 to compromise Citrix Application Delivery Controllers (ADC) and gateway devices.[12]
Axiom has been observed using SQL injection to gain access to systems.[13][14]
BlackTech has exploited a buffer overflow vulnerability in Microsoft Internet Information Services (IIS) 6.0, CVE-2017-7269, in order to establish a new HTTP or command and control (C2) server.[15]
Blue Mockingbird has gained initial access by exploiting CVE-2019-18935, a vulnerability within Telerik UI for ASP.NET AJAX.[16]
Fox Kitten has exploited known vulnerabilities in Fortinet, PulseSecure, and Palo Alto VPN appliances.[17][18][19][20][21]
GALLIUM exploited a publicly-facing servers including Wildfly/JBoss servers to gain access to the network.[22][23]
GOLD SOUTHFIELD has exploited Oracle WebLogic vulnerabilities for initial compromise.[24]
Havij is used to automate SQL injection.[25]
Night Dragon has performed SQL injection attacks of extranet web servers to gain access.[26]
Operation Wocao has gained initial access via vulnerable webservers.[27]
Rocke exploited Apache Struts, Oracle WebLogic (CVE-2017-10271), and Adobe ColdFusion (CVE-2017-3066) vulnerabilities to deliver malware.[28][29]
SoreFang can gain access by exploiting a Sangfor SSL VPN vulnerability that allows for the placement and delivery of malicious update binaries.[30]
sqlmap can be used to automate exploitation of SQL injection vulnerabilities.[31]
Volatile Cedar has targeted publicly facing web servers, with both automatic and manual vulnerability discovery.[32] [33] 
/techniques/T1190===========================
APT18 actors leverage legitimate credentials to log into external remote services.[4]
APT29 has used compromised identities to access VPNs and remote access tools.[5]
APT41 compromised an online billing/payment service using VPN access between a third-party service provider and the targeted payment service.[6]
Chimera has used legitimate credentials to login to an external VPN, Citrix, SSH, and other remote services.[7][8]
Doki was executed through an open Docker daemon API port.[9]
Dragonfly 2.0 used VPNs and Outlook Web Access (OWA) to maintain access to victim networks.[10][11]
FIN5 has used legitimate VPN, Citrix, or VNC credentials to maintain access to a victim environment.[12][13][14]
GALLIUM has used VPN services, including SoftEther VPN, to access and maintain persistence in victim environments.[15][16]
GOLD SOUTHFIELD has used publicly-accessible RDP and remote management and monitoring (RMM) servers to gain access to victim machines.[17] 
Hildegard was executed through an unsecure kubelet that allowed anonymous access to the victim environment.[3]
Ke3chang regained access after eviction via the corporate VPN solution with a stolen VPN certificate, which they had extracted from a compromised host.[18]
Kimsuky has used RDP to establish persistence.[19]
Kinsing was executed in an Ubuntu container deployed via an open Docker daemon API.[20]
Linux Rabbit attempts to gain access to the server via SSH.[21]
Night Dragon has used compromised VPN accounts to gain access to victim systems.[22]
OilRig uses remote services such as VPN, Citrix, or OWA to persist in an environment.[23]
Operation Wocao has used stolen credentials to connect to the victim's network via VPN.[24]
Sandworm Team has used Dropbear SSH with a hardcoded backdoor password to maintain persistence within the target network. Sandworm Team has also used VPN tunnels established in legitimate software company infrastructure to gain access to internal networks of that software company's users.[25][26][27]
TEMP.Veles has used a VPN to persist in the victim environment.[28]
Threat Group-3390 actors look for and use VPN profiles during an operation to access the network using external VPN services.[29] Threat Group-3390 has also obtained OWA account credentials during intrusions that it subsequently used to attempt to regain access when evicted from a victim network.[30]
Wizard Spider has accessed victim networks by using stolen credentials to access the corporate VPN infrastructure.[31]

/techniques/T1566/003===========================
Agent.btz drops itself onto removable media devices and creates an autorun.inf file with an instruction to run that file. When the device is inserted into another system, it opens autorun.inf and loads the malware.[1]
APT28 uses a tool to infect connected USB devices and transmit itself to air-gapped computers when the infected USB device is inserted.[2]
Part of APT28's operation involved using CHOPSTICK modules to copy itself to air-gapped machines and using files written to USB sticks to transfer data and command traffic.[3][2]
Darkhotel's selective infector modifies executables stored on removable media as a method of spreading across computers.[4]
DustySky searches for removable media and duplicates itself onto it.[5]
Flame contains modules to infect USB sticks and spread laterally to other Windows systems the stick is plugged into using Autorun functionality.[6]
H1N1 has functionality to copy itself to removable media.[7]
Mustang Panda has used a customized PlugX variant which could spread through USB connections.[8]
njRAT can be configured to spread via removable drives.[9][10]
Ramsay can spread itself by infecting other portable executable files on removable drives.[11] 
APT30 may have used the SHIPSHAPE malware to move onto air-gapped networks. SHIPSHAPE targets removable drives to spread to other systems by modifying the drive to use Autorun to execute or by hiding legitimate document files and copying an executable to the folder with the same name as the legitimate document.[12]
Tropic Trooper has attempted to transfer USBferry from an infected USB device by copying an Autorun function to the target machine.[13]
Unknown Logger is capable of spreading to USB devices.[14]
Ursnif has copied itself to and infected removable drives for propagation.[15][16]
USBferry can copy its installer to attached USB storage devices.[13]
USBStealer drops itself onto removable media and relies on Autorun to execute the malicious file when a user opens the removable media on another system.[17]
/techniques/T1091===========================
/techniques/T1195/001===========================
APT29 gained initial network access to some victims via a trojanized update of SolarWinds Orion software.[3]
APT41 gained access to production environments where they could inject malicious code into legitimate, signed files and widely distribute them to end users.[4]
CCBkdr was added to a legitimate, signed version 5.33 of the CCleaner software and distributed on CCleaner's distribution site.[5][6][1]
Cobalt Group has compromised legitimate web browser updates to deliver a backdoor. [7]
Dragonfly has placed trojanized installers on legitimate vendor app stores.[8]
GOLD SOUTHFIELD has distributed ransomware by backdooring software installers via a strategic web compromise of the site hosting Italian WinRAR.[9][10][11]
GoldenSpy has been packaged with a legitimate tax preparation software.[12]
Sandworm Team has distributed NotPetya by compromising the legitimate Ukrainian accounting software M.E.Doc and replacing a legitimate software update with a malicious one.[13][14][15]
SUNSPOT malware was designed and used to insert SUNBURST into software builds of the SolarWinds Orion IT management product.[16]

/techniques/T1078/001===========================
APT29 has used valid accounts, including administrator accounts, to help facilitate lateral movement on compromised networks.[3][4]
APT3 leverages valid accounts after gaining credentials for use within the victim domain.[5]
Chimera has used compromised domain accounts to gain access to the target environment.[6]
Cobalt Strike can use known credentials to run commands and spawn processes as a domain user account.[7][8]
Indrik Spider has collected credentials from infected systems, including domain accounts.[9]
Operation Wocao has used domain credentials, including domain admin, for lateral movement and privilege escalation.[10]
Ryuk can use stolen domain admin accounts to move laterally within a victim domain.[11]
Sandworm Team has used stolen credentials to access administrative accounts within the domain.[12]
If Shamoon cannot access shares using current privileges, it attempts access using hard coded, domain-specific credentials gathered earlier in the intrusion.[13][14]
TA505 has used stolen domain admin accounts to compromise additional hosts.[15]
Threat Group-1314 actors used compromised domain credentials for the victim's endpoint management platform, Altiris, to move laterally.[16]
Wizard Spider has used administrative accounts, including Domain Admin, to move laterally within a victim network.[17]

Ramsay can use Windows API functions such as WriteFile, CloseHandle, and GetCurrentHwProfile during its collection and file storage operations. Ramsay can execute its embedded components via CreateProcessA and ShellExecute.[68]
RDFSNIFFER has used several Win32 API functions to interact with the victim machine.[69]
REvil can use Native API for execution and to retrieve active services.[70][71]
Rising Sun used dynamic API resolutions to various Windows APIs by leveraging LoadLibrary() and GetProcAddress().[72]
RTM can use the FindNextUrlCacheEntryA and FindFirstUrlCacheEntryA functions to search for specific strings within browser history.[73]
Ryuk has used multiple native APIs including ShellExecuteW to run executables,GetWindowsDirectoryW to create folders, and VirtualAlloc, WriteProcessMemory, and CreateRemoteThread for process injection.[74]
Sharpshooter's first-stage downloader resolved various Windows libraries and APIs, including LoadLibraryA(), GetProcAddress(), and CreateProcessA().[72] 
ShimRat has used Windows API functions to install the service and shim.[75] 
ShimRatReporter used several Windows API functions to gather information from the infected system.[75]
Silence has leveraged the Windows API, including using CreateProcess() or ShellExecute(), to perform a variety of tasks.[76][77]
SUNSPOT used Windows API functions such as MoveFileEx and NtQueryInformationProcess as part of the SUNBURST injection process.[78] 
SynAck parses the export tables of system DLLs to locate and call various Windows API functions.[79][80]
TrickBot uses the Windows API call, CreateProcessW(), to manage execution flow.[81]
Tropic Trooper has used multiple Windows APIs including HttpInitialize, HttpCreateHttpHandle, and HttpAddUrl.[82]
Turla and its RPC backdoors have used APIs calls for various tasks related to subverting AMSI and accessing then executing commands through RPC and/or named pipes.[83]
Ursnif has used CreateProcessW to create child processes.[84]
Volgmer executes payloads using the Windows API call CreateProcessW().[85]
Waterbear can leverage API functions for execution.[86]
WindTail can invoke Apple APIs contentsOfDirectoryAtPath, pathExtension, and (string) compare.[87]
XAgentOSX contains the execFile function to execute a specified file on the system using the NSTask:launch method.[88]
/techniques/T1106===========================

at can be used to schedule a task on a system.[2]

CrackMapExec can set a scheduled task on the target system to execute commands remotely using at.[4]
MURKYTOP has the capability to schedule remote AT jobs.[5]
Threat Group-3390 actors use at to schedule tasks to run self-extracting RAR archives, which install HTTPBrowser or PlugX on other victims on a network.[6]
/techniques/T1053/002===========================
Agent Tesla  has achieved persistence via scheduled tasks.[1] 
Anchor can create a scheduled task for persistence.[2]
AppleJeus has created a scheduled SYSTEM task that runs when a user logs in.[3]
APT-C-36 has used a macro function to set scheduled tasks, disguised as those used by Google.[4]
APT29 used scheduler and schtasks to create new tasks on remote hosts as part of lateral movement.[5] They have manipulated scheduled tasks by updating an existing legitimate task to execute their tools and then returned the scheduled task to its original configuration.[6] APT29 also created a scheduled task to maintain SUNSPOT persistence when the host booted during the 2020 SolarWinds intrusion.[7] They previously used named and hijacked scheduled tasks to also establish persistence.[8]
An APT3 downloader creates persistence by creating the following scheduled task: schtasks /create /tn "mysc" /tr C:\Users\Public\test.exe /sc ONLOGON /ru "System".[9]

SYSCON has been executed by luring victims to open malicious e-mail attachments.[140]
TA459 has attempted to get victims to open malicious Microsoft Word attachment sent via spearphishing.[141]
TA505 has used lures to get users to enable content in malicious attachments and execute malicious files contained in archives. For example, TA505 makes their malware look like legitimate Microsoft Word documents, .pdf and/or .lnk files. [142][143][144][145][146][147][148][149][150]
TA551 has prompted users to enable macros within spearphishing attachments to install malware.[151]
The White Company has used phishing lure documents that trick users into opening them and infecting their computers.[152]
TrickBot has attempted to get users to launch malicious documents to deliver its payload. [153][154]
Tropic Trooper has lured victims into executing malware via malicious e-mail attachments.[155]
A Word document delivering TYPEFRAME prompts the user to enable macro execution.[156]
Valak has been executed via Microsoft Word documents containing malicious macros.[157][158][159]
Whitefly has used malicious .exe or .dll files disguised as documents or images.[160]
Windshift has used e-mail attachments to lure victims into executing malicious code.[161]
Wizard Spider has lured victims to execute malware with spearphishing attachments containing macros to download either Emotet, Bokbot, or TrickBot.[162]
/techniques/T1204/002===========================

/techniques/T1047===========================
APT29 added their own devices as allowed IDs for active sync using Set-CASMailbox, allowing it to obtain copies of victim mailboxes. It also added additional permissions (such as Mail.Read and Mail.ReadWrite) to compromised Application or Service Principals.[5][6]
Magic Hound granted compromised email accounts read access to the email boxes of additional targeted accounts. The group then was able to authenticate to the intended victim's OWA (Outlook Web Access) portal and read hundreds of email communications for information on Middle East organizations.[2]

/techniques/T1547/004===========================
Empire can enumerate Security Support Providers (SSPs) as well as utilize PowerSploit's Install-SSP and Invoke-Mimikatz to install malicious SSPs and log authentication events.[2]

/techniques/T1176===========================
Bonadan has maliciously altered the OpenSSH binary on targeted systems to create a backdoor.[1]

Kessel has maliciously altered the OpenSSH binary on targeted systems to create a backdoor.[1]
ThiefQuest searches through the /Users/ folder looking for executable files. For each executable, ThiefQuest prepends a copy of itself to the beginning of the file. When the file is executed, the ThiefQuest code is executed first. ThiefQuest creates a hidden file, copies the original target executable to the file, then executes the new hidden file to maintain the appearance of normal behavior. [3][4]

/techniques/T1546/009===========================
APT39 has used malware to set LoadAppInit_DLLs in the Registry key SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows NT\CurrentVersion\Windows in order to establish persistence.[4]
Some variants of Cherry Picker use AppInit_DLLs to achieve persistence by creating the following Registry key: HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows NT\CurrentVersion\Windows "AppInit_DLLs"="pserver32.dll"[5]
Ramsay can insert itself into the address space of other applications using the AppInit DLL Registry key.[6] 
If a victim meets certain criteria, T9000 uses the AppInit_DLL functionality to achieve persistence by ensuring that every user mode process that is spawned will load its malicious DLL, ResN32.dll. It does this by creating the following Registry keys: HKLM\Software\Microsoft\Windows NT\CurrentVersion\Windows\AppInit_DLLs – %APPDATA%\Intel\ResN32.dll and HKLM\Software\Microsoft\Windows NT\CurrentVersion\Windows\LoadAppInit_DLLs – 0x1.[7]

Prikormka uses DLL search order hijacking for persistence by saving itself as ntshrui.dll to the Windows directory so it will load before the legitimate ntshrui.dll saved in the System32 subdirectory.[25]
Ramsay can hijack outdated Windows application dependencies with malicious versions of its own DLL payload.[26] 
RedLeaves is launched through use of DLL search order hijacking to load a malicious dll.[27]
RTM has used search order hijacking to force TeamViewer to load a malicious DLL.[28]
Threat Group-3390 has performed DLL search order hijacking to execute their payload.[29]
Variants of WEBC2 achieve persistence by using DLL search order hijacking, usually by copying the DLL file to %SYSTEMROOT% (C:\WINDOWS\ntshrui.dll).[30]
Whitefly has used search order hijacking to run the loader Vcrodat.[31] 
/techniques/T1574/001===========================
APT19 launched an HTTP malware variant and a Port 22 malware variant using a legitimate executable that loaded the malicious DLL.[2]
APT3 has been known to side load DLLs with a valid version of Chrome with one of their tools.[3][4]
APT32 ran legitimately-signed executables from Symantec and McAfee which load a malicious DLL. The group also side-loads its backdoor by dropping a library and a legitimate, signed executable (AcroTranscoder).[5][6][7]
APT41 used legitimate executables to perform DLL side-loading of their malware.[8] 
BADNEWS typically loads its DLL file into a legitimate signed Java or VMware executable.[9][10]
DLL side-loading has been used to execute BBSRAT through a legitimate Citrix executable, ssonsvr.exe. The Citrix executable was dropped along with BBSRAT by the dropper.[11]
BlackTech has used DLL side loading by giving DLLs hardcoded names and placing them in searched directories.[12] 
BRONZE BUTLER has used legitimate applications to side-load malicious DLLs.[13]
Chimera has used side loading to place malicious DLLs in memory.[14]
Denis exploits a security vulnerability to load a fake DLL and execute its code.[5]
Egregor has used DLL side-loading to execute its payload.[15] 
FinFisher uses DLL side-loading to load malicious programs.[16][17]
GALLIUM used DLL side-loading to covertly load PoisonIvy into memory on the victim machine.[18]
A gh0st RAT variant has used DLL side-loading.[19]
Goopy has the ability to side-load malicious DLLs with legitimate applications from Kaspersky, Microsoft, and Google.[6]
Higaisa’s JavaScript file used a legitimate Microsoft Office 2007 package to side-load the OINFO12.OCX dynamic link library.[20]
HTTPBrowser has used DLL side-loading.[21]
HyperBro has used a legitimate application to sideload a DLL to decrypt, decompress, and run a payload.[22]
Javali can use DLL side-loading to load malicious DLLs into legitimate executables.[23]
LookBack side loads its communications module as a DLL into the libcurl.dll loader.[24]
menuPass has used DLL side-loading to launch versions of Mimikatz and PwDump6 as well as UPPERCUT.[25][26][27]
Metamorfo has side-loaded its malicious DLL file.[28][29]
Mustang Panda has used a legitimately signed executable to execute a malicious payload within a DLL file.[30][31][32]
Naikon has used DLL side-loading to load malicious DLL's into legitimate executables.[33]
OwaAuth has been loaded onto Exchange servers and disguised as an ISAPI filter (DLL file). The IIS w3wp.exe process then loads the malicious DLL.[21]
A Patchwork .dll that contains BADNEWS is loaded and executed using DLL side-loading.[34]
PlugX has used DLL side-loading to evade anti-virus.[4][21][35][25][36]
Sakula uses DLL side-loading, typically using a digitally signed sample of Kaspersky Anti-Virus (AV) 6.0 for Windows Workstations or McAfee's Outlook Scan About Box to load malicious DLL files.[37]
Sidewinder has used DLL side-loading to drop and execute malicious payloads including the hijacking of the legitimate Windows application file rekeywiz.exe.[38]
During the T9000 installation process, it drops a copy of the legitimate Microsoft binary igfxtray.exe. The executable contains a side-loading weakness which is used to load a portion of the malware.[39]
Threat Group-3390 has used DLL side-loading, including by using legitimate Kaspersky antivirus variants in which the DLL acts as a stub loader that loads and executes the shell code.[21][40][41][22]
Tropic Trooper has been known to side-load DLLs using a valid version of a Windows Address Book and Windows Defender executable with one of their tools.[42][43]
Waterbear has used DLL side loading to import and load a malicious DLL loader.[12] 
Wingbird side loads a malicious file, sspisrv.dll, in part of a spoofed lssas.exe service.[44][45]
ZeroT has used DLL side-loading to load malicious payloads.[46][47]

China Chopper's server component is a Web Shell payload.[1]
Deep Panda uses Web shells on publicly accessible Web servers to access victim networks.[5]
Dragonfly 2.0 commonly created Web shells on victims' publicly accessible email and web servers, which they used to maintain access to a victim network and download additional malicious files.[6][7]

Leviathan relies on web shells for an initial foothold as well as persistence into the victim's systems. [16]
OilRig has used web shells, often to maintain access to a victim network.[17][18][19]
Operation Wocao has used their own web shells, as well as those previously placed on target systems by other threat actors, for reconnaissance and lateral movement.[20]

P.A.S. Webshell can gain remote access and execution on target web servers.[21]

/techniques/T1548/001===========================
AppleJeus has presented the user with a UAC prompt to elevate privileges while installing.[9]
APT29 has bypassed UAC.[10]
APT37 has a function in the initial dropper to bypass Windows UAC in order to execute the next payload with higher privileges.[11]
AutoIt backdoor attempts to escalate privileges by bypassing User Access Control.[12]
BitPaymer can suppress UAC prompts by setting the HKCU\Software\Classes\ms-settings\shell\open\command registry key on Windows 10 or HKCU\Software\Classes\mscfile\shell\open\command on Windows 7 and launching the eventvwr.msc process, which launches BitPaymer with elevated privileges.[13]
BlackEnergy attempts to bypass default User Access Control (UAC) settings by exploiting a backward-compatibility setting found in Windows 7 and later.[14]
BRONZE BUTLER has used a Windows 10 specific tool and xxmm to bypass UAC for privilege escalation.[15][16]
Cobalt Group has bypassed UAC.[17]
Cobalt Strike can use a number of known techniques to bypass Windows UAC.[18]
CSPY Downloader can bypass UAC using the SilentCleanup task to execute the binary with elevated privileges.[19]
Downdelph bypasses UAC to escalate privileges by using a custom "RedirectEXE" shim database.[20]
Empire includes various modules to attempt to bypass UAC for escalation of privileges.[21]
Evilnum has used PowerShell to bypass UAC.[22]
FinFisher performs UAC bypass.[23][24]
Grandoreiro can bypass UAC by registering as the default handler for .MSC files.[25]
H1N1 bypasses user access control by using a DLL hijacking vulnerability in the Windows Update Standalone Installer (wusa.exe).[26]
Honeybee uses a combination of NTWDBLIB.dll and cliconfg.exe to bypass UAC protections using DLL hijacking.[27]
InvisiMole can use fileless UAC bypass and create an elevated COM object to escalate privileges.[28][29]
Koadic has 2 methods for elevating integrity. It can bypass UAC through eventvwr.exe and sdclt.exe.[30]
KONNI bypassed UAC with the "AlwaysNotify" settings.[31]
MuddyWater uses various techniques to bypass UAC.[32]
Patchwork bypassed User Access Control (UAC).[33]
PipeMon installer can use UAC bypass techniques to install the payload.[34]
An older variant of PLAINTEE performs UAC bypass.[35]
PoshC2 can utilize multiple methods to bypass UAC.[36]
Pupy can bypass Windows UAC through either DLL hijacking, eventvwr, or appPaths.[37]
Ramsay can use UACMe for privilege escalation.[38][39] 
Remcos has a command for UAC bypassing.[40]
RTM can attempt to run the program as admin, then show a fake error message and a legitimate UAC bypass prompt to the user in an attempt to socially engineer the user into escalating privileges.[41]
Sakula contains UAC bypass code for both 32- and 64-bit systems.[42]
Shamoon attempts to disable UAC remote restrictions by modifying the Registry.[43]
ShimRat has hijacked the cryptbase.dll within migwiz.exe to escalate privileges. This prevented the User Access Control window from appearing.[44]
A Threat Group-3390 tool can use a public UAC bypass method to elevate privileges.[45]
UACMe contains many methods for bypassing Windows User Account Control on multiple versions of the operating system.[5]
Many ZeroT samples can perform UAC bypass by using eventvwr.exe to execute a malicious file.[46]

Ramsay can use ImprovedReflectiveDLLInjection to deploy components.[42]

/techniques/T1055/013===========================

Astaroth can create a new process in a suspended state from a targeted legitimate process in order to unmap its memory and replace it with malicious code.[4][5]

Cobalt Strike can use process hollowing for execution.[14]

Dtrack has used process hollowing shellcode to target a predefined list of processes from %SYSTEM32%.[16]
Duqu is capable of loading executable code via process hollowing.[17]
Gorgon Group malware can use process hollowing to inject one of its trojans into another process.[18]

DropBook can unarchive data downloaded from the C2 to obtain the payload and persistence modules.[44] 
Drovorub has de-obsfuscated XOR encrypted payloads in WebSocket messages.[45]
Dtrack has used a decryption routine that is part of an executable physical patch.[46]
Dyre decrypts resources needed for targeting the victim.[47][48]
Ebury has verified C2 domain ownership by decrypting the TXT record using an embedded RSA public key.[49]
Egregor has been decrypted before execution.[50][51] 
Exaramel for Linux can decrypt its configuration file.[52]
Expand can be used to decompress a local or remote CAB file into an executable.[53]
FatDuke can decrypt AES encrypted C2 communications.[54]
Final1stspy uses Python code to deobfuscate base64-encoded strings.[55]
FinFisher extracts and decrypts stage 3 malware, which is stored in encrypted resources.[56][57]
Frankenstein has deobfuscated base64-encoded commands following the execution of a malicious script, which revealed a small script designed to obtain an additional payload.[58] 
Gamaredon Group tools decrypted additional payloads from the C2. Gamaredon Group has also decoded base64-encoded source code of a downloader.[59][60]
gh0st RAT has decrypted and loaded the gh0st RAT DLL into memory, once the initial dropper executable is launched.[61]
GoldMax has decoded and decrypted the configuration file when executed.[62][63]
Goopy has used a polymorphic decryptor to decrypt itself at runtime.[43]
Gorgon Group malware can decode contents from a payload that was Base64 encoded and write the contents to a file.[64]
Grandoreiro can decrypt its encrypted internal strings.[65]
Hancitor has decoded Base64 encoded URLs to insert a recipient’s name into the filename of the Word document. Hancitor has also extracted executables from ZIP files.[66][67]
HiddenWasp uses a cipher to implement a decoding function.[68]
Higaisa used certutil to decode Base64 binaries at runtime and a 16-byte XOR key to decrypt data.[69][70]
Hildegard has decrypted ELF files with AES.[71]
Honeybee drops a Word file containing a Base64-encoded file in it that is read, decoded, and dropped to the disk by the macro.[72]
Imminent Monitor has decoded malware components that are then dropped to the system.[73]
InvisiMole can decrypt, unpack and load a DLL from its resources, or from blobs encrypted with Data Protection API, two-key triple DES, and variations of the XOR cipher.[74][75]
IronNetInjector has the ability to decrypt embedded .NET and PE payloads.[76]
ISMInjector uses the certutil command to decode a payload file.[77]
Kessel has decrypted the binary's configuration once the main function was launched.[78]
KGH_SPY can decrypt encrypted strings and write them to a newly created folder.[79]
KONNI has used certutil to download and decode base64 encoded strings.[80] 
Kwampirs decrypts and extracts a copy of its main DLL payload when executing.[81]
Leviathan has used a DLL known as SeDll to decrypt and execute other JavaScript backdoors.[82]
LightNeuron has used AES and XOR to decrypt configuration files and commands.[83]
LookBack has a function that decrypts malicious data.[84]
Lucifer can decrypt its C2 address upon execution.[85]
Machete’s downloaded data is decrypted using AES.[86]
MegaCortex has used a Base64 key to decode its components.[87]
menuPass has used certutil in a macro to decode base64-encoded content contained in a dropper document attached to an email. The group has also used certutil -decode to decode files on the victim’s machine when dropping UPPERCUT.[88][89]
After checking for the existence of two files, keyword_parm.txt and parm.txt, MESSAGETAP XOR decodes and read the contents of the files. [90]
Upon execution, Metamorfo has unzipped itself after being downloaded to the system.[91][92] 
MirageFox has a function for decrypting data containing C2 configuration information.[93]
Molerats decompresses ZIP files once on the victim machine.[94]
More_eggs will decode malware components that are then dropped to the system.[95]
MuddyWater decoded base64-encoded PowerShell commands using a VBS file.[96][97][98]
Netwalker's PowerShell script can decode and decrypt multiple layers of obfuscation, leading to the Netwalker DLL being loaded into memory.[99]
NOKKI uses a unique, custom de-obfuscation technique.[100]
A OilRig macro has run a PowerShell command to decode file contents. OilRig has also used certutil to decode base64-encoded files on victims.[101][77][102][103]
Okrum's loader can decrypt the backdoor code, embedded within the loader or within a legitimate PNG file. A custom XOR cipher or RC4 is used for decryption.[104]
OnionDuke can use a custom decryption algorithm to decrypt strings.[54]
OopsIE concatenates then decompresses multiple resources to load an embedded .Net Framework assembly.[102]
OSX/Shlayer can base64-decode and AES-decrypt downloaded payloads.[105]
P.A.S. Webshell can use a decryption mechanism to process a user supplied password and allow execution.[52]
Pillowmint has been decompressed by included shellcode prior to being launched.[106] 
PipeMon can decrypt password-protected executables.[107]
PlugX decompresses and decrypts itself using the Microsoft API call RtlDecompressBuffer.[108]
PoetRAT has used LZMA and base64 libraries to decode obfuscated scripts.[109]
PolyglotDuke can use a custom algorithm to decrypt strings used by the malware.[54]
POWERSTATS can deobfuscate the main backdoor code.[98]
Proton uses an encrypted file to store commands and configuration values.[110]
PUNCHBUGGY has used PowerShell to decode base64-encoded assembly.[111]
QUADAGENT uses AES and a preshared key to decrypt the custom Base64 routine used to encode strings and scripts.[112]
Raindrop decrypted its Cobalt Strike payload using an AES-256 encryption algorithm in CBC mode with a unique key per sample.[10][113]
Ramsay can extract its agent from the body of a malicious document.[114] 
RDAT can deobfuscate the base64-encoded and AES-encrypted files downloaded from the C2 server.[115] 
RegDuke can decrypt strings with a key either stored in the Registry or hardcoded in the code.[54]
Remexi decrypts the configuration data using XOR with 25-character keys.[116]
REvil can decode encrypted strings to enable execution of commands and payloads.[117][118][119][120][121][122]
RGDoor decodes Base64 strings and decrypts strings using a custom XOR algorithm.[123]
Rising Sun decrypted itself using a single-byte XOR scheme. Additionally, Rising Sun can decrypt its configuration data at runtime.[124] 
Rocke has extracted tar.gz files after downloading them from a C2 server.[125]
RogueRobin decodes an embedded executable using base64 and decompresses it.[126]
Sandworm Team's VBS backdoor can decode Base64-encoded data and save it to the %TEMP% folder. The group also decrypted received information using the Triple DES algorithm and decompresses it using GZip.[127][128]
SDBbot has the ability to decrypt and decompress its payload to enable code execution.[129][130]
ShadowPad has decrypted a binary blob to start execution.[131]
Shamoon decrypts ciphertext using an XOR cipher and a base64-encoded string.[132] 
SharpStage has decompressed data received from the C2 server.[133]
ShimRat has decompressed its core DLL using shellcode once an impersonated antivirus component was running on a system.[134]
Sibot can decrypt data received from a C2 and save to a file.[62]
Skidmap has the ability to download, unpack, and decrypt tar.gz files .[135] 
Smoke Loader deobfuscates its code.[136]
SoreFang can decode and decrypt exfiltrated data sent to C2.[137]
Spark has used a custom XOR algorithm to decrypt the payload.[138] 
SQLRat has scripts that are responsible for deobfuscating additional scripts.[139]
Starloader decrypts and executes shellcode from a file called Stars.jps.[140]
SUNSPOT decrypts SUNBURST, which was stored in AES128-CBC encrypted blobs.[141] 
TEARDROP was decoded using a custom rolling XOR algorithm to execute a customized Cobalt Strike payload.[142][143][113]
During execution, Threat Group-3390 malware deobfuscates and decompresses code that was encoded with Metasploit’s shikata_ga_nai encoder as well as compressed with LZNT1 compression.[144]
TrickBot decodes the configuration data and modules.[145][146]
Tropic Trooper used shellcode with an XOR algorithm to decrypt a payload. Tropic Trooper also decrypted image files which contained a payload.[147][148]
TSCookie has the ability to decrypt, load, and execute a DLL and its resources.[149]
Turla has used a custom decryption routine, which pulls key and salt values from other artifacts such as a WMI filter or PowerShell Profile, to decode encrypted PowerShell payloads.[150]
One TYPEFRAME variant decrypts an archive using an RC4 key, then decompresses and installs the decrypted malicious DLL module. Another variant decodes the embedded file by XORing it with the value "0x35".[151]
Ursnif has used crypto key information stored in the Registry to decrypt Tor clients dropped to disk.[152]
Valak has the ability to decode and decrypt downloaded files.[153][154]
VERMIN decrypts code, strings, and commands to use once it's on the victim's machine.[155]
Volgmer deobfuscates its strings and APIs once its executed.[156]
Waterbear has the ability to decrypt its RC4 encrypted payload for execution.[157]
WellMail can decompress scripts received from C2.[158]
WellMess can decode and decrypt data received from C2.[159][160][161]
WindTail has the ability to decrypt strings using hard-coded AES keys.[162]
Winnti for Linux has decoded XOR encoded strings holding its configuration upon execution.[163]
WIRTE has decoded a base64 encoded document which was embedded in a VBS script.[164]
YAHOYAH decrypts downloaded files before execution.[165]
Zebrocy decodes its secondary payload and writes it to the victim’s machine. Zebrocy also uses AES and XOR to decrypt strings and payloads.[166][167]
ZeroT shellcode decrypts and decompresses its RC4-encrypted payload.[168]
Zeus Panda decrypts strings in the code during the execution process.[169]
ZIRCONIUM has used the AES256 algorithm with a SHA1 derived key to decrypt exploit code.[170]

/techniques/T1006===========================
APT41 has encrypted payloads using the Data Protection API (DPAPI), which relies on keys tied to specific user accounts on specific machines. APT41 has also environmentally keyed second stage malware with an RC5 key derived in part from the infected system's volume serial number.[8]
Equation has been observed utilizing environmental keying in payload delivery.[2][9]
InvisiMole can use Data Protection API to encrypt its components on the victim’s computer, to evade detection, and to make sure the payload can only be decrypted and loaded on one specific compromised computer.[10]

/techniques/T1211===========================
BitPaymer can use icacls /reset and takeown /F to reset a targeted executable's permissions and then take ownership.[5]
Grandoreiro can modify the binary ACL to prevent security tools from running.[6]
JPIN can use the command-line utility cacls.exe to change file permissions.[7]
Ryuk can launch icacls  /grant Everyone:F /T /C /Q to delete every access-based restrictions on files and directories.[8]
WannaCry uses attrib +h and icacls . /grant Everyone:F /T /C /Q to make some of its files hidden and grant all users full access controls.[9]
Wizard Spider has used the icacls command to modify access control to backup servers, providing them with full control of all the system folders.[10]
/techniques/T1222/001===========================
APT32's macOS backdoor changes the permission of the file it wants to execute to 755.[3]
Kinsing has used chmod to modify permissions on key files for use.[4]
OSX/Shlayer can use the chmod utility to set a .app file as executable, and the spctl application to disable Gatekeeper protection for a downloaded file.[5].[5]
P.A.S. Webshell has the ability to modify file permissions.[6]
Penquin can add the executable flag to a downloaded file.[7]
Rocke has changed file permissions of files so they could not be modified.[8] 
/techniques/T1222/002===========================
Agent Tesla has created hidden folders.[4]
AppleJeus has added a leading . to plist filenames, unlisting them from the Finder app and default Terminal directory listings.[5]
APT28 has saved files with hidden file attributes.[6][6]
APT32's macOS backdoor hides the clientID file via a chflags function.[7]
Attor can set attributes of log files and directories to HIDDEN, SYSTEM, ARCHIVE, or a combination of those.[8]
BackConfig has the ability to set folders or files to be hidden from the Windows Explorer default view.[9]
Calisto uses a hidden directory named .calisto to store data from the victim’s machine before exfiltration.[10][11]
Carberp has created a hidden file in the Startup folder of the current user.[12]
CoinTicker downloads the following hidden files to evade detection and maintain persistence: /private/tmp/.info.enc, /private/tmp/.info.py, /private/tmp/.server.sh, ~/Library/LaunchAgents/.espl.plist, ~/Library/Containers/.[random string]/[random string].[13]
Dacls has had its payload named with a dot prefix to make it hidden from view in the Finder application.[14][15]
Explosive has commonly set file and path attributes to hidden.[16]
FruitFly saves itself with a leading "." to make it a hidden file.[17]
iKitten saves itself with a leading "." so that it's hidden from users by default.[17]
Imminent Monitor has a dynamic debugging feature to set the file attribute to hidden.[18]
InvisiMole can create hidden system directories.[19]
Ixeshe sets its own executable file's attributes to hidden.[20]
The Komplex payload is stored in a hidden directory at /Users/Shared/.local/kextd.[1]
Lazarus Group has used a VBA Macro to set its file attributes to System and Hidden and has named files with a dot prefix to hide them from the Finder application.[21][14][15]
Lokibot has the ability to copy itself to a hidden file and directory.[22]
LoudMiner has set the attributes of the VirtualBox directory and VBoxVmService parent directory to "hidden".[23]
Machete has the capability to exfiltrate stolen data to a hidden folder on a removable drive.[24]
MacSpy stores itself in ~/Library/.DS_Stores/ [25]
Micropsia creates a new hidden directory to store all components' outputs in a dedicated sub-folder for each.[26]
Mustang Panda's PlugX variant has created a hidden folder on USB drives named RECYCLE.BIN to store malicious executables and collected data.[27]
NETWIRE can copy itself to and launch itself from hidden folders.[28]
Before exfiltration, Okrum's backdoor has used hidden files to store logs and outputs from backdoor commands.[29]
OSX/Shlayer executes a .command script from a hidden directory in a mounted DMG.[30]
OSX_OCEANLOTUS.D sets the main loader file’s attributes to hidden.[31]
PoetRAT has the ability to hide and unhide files.[32]
Rising Sun can modify file attributes to hide files.[33]
Rocke downloaded a file "libprocesshider", which could hide files on the target system.[34][35]
SLOTHFULMEDIA has been created with a hidden attribute to insure it's not visible to the victim.[36]
ThiefQuest hides a copy of itself in the user's ~/Library directory by using a . at the beginning of the file name followed by 9 random characters.[37]
Tropic Trooper has created a hidden directory under C:\ProgramData\Apple\Updates\ and C:\Users\Public\Documents\Flash\.[38][39]
WannaCry uses attrib +h to make some of its files hidden.[40]

/techniques/T1564/003===========================
Anchor has used NTFS to hide files.[7]
APT32 used NTFS alternate data streams to hide their payloads.[8]
Astaroth can abuse alternate data streams (ADS) to store content for malicious payloads.[9]
BitPaymer has copied itself to the :bin alternate data stream of a newly created file.[10]
esentutl can be used to read and write alternate data streams.[11]
Expand can be used to download or copy a file into an alternate data stream.[12]
Gazer stores configuration items in alternate data streams (ADSs) if the Registry is not accessible.[13]
LoJax has loaded an embedded NTFS DXE driver to be able to access and write to NTFS partitions.[14]
PowerDuke hides many of its backdoor payloads in an alternate data stream (ADS).[15]
If the victim is using PowerShell 3.0 or later, POWERSOURCE writes its decoded payload to an alternate data stream (ADS) named kernel32.dll that is saved in %PROGRAMDATA%\Windows\.[16]
The Regin malware platform uses Extended Attributes to store encrypted executables.[17]
Valak has the ability save and execute files as alternate data streams (ADS).[18][19][20]
Some variants of the Zeroaccess Trojan have been known to store data in Extended Attributes.[21]
/techniques/T1564/004===========================
BOOTRASH has used unallocated disk space between partitions for a hidden file system that stores components of the Nemesis bootkit.[2]
ComRAT has used a portable FAT16 partition image placed in %TEMP% as a hidden file system.[3]
Equation has used an encrypted virtual file system stored in the Windows Registry.[4]
Regin has used a hidden file system to store some of its components.[5]
Strider has used a hidden file system that is stored as a file on disk.[6]
/techniques/T1564/005===========================
LoudMiner has used QEMU and VirtualBox to run a Tiny Core Linux virtual machine, which runs XMRig and makes connections to the C2 server for updates.[3]
Maze operators have used VirtualBox and a Windows 7 virtual machine to run the ransomware; the virtual machine's configuration file mapped the shared network drives of the target company, presumably so Maze can encrypt files on the shared drives as well as the local machine.[4] 
Ragnar Locker has used VirtualBox and a stripped Windows XP virtual machine to run itself. The use of a shared folder specified in the configuration enables Ragnar Locker to encrypt files on the host operating system, including files on any mapped drives.[2]

/techniques/T1564/007===========================
Agent Tesla has the capability to kill any running analysis processes and AV software.[1]

Bazar has manually loaded ntdll from disk in order to identity and remove API hooks set by security products.[3] 
Brave Prince terminates antimalware processes.[4]
BRONZE BUTLER has incorporated code into several tools that attempts to terminate anti-virus processes.[5]
Bundlore can change macOS security settings and browser preferences to enable follow-on behaviors.[6]
Carberp has attempted to disable security software by creating a suspended process for the security software and injecting code to delete antivirus core files when the process is resumed.[7]
ChChes can alter the victim's proxy configuration.[8]
Cobalt Strike has the ability to use Smart Applet attacks to disable the Java SecurityManager sandbox.[9]
DarkComet can disable Security Center functions like anti-virus.[10][11]

Egregor has disabled Windows Defender to evade protections.[13]
FIN6 has deployed a utility script named kill.bat to disable anti-virus.[14]

Goopy has the ability to disable Microsoft Outlook's security policies to disable macro warnings.[16] 
Gorgon Group malware can attempt to disable security features in Microsoft Office and Windows Defender using the taskkill command.[17]

Hildegard has modified DNS resolvers to evade DNS monitoring tools.[21]
Imminent Monitor has a feature to disable Windows Task Manager.[22] 
JPIN can lower security settings by changing Registry keys.[23]
Kimsuky has been observed turning off Windows Security Center.[24]

Additionally, Lazarus Group malware SHARPKNOT disables the Microsoft Windows System Event Notification and Alerter services.[25][26][27][28]. During a 2019 intrusion, Lazarus Group disabled Windows Defender and Credential Guard as some of their first actions on host.[29]

Maze has disabled dynamic analysis and other security tools including IDA debugger, x32dbg, and OllyDbg.[31] It has also disabled Windows Defender's Real-Time Monitoring feature and attempted to disable endpoint protection services.[32]

Metamorfo has a function to kill processes associated with defenses and can prevent certain processes from launching.[34][35]

Night Dragon has disabled anti-virus and anti-spyware tools in some instances on the victim’s machines. The actors have also disabled proxy settings to allow direct communication from victims to the Internet.[42]
POWERSTATS can disable Microsoft Office Protected View by changing Registry keys.[43]
Proton kills security tools like Wireshark that are running.[44]
Malware used by Putter Panda attempts to terminate processes corresponding to two components of Sophos Anti-Virus (SAVAdminService.exe and SavService.exe).[45]
Pysa has the capability to stop antivirus services and disable Windows Defender.[46] 
Ragnar Locker has attempted to terminate/stop processes and services associated with endpoint security products.[47]
REvil can connect to and disable the Symantec server on the victim's network.[48]
RobbinHood will search for Windows services that are associated with antivirus software on the system and kill the process.[49]

RunningRAT kills antimalware running process.[4]

SslMM identifies and kills anti-malware processes.[20]
StrongPity can add directories used by the malware to the Windows Defender exclusions list to prevent detection.[54]
SUNBURST attempted to disable software security services following checks against a FNV-1a + XOR hashed hardcoded blocklist.[55]
ThiefQuest uses the function kill_unwanted to obtain a list of running processes and kills each process matching a list of security related processes.[56]
TinyZBot can disable Avira anti-virus.[57]
TrickBot can disable Windows Defender.[58]
Turla has used a AMSI bypass, which patches the in-memory amsi.dll, in PowerShell scripts to bypass Windows antimalware products.[59]
Unknown Logger has functionality to disable security tools, including Kaspersky, BitDefender, and MalwareBytes.[60]

ZxShell can kill AV products' processes.[64]

/techniques/T1562/003===========================
APT29 used netsh to configure firewall rules that limited certain UDP outbound packets.[1]

Recent versions of Cherry Picker delete files and registry keys created by the malware.[32]
Chimera has performed file deletion to evade detection.[33] 
cmd can be used to delete files from the file system.[34]
Cobalt Group deleted the DLL dropper from the victim’s machine to cover their tracks.[35]

Derusbi is capable of deleting files. It has been observed loading a Linux Kernel Module (LKM) and then deleting it from the hard disk as well as overwriting the data with null bytes.[40][41]
Dragonfly 2.0 deleted many of its files used during operations as part of cleanup, including removing applications and deleting screenshots.[42][43]
Drovorub can delete specific files from a compromised host.[44]

/techniques/T1070/004===========================
InvisiMole can disconnect previously connected remote drives.[2]
The net use \system\share /delete command can be used in Net to remove an established connection to a network share.[1]
RobbinHood disconnects all network shares from the computer with the command net use * /DELETE /Y.[3]
Threat Group-3390 has detached network shares after exfiltrating files, likely to evade detection.[4]
/techniques/T1070/005===========================
3PARA RAT has a command to set certain attributes such as creation/modification timestamps on files.[2]
APT28 has performed timestomping on victim files.[3]
APT29 modified timestamps of backdoors to match legitimate Windows files.[4]
APT32 has used scheduled task raw XML with a backdated timestamp of June 2, 2016. The group has also set the creation time of the files dropped by the second stage of the exploit to match the creation time of kernel32.dll. Additionally, APT32 has used a random value to modify the timestamp of the file storing the clientID.[5][6][7]
Attor has manipulated the time of last access to files and registry keys after they have been created or modified.[8]
Bankshot modifies the time of a file as specified by the control server.[9]
BitPaymer can modify the timestamp of an executable so that it can be identified and restored by the decryption tool.[10]
BLINDINGCAN has modified file and directory timestamps.[11][12]
Chimera has used a Windows version of the Linux touch command to modify the date and time stamp on DLLs.[13]
China Chopper's server component can change the timestamp of files.[14][15][16]
Cobalt Strike can timestomp any files or payloads placed on a target machine to help them blend in.[17]
The Derusbi malware supports timestomping.[18][19]
Elise performs timestomping of a CAB file it creates.[20]
Empire can timestomp any files or payloads placed on a target machine to help them blend in.[21]
EVILNUM has changed the creation date of files.[22]
FALLCHILL can modify file or directory timestamps.[23]
For early Gazer versions, the compilation timestamp was faked.[24]
InvisiMole samples were timestomped by the authors by setting the PE timestamps to all zero values. InvisiMole also has a built-in command to modify file times.[25]
KeyBoy time-stomped its DLL in order to evade detection.[26]
Kimsuky has manipulated timestamps for creation or compilation dates to defeat anti-forensics.[27]
Several Lazarus Group malware families use timestomping, including modifying the last write timestamp of a specified Registry key to a random date, as well as copying the timestamp for legitimate .exe files (such as calc.exe or mspaint.exe) to its dropped files.[28][29][30][31]
Many Misdat samples were programmed using Borland Delphi, which will mangle the default PE compile timestamp of a file.[32]
OSX_OCEANLOTUS.D can use the touch command to change timestamps.[33]
OwaAuth has a command to timestop a file or directory.[34]
POSHSPY modifies timestamps of all downloaded executables to match a randomly selected file created prior to 2013.[35]
PowerStallion modifies the MAC times of its local log files to match that of the victim's desktop.ini file.[36]
Psylo has a command to conduct timestomping by setting a specified file’s timestamps to match those of a system file in the System32 directory.[37]
Rocke has changed the time stamp of certain files.[38] 
SEASHARPEE can timestomp files on victims using a Web shell.[39]
Shamoon can change the modified time for files to evade forensic detection.[40] 
TAINTEDSCRIBE can change the timestamp of specified filenames.[41]
After creating a new service for persistence, TDTESS sets the file creation time for the service to the creation time of the victim's legitimate svchost.exe file.[42]
TEMP.Veles used timestomping to modify the $STANDARD_INFORMATION attribute on tools.[43]
USBStealer sets the timestamps of its dropper files to the last-access and last-write timestamps of a standard Windows library chosen on the system.[44]
/techniques/T1070/006===========================
Forfiles can be used to subvert controls and possibly conceal command execution by not directly invoking cmd.[1][2]
Revenge RAT uses the Forfiles utility to execute commands on the system.[3]
/techniques/T1202===========================
APT37 has signed its malware with an invalid digital certificates listed as "Tencent Technology (Shenzhen) Company Limited."[2]
BADNEWS is sometimes signed with an invalid Authenticode certificate in an apparent effort to make it look more legitimate.[3]
The NETWIRE client has been signed by fake and invalid digital certificates.[4]
Regin stage 1 modules for 64-bit systems have been found to be signed with fake certificates masquerading as originating from Microsoft Corporation and Broadcom Corporation.[5]
Windshift has used revoked certificates to sign malware.[6][7]
WindTail has been incompletely signed with revoked certificates.[6]
/techniques/T1036/001===========================
BlackTech has used right-to-left-override to obfuscate the filenames of malicious e-mail attachments.[4]
BRONZE BUTLER has used Right-to-Left Override to deceive victims into executing several strains of malware.[5]
Ke3chang has used the right-to-left override character in spearphishing attachment names to trick targets into executing .scr and .exe files.[6]
Scarlet Mimic has used the left-to-right override character in self-extracting RAR archive spearphishing attachment file names.[7]
/techniques/T1036/002===========================
APT32 has moved and renamed pubprn.vbs to a .txt file to avoid detection.[4]
The CozyCar dropper has masqueraded a copy of the infected system's rundll32.exe executable that was moved to the malware's install directory and renamed according to a predefined configuration file.[3]
GALLIUM used a renamed cmd.exe file to evade detection.[5]
menuPass has renamed certutil and moved it to a different location on the system to avoid detection based on use of the tool.[6]
/techniques/T1036/003===========================
APT-C-36 has disguised its scheduled tasks as those used by Google.[5]
APT29 named tasks \Microsoft\Windows\SoftwareProtectionPlatform\EventCacheManager in order to appear legitimate.[6]
APT32 has used hidden or non-printing characters to help masquerade service names, such as appending a Unicode no-break space character to a legitimate service name. APT32 has also impersonated the legitimate Flash installer file name "install_flashplayer.exe".[7]
Attor's dispatcher disguises itself as a legitimate task (i.e., the task name and description appear legitimate).[8]
Bazar can create a task named to appear benign.[9]
build_downer has added itself to the Registry Run key as "NVIDIA" to appear legitimate.[10]
Carbanak has copied legitimate service names to use for malicious services.[11]
Catchamas adds a new service named NetAdapter in an apparent attempt to masquerade as a legitimate service.[12]
ComRAT has used a task name associated with Windows SQM Consolidator.[13]
Crutch has established persistence with a scheduled task impersonating the Outlook item finder.[14]
CSPY Downloader has attempted to appear as a legitimate Windows service with a fake description claiming it is used to support packed applications.[15]
Egregor has masqueraded the svchost.exe process to exfiltrate data.[16]
The Exaramel for Windows dropper creates and starts a Windows service named wsmprovav with the description "Windows Check AV" in an apparent attempt to masquerade as a legitimate service.[17]
FIN6 has renamed the "psexec" service name to "mstdc" to masquerade as a legitimate Windows service.[18] 
FIN7 has created a scheduled task named "AdobeFlashSync" to establish persistence.[19]
Fox Kitten has named the task for a reverse proxy lpupdate to appear legitimate.[20]
Fysbis has masqueraded as the rsyncd and dbus-inotifier services.[4]
GoldMax has impersonated systems management software to avoid detection.[21]
Higaisa named a shellcode loader binary svchast.exe to spoof the legitimate svchost.exe.[22][23] 
InnaputRAT variants have attempted to appear legitimate by adding a new service named OfficeUpdateService.[24]
InvisiMole has attempted to disguise itself by registering under a seemingly legitimate service name.[25]
IronNetInjector has been disguised as a legitimate service using the name PythonUpdateSrvc.[26]
Kimsuky has disguised services to appear as benign software or related to operating system functions.[27]
Kwampirs establishes persistence by adding a new service with the display name "WMI Performance Adapter Extension" in an attempt to masquerade as a legitimate WMI service.[28]
A Lazarus Group custom backdoor implant included a custom PE loader named "Security Package" that was added into the lsass.exe process via registry key.[29] 
Machete renamed task names to masquerade as legitimate Google Chrome, Java, Dropbox, Adobe Reader and Python tasks.[30] 
Maze operators have created scheduled tasks masquerading as "Windows Update Security", "Windows Update Security Patches", and "Google Chrome Security Update" designed to launch the ransomware.[31] 
Nidiran can create a new service named msamger (Microsoft Security Accounts Manager), which mimics the legitimate Microsoft database by the same name.[32][33]
Okrum can establish persistence by adding a new service NtmsSvc with the display name Removable Storage to masquerade as a legitimate Removable Storage Manager.[34]
OSX_OCEANLOTUS.D has disguised its app bundle by adding special characters to the filename and using the icon for legitimate Word documents.[35]
In one instance, menuPass added PlugX as a service with a display name of "Corel Writing Tools Utility."[36]
POWERSTATS has created a scheduled task named "MicrosoftEdge" to establish persistence.[37]
PROMETHIUM has named services to appear legitimate.[38][39]
New services created by RawPOS are made to appear like legitimate Windows services, with names such as "Windows Management Help Service", "Microsoft Support", and "Windows Advanced Task Manager".[40][41][42]
RDAT has used Windows Video Service as a name for malicious services.[43]
RTM has named the scheduled task it creates "Windows Update".[44]
Seasalt has masqueraded as a service called "SaSaut" with a display name of "System Authorization Service" in an apparent attempt to masquerade as a legitimate service.[45]
Shamoon creates a new service named "ntssrv" that attempts to appear legitimate; the service's display name is "Microsoft Network Realtime Inspection Service" and its description is "Helps guard against time change attempts targeting known and newly discovered vulnerabilities in network time protocols." Newer versions create the "MaintenaceSrv" service, which misspells the word "maintenance."[3][46]
ShimRat can impersonate Windows services and antivirus products to avoid detection on compromised systems.[47]
SLOTHFULMEDIA has named a service it establishes on victim machines as "TaskFrame" to hide its malicious purpose.[48] 
StrongPity has named services to appear legitimate.[38][39]
To establish persistence, Truvasys adds a Registry Run key with a value "TaskMgr" in an attempt to masquerade as the legitimate Windows Task Manager.[49]
Some Volgmer variants add new services with display names generated by a list of hard-coded strings such as Application, Background, Security, and Windows, presumably as a way to masquerade as a legitimate service.[50][51]
Wizard Spider has used scheduled tasks to install TrickBot, using task names to appear legitimate such as WinDotNet, GoogleTask, or Sysnetsf.[52] It has also used common document file names for other malware binaries.[53]
ZIRCONIUM has created a run key named Dropbox Update Setup to mask a persistence mechanism for a malicious binary.[54]
/techniques/T1036/004===========================
admin@338 actors used the following command to rename one of their tools to a benign file name: ren "%temp%\upload" audiodg.exe[1]
The file name AcroRD32.exe, a legitimate process name for Adobe's Acrobat Reader, was used by APT1 as a name for malware.[2][3]
APT29 renamed a version of AdFind to sqlceip.exe or csrss.exe in an attempt to appear as the SQL Server Telemetry Client or Client Service Runtime Process, respectively.[4][5]
APT32 has renamed a NetCat binary to kb-10233.exe to masquerade as a Windows update. APT32 has also renamed a Cobalt Strike beacon payload to install_flashplayers.exe. [6][7]
APT39 has used malware disguised as Mozilla Firefox and a tool named mfevtpse.exe to proxy C2 communications, closely mimicking a legitimate McAfee file mfevtps.exe.[8][9]
APT41 attempted to masquerade their files as popular anti-virus software.[10]
BackConfig has hidden malicious payloads in %USERPROFILE%\Adobe\Driver\dwg\ and mimicked the legitimate DHCP service binary.[11]
BADNEWS attempts to hide its payloads using legitimate filenames.[12]
The Bazar loader has named malicious shortcuts adobe.[13][14]
BLINDINGCAN has attempted to hide its payload by using legitimate file names such as "iconcache.db".[15]
Blue Mockingbird has masqueraded their XMRIG payload name by naming it wercplsupporte.dll after the legitimate wercplsupport.dll file.[16]
BRONZE BUTLER has given malware the same name as an existing file on the file share server to cause users to unwittingly launch and install the malware on additional systems.[17]
Bundlore has disguised a malicious .app file as a Flash Player update.[18]
Calisto's installation file is an unsigned DMG image under the guise of Intego’s security solution for mac.[19]
Carbanak has named malware "svchost.exe," which is the name of the Windows shared service host program.[20]
Carberp has masqueraded as Windows system file names, as well as "chkntfs.exe" and "syscron.exe".[21][22]
ChChes copies itself to an .exe file with a filename that is likely intended to imitate Norton Antivirus but has several letters reversed (e.g. notron.exe).[23]
Chimera has renamed malware to GoogleUpdate.exe and WinRAR to jucheck.exe, RecordedTV.ms, teredo.tmp, update.exe, and msadcs1.exe.[24]
DarkComet has dropped itself onto victim machines with file names such as WinDefender.Exe and winupdate.exe in an apparent attempt to masquerade as a legitimate file.[25]
Darkhotel has used malware that is disguised as a Secure Shell (SSH) tool.[26]
Daserf uses file and folder names related to legitimate programs in order to blend in, such as HP, Intel, Adobe, and perflogs.[27]
Doki has disguised a file as a Linux kernel module.[28]
One of Dtrack can hide in replicas of legitimate programs like OllyDbg, 7-Zip, and FileZilla.[29]
If installing itself as a service fails, Elise instead writes itself as a file named svchost.exe saved in %APPDATA%\Microsoft\Network.[30]
FatDuke has attempted to mimic a compromised user's traffic by using the same user agent as the installed browser.[31]
Felismus has masqueraded as legitimate Adobe Content Management System files.[32]
FinFisher renames one of its .dll files to uxtheme.dll in an apparent attempt to masquerade as a legitimate file.[33][34]
Fox Kitten has named binaries and configuration files svhost and dllhost respectively to appear legitimate.[35]
Fysbis has masqueraded as trusted software rsyncd and dbus-inotifier.[36]
GoldenSpy's setup file installs initial executables under the folder %WinDir%\System32\PluginManager.[37] 
GoldMax appeared as a scheduled task impersonating systems management software within the corresponding ProgramData subfolder.[38]
Goopy has impersonated the legitimate goopdate.dll, which was dropped on the target system with a legitimate GoogleUpdate.exe.[6]
Grandoreiro has named malicious browser extensions and update files to appear legitimate.[39][40]
Hildegard has disguised itself as a known Linux process.[41]
HTTPBrowser's installer contains a malicious file named navlu.dll to decrypt and run the RAT. navlu.dll is also the name of a legitimate Symantec DLL.[42]
Indrik Spider used fake updates for FlashPlayer plugin and Google Chrome as initial infection vectors.[43]
InnaputRAT variants have attempted to appear legitimate by using the file names SafeApp.exe and NeutralApp.exe.[44]
InvisiMole has disguised its droppers as legitimate software or documents, matching their original names and locations, and saved its files as mpr.dll in the Windows folder.[45][46]
Ixeshe has used registry values and file names associated with Adobe software, such as AcroRd32.exe.[47]
KGH_SPY has masqueraded as a legitimate Windows tool.[48]
KONNI creates a shortcut called "Anti virus service.lnk" in an apparent attempt to masquerade as a legitimate file.[49]
Lazarus Group has renamed the TAINTEDSCRIBE main executable to disguise itself as Microsoft's narrator.[50]
LightNeuron has used filenames associated with Exchange and Outlook for binary and configuration files, such as winmail.dat.[51]
LookBack has a C2 proxy tool that masquerades as GUP.exe, which is software used by Notepad++.[52]
Machete renamed payloads to masquerade as legitimate Google Chrome, Java, Dropbox, Adobe Reader and Python executables.[53][54]
Machete's Machete MSI installer has masqueraded as a legitimate Adobe Acrobat Reader installer.[55]
MCMD has been named Readme.txt to appear legitimate.[56]
MechaFlounder has been downloaded as a file named lsass.exe, which matches the legitimate Windows file.[57]
menuPass has been seen changing malicious files to appear legitimate.[58]
Metamorfo has disguised an MSI file as the Adobe Acrobat Reader Installer.[59]
Mis-Type saves itself as a file named msdtc.exe, which is also the name of the legitimate Microsoft Distributed Transaction Coordinator service binary.[60][61]
Misdat saves itself as a file named msdtc.exe, which is also the name of the legitimate Microsoft Distributed Transaction Coordinator service binary.[60][61]
MuddyWater has disguised malicious executables and used filenames and Registry key names associated with Windows Defender.[62][63][64]
Mustang Panda has used 'adobeupdate.dat' as a PlugX loader, and a file named 'OneDrive.exe' to load a Cobalt Strike payload.[65]
NETWIRE has masqueraded as legitimate software including TeamViewer and macOS Finder.[66]
NOKKI is written to %LOCALAPPDATA%\MicroSoft Updatea\svServiceUpdate.exe prior being executed in a new process in an apparent attempt to masquerade as a legitimate folder and file.[67]
OLDBAIT installs itself in %ALLUSERPROFILE%\Application Data\Microsoft\MediaPlayer\updatewindws.exe; the directory name is missing a space and the file name is missing the letter "o."[68]
OSX/Shlayer can masquerade as a Flash Player update.[69][70]
OwaAuth uses the filename owaauth.dll, which is a legitimate file that normally resides in %ProgramFiles%\Microsoft\Exchange Server\ClientAccess\Owa\Auth\; the malicious file by the same name is saved in %ProgramFiles%\Microsoft\Exchange Server\ClientAccess\Owa\bin\.[71]
Patchwork installed its payload in the startup programs folder as "Baidu Software Update." The group also adds its second stage payload to the startup programs as "Net Monitor."[72] They have also dropped QuasarRAT binaries as files named microsoft_network.exe and crome.exe.[73]
Penquin has mimicked the Cron binary to hide itself on compromised systems.[74]
PipeMon modules are stored on disk with seemingly benign names including use of a file extension associated with a popular word processor.[75]
Pony has used the Adobe Reader icon for the downloaded file to look more trustworthy.[76] 
Poseidon Group tools attempt to spoof anti-virus processes as a means of self-defense.[77]
PROMETHIUM has disguised malicious installer files by bundling them with legitimate software installers.[78][79]
PUNCHBUGGY mimics filenames from %SYSTEM%\System32 to hide DLLs in %WINDIR% and/or %TEMP%.[80][81]
Pysa has executed a malicious executable by naming it svchost.exe.[82]
QUADAGENT used the PowerShell filenames Office365DCOMCheck.ps1 and SystemDiskClean.ps1.[83]
Raindrop was installed under names that resembled legitimate Windows file and directory names.[84][85]
Ramsay has masqueraded as a 7zip installer.[86][87] 
RDAT has masqueraded as VMware.exe.[88] 
The Remsec loader implements itself with the name Security Support Provider, a legitimate Windows function. Various Remsec .exe files mimic legitimate file names used by Microsoft, Symantec, Kaspersky, Hewlett-Packard, and VMWare. Remsec also disguised malicious modules using similar filenames as custom network encryption software on victims.[89][90]
REvil can mimic the names of known executables.[91]
Rocke has used shell scripts which download mining executables and saves them with the filename "java".[92]
Ryuk has constructed legitimate appearing installation folder paths by calling GetWindowsDirectoryW and then inserting a null byte at the fourth character of the path. For Windows Vista or higher, the path would appear as C:\Users\Public.[93]
S-Type may save itself as a file named msdtc.exe, which is also the name of the legitimate Microsoft Distributed Transaction Coordinator service binary.[60][61]
Sandworm Team has avoided detection by naming a malicious binary explorer.exe.[94][95]
ShimRatReporter spoofed itself as AlphaZawgyl_font.exe, a specialized Unicode font.[96]
Sibot has downloaded a DLL to the C:\windows\system32\drivers\ folder and renamed it with a .sys extension.[38]
Sidewinder has named malicious files rekeywiz.exe to match the name of a legitimate Windows executable.[97]
Silence has named its backdoor "WINWORD.exe".[98]
Skidmap has created a fake rm binary to replace the legitimate Linux binary.[99]
SLOTHFULMEDIA has mimicked the names of known executables, such as mediaplayer.exe.[100]
Sowbug named its tools to masquerade as Windows or Adobe Reader software, such as by using the file name adobecms.exe and the directory CSIDL_APPDATA\microsoft\security.[101]
To establish persistence, SslMM identifies the Start Menu Startup directory and drops a link to its own executable disguised as an "Office Start," "Yahoo Talk," "MSN Gaming Z0ne," or "MSN Talk" shortcut.[102]
Starloader has masqueraded as legitimate software update packages such as Adobe Acrobat Reader and Intel.[101]
StrongPity has been bundled with legitimate software installation files for disguise.[78]
SUNBURST created VBScripts that were named after existing services or folders to blend into legitimate activities.[85] 
SUNSPOT was identified on disk with a filename of taskhostsvc.exe and it created an encrypted log file at C:\Windows\Temp\vmware-vmdmp.log.[103] 
SUPERNOVA has masqueraded as a legitimate SolarWinds DLL.[104][105]
The TAINTEDSCRIBE main executable has disguised itself as Microsoft’s Narrator.[50]
TEARDROP files had names that resembled legitimate Window file and directory names.[106][85]
TEMP.Veles has renamed files to look like legitimate files, such as Windows update files or Schneider Electric application files.[107]
ThiefQuest prepends a copy of itself to the beginning of an executable file while maintaining the name of the executable.[108][109]
Tropic Trooper has hidden payloads in Flash directories and fake installer files.[110]
Ursnif has used strings from legitimate system files and existing folders for its file, folder, and Registry entry names.[111]
USBStealer mimics a legitimate Russian program called USB Disk Security.[112]
Whitefly has named the malicious DLL the same name as DLLs belonging to legitimate software from various security vendors.[113]
A Winnti for Windows implant file was named ASPNET_FILTER.DLL, mimicking the legitimate ASP.NET ISAPI filter DLL with the same name.[114]
ZLib mimics the resource version information of legitimate Realtek Semiconductor, Nvidia, or Synaptics modules.[60]
/techniques/T1036/005===========================
Keydnap puts a space after a false .jpg extension so that execution actually goes through the Terminal.app program.[2]
/techniques/T1036/006===========================
Chimera's malware has altered the NTLM authentication program on domain controllers to allow Chimera to login without a valid credential.[2] 
Skeleton Key is used to patch an enterprise domain controller authentication process with a backdoor password. It allows adversaries to bypass the standard authentication system to use a defined password for all accounts authenticating to that domain controller.[1]
/techniques/T1556/001===========================
Remsec harvests plain-text credentials as a password filter registered on domain controllers.[2]
Strider has registered its persistence module on domain controllers as a Windows LSA (Local System Authority) password filter to acquire credentials any time a domain, local user, or administrator logs in or changes a password.[2]
