ADVSTORESHELL is capable of setting and deleting Registry values.[6]
Agent Tesla can achieve persistence by modifying Registry key entries.[7] 
APT19 uses a Port 22 malware variant to modify several Registry keys.[8]
APT32's backdoor has modified the Windows Registry to store the backdoor's configuration. [9] 
APT38 uses a tool called CLEANTOAD that has the capability to modify Registry keys.[10]
APT41 used a malware variant called GOODLUCK to modify the registry in order to steal credentials.[11]
Attor's dispatcher can modify the Run registry key.[12]
BACKSPACE is capable of deleting Registry keys, sub-keys, and values on a victim system.[13]
BADCALL modifies the firewall Registry key SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Services\SharedAccess\Parameters\FirewallPolicy\StandardProfileGloballyOpenPorts\List.[14]
Bankshot writes data into the Registry key HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Pniumj.[15]
BitPaymer can set values in the Registry to help in execution.[16] 
Blue Mockingbird has used Windows Registry modifications to specify a DLL payload.[17] 
Cardinal RAT sets HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows NT\CurrentVersion\Windows\Load to point to its executable.[18]
Catchamas creates three Registry keys to establish persistence by adding a Windows Service.[19]
Caterpillar WebShell has a command to modify a Registry key.[20]
CHOPSTICK may store RC4 encrypted configuration information in the Windows Registry.[21]
Cobalt Strike can modify Registry values within HKEY_CURRENT_USER\Software\Microsoft\Office\\Excel\Security\AccessVBOM\ to enable the execution of additional code.[22]
ComRAT has encrypted and stored its orchestrator code in the Registry as well as a PowerShell script into the WsqmCons Registry key.[23][24] 
CrackMapExec can create a registry key using wdigest.[25]
CSPY Downloader can write to the Registry under the %windir% variable to execute tasks.[26]
DarkComet adds a Registry value for its installation routine to the Registry Key HKEY_CURRENT_USER\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\System Enable LUA="0" and HKEY_CURRENT_USER\Software\DC3_FEXEC.[27][28]
Dragonfly 2.0 modified the Registry to perform multiple techniques through the use of Reg.[29]
EVILNUM can make modifications to the Regsitry for persistence.[30]
Exaramel for Windows adds the configuration to the Registry in XML format.[31]
Explosive has a function to write itself to Registry values.[32] 
FELIXROOT deletes the Registry key HKCU\Software\Classes\Applications\rundll32.exe\shell\open.[33]
FIN8 has deleted Registry keys during post compromise cleanup activities.[34]
Gamaredon Group has removed security settings for VBA macro execution by changing registry values HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Office\<version>\<product>\Security\VBAWarnings and HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Office\<version>\<product>\Security\AccessVBOM.[35]
gh0st RAT has altered the InstallTime subkey.[36]
Gorgon Group malware can deactivate security mechanisms in Microsoft Office by editing several keys and values under HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Office\.[37]
Grandoreiro can store its configuration in the Registry at HKCU\Software\ under frequently changing names including %USERNAME% and ToolTech-RM.[38]
GreyEnergy modifies conditions in the Registry and adds keys.[39]
Honeybee uses a batch file that modifies Registry keys to launch a DLL into the svchost.exe process.[40]
HOPLIGHT has modified Managed Object Format (MOF) files within the Registry to run specific commands and create persistence on the system.[41] 
Hydraq creates a Registry subkey to register its created service, and can also uninstall itself later by deleting this value. Hydraq's backdoor also enables remote attackers to modify and delete subkeys.[42][43]
HyperStack can add the name of its communication pipe to HKLM\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Services\lanmanserver\parameters\NullSessionPipes.[44]
InvisiMole has a command to create, set, copy, or delete a specified Registry key or value.[45][46]
KEYMARBLE has a command to create Registry entries for storing data under HKEY_CURRENT_USER\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\WABE\DataPath.[47]
Kimsuky has modified Registry settings for default file associations to enable the opening of malicious documents.[48][49]
KONNI has modified registry keys of ComSysApp service and Svchost on the machine to gain persistence.[50]
Lazarus Group has modified registry keys using the reg windows utility for its custom backdoor implants.[51]
LoJax has modified the Registry key ‘HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Control\Session Manager\BootExecute’ from ‘autocheck autochk ’ to ‘autocheck autoche ’.[52]
MegaCortex has added entries to the Registry for ransom contact information.[53]
Metamorfo has written process names to the Registry, disabled IE browser features, deleted Registry keys, and changed the ExtendedUIHoverTime key.[54][55][56]
Mosquito stores configuration values under the Registry key HKCU\Software\Microsoft[dllname] and modifies Registry keys under HKCR\CLSID...\InprocServer32with a path to the launcher.[57]
Naid creates Registry entries that store information about a created service and point to a malicious DLL dropped to disk.[58]
NanoCore has the capability to edit the Registry.[59][60]
Nerex creates a Registry subkey that registers a new service.[61]
Netwalker can add the following registry entry: HKEY_CURRENT_USER\SOFTWARE{{8 random characters}}.[62]
NETWIRE stores its configuration file within the Registry.[63]
njRAT can create, delete, or modify a specified Registry key or value.[64][65]
Operation Wocao has enabled Wdigest by changing the registry value from 0 to 1.[66]
A Patchwork payload deletes Resiliency Registry keys created by Microsoft Office applications in an apparent effort to trick users into thinking there were no issues during application runs.[67]
PHOREAL is capable of manipulating the Registry.[68]
Pillowmint has stored its malicious payload in the registry key HKLM\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\DRM.[69]
PipeMon has stored its encrypted payload in the Registry.[70]
PLAINTEE uses reg add to add a Registry Run key for persistence.[71]
PlugX has a module to create, delete, or modify Registry keys.[72]
PoetRAT has made registry modifications to alter its behavior upon execution.[73]
PoisonIvy creates a Registry subkey that registers a new system device.[74]
PolyglotDuke can write encrypted JSON configuration files to the Registry.[75]
PowerShower has added a registry key so future powershell.exe instances are spawned off-screen by default, and has removed all registry entries that are left behind during the dropper process.[76]
Pysa has modified the registry key "SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\System" and added the ransom note.[77] 
QUADAGENT modifies an HKCU Registry key to store a session identifier unique to the compromised system as well as a pre-shared key used for encrypting and decrypting C2 communications.[78]
QuasarRAT has a command to edit the Registry on the victim’s machine.[79]
Reg may be used to interact with and modify the Windows Registry of a local or remote system at the command-line interface.[1]
RegDuke can store its encryption key in the Registry.[75]
Regin appears to have functionality to modify remote Registry information.[80]
Remcos has full control of the Registry, including the ability to modify it.[81]
REvil can save encryption parameters and system information to the Registry.[82][83][84][85][86]
Rover has functionality to remove Registry Run key persistence as a cleanup procedure.[87]
RTM can delete all Registry entries created during its execution.[88]
ShadowPad maintains a configuration block and virtual file system in the Registry.[89]
Once Shamoon has access to a network share, it enables the RemoteRegistry service on the target system. It will then connect to the system with RegConnectRegistryW and modify the Registry to disable UAC remote restrictions by setting SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\System\LocalAccountTokenFilterPolicy to 1.[90][91][92]
ShimRat has registered two registry keys for shim databases.[93]
Sibot has installed a second-stage script in the HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\sibot registry key.[94]
Silence can create, delete, or modify a specified Registry key or value.[95]
SLOTHFULMEDIA can add, modify, and/or delete registry keys. It has changed the proxy configuration of a victim system by modifying the HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Internet Settings\ZoneMap registry.[96]
SOUNDBITE is capable of modifying the Registry.[68]
StreamEx has the ability to modify the Registry.[97]
SUNBURST had commands that allow an attacker to write or delete registry keys, and was observed stopping services by setting their HKLM\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\services\[service_name]\Start registry entries to value 4.[98][99] It also deleted previously-created Image File Execution Options (IFEO) Debugger registry values and registry keys related to HTTP proxy to clean up traces of its activity.[100]
SynAck can manipulate Registry keys.[101]
TajMahal can set the KeepPrintedJobs attribute for configured printers in SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows NT\CurrentVersion\Print\Printers to enable document stealing.[102]
TEARDROP modified the Registry to create a Windows service for itself on a compromised host.[103]
A Threat Group-3390 tool can create a new Registry key under HKEY_CURRENT_USER\Software\Classes\.[104]
TrickBot can modify registry entries.[105]
Turla has used the Registry to store encrypted payloads.[106][107]
TYPEFRAME can install encrypted configuration data under the Registry key HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\ShellCompatibility\Applications\laxhost.dll and HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\PrintConfigs.[108]
Ursnif has used Registry modifications as part of its installation routine.[109][110]
Valak has the ability to modify the Registry key HKCU\Software\ApplicationContainer\Appsw64 to store information regarding the C2 server and downloads.[111][112][113]
Volgmer stores the encoded configuration file in the Registry key HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Control\WMI\Security.[114][115]
Wizard Spider has modified the Registry key HKLM\System\CurrentControlSet\Control\SecurityProviders\WDigest by setting the UseLogonCredential registry value to 1 in order to force credentials to be stored in clear text in memory.[116]
Zeus Panda modifies several Registry keys under HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Internet Explorer\ PhishingFilter\ to disable phishing filters.[117]
zwShell can modify the Registry.[118]

APT32 includes garbage code to mislead anti-malware software and researchers.[1][4]

Comnie appends a total of 64MB of garbage data to a file to deter any security products in place that may be scanning files on disk.[7]
CORESHELL contains unused machine instructions in a likely attempt to hinder analysis.[8]
A variant of Emissary appends junk data to the end of its DLL file to create a large file that may exceed the maximum size that anti-virus programs can scan.[9]
FatDuke has been packed with junk code and strings.[10]
FinFisher contains junk code in its functions in an effort to confuse disassembly programs.[11][12]
Gamaredon Group has obfuscated .NET executables by inserting junk code.[13] 
Goopy has had null characters padded in its malicious DLL payload.[14]
Grandoreiro has added BMP images to the resources section of its Portable Executable (PE) file increasing each binary to at least 300MB in size.[15]
Higaisa performed padding with null bytes before calculating its hash.[16]
Javali can use large obfuscated libraries to hinder detection and analysis.[17]
Before writing to disk, Kwampirs inserts a randomly generated string into the middle of the decrypted payload in an attempt to evade hash-based detections.[18]
Leviathan has inserted garbage characters into code, presumably to avoid anti-virus detection.[19]
Maze has inserted large blocks of junk code, including some components to decrypt strings and other important information for later in the encryption process.[20]
Moafee has been known to employ binary padding.[21]
Mustang Panda has used junk code within their DLL files to hinder analysis.[22]

TAINTEDSCRIBE can execute FileRecvWriteRand to append random bytes to the end of a file received from C2.[27]

yty contains junk code in its binary, likely to confuse malware analysts.[29]
ZeroT has obfuscated DLLs and functions using dummy API calls inserted between real instructions.[30]

/techniques/T1027/004===========================
APT3 has been known to remove indicators of compromise from tools.[1]
Cobalt Strike includes a capability to modify the "beacon" payload to eliminate known signatures or unpacking methods.[2]
Analysis of Daserf has shown that it regularly undergoes technical improvements to evade anti-virus detection.[3]
Deep Panda has updated and modified its malware, resulting in different hash values that evade detection.[4]
GALLIUM ensured each payload had a unique hash, including by using different types of packers.[5]
The author of GravityRAT submitted samples to VirusTotal for testing, showing that the author modified the code to try to hide the DDE object in a different part of the document.[6]
InvisiMole has undergone regular technical improvements in an attempt to evade detection.[7]
OilRig has tested malware samples to determine AV detection and subsequently modified the samples to ensure AV evasion.[8][9]

Patchwork apparently altered NDiskMonitor samples by adding four bytes of random letters in a likely attempt to change the file hashes.[11]
Penquin can remove strings from binaries.[12]
PowerSploit's Find-AVSignature AntivirusBypass module can be used to locate single byte anti-virus signatures.[13][14]
SUNBURST source code used generic variable names and pre-obfuscated strings, and was likely sanitized of developer comments before being added to SUNSPOT.[15] 
TEMP.Veles has modified files based on the open-source project cryptcat in an apparent attempt to decrease AV detection rates.[16]
Based on comparison of Gazer versions, Turla made an effort to obfuscate strings in the malware that could be used as IoCs, including the mutex name and named pipe.[17]

/techniques/T1207===========================
APT28 has used a UEFI (Unified Extensible Firmware Interface) rootkit known as LoJax.[5][6]
APT41 deployed rootkits on Linux systems.[7][8]
Carberp has used user mode rootkit techniques to remain hidden on the system.[9]
Caterpillar WebShell has a module to use a rootkit on a system.[10] 
Drovorub has used a kernel module rootkit to hide processes, files, executables, and network artifacts from user space view.[11]
Ebury has used user mode rootkit techniques to remain hidden on the system.[12]
Hacking Team UEFI Rootkit is a UEFI BIOS rootkit developed by the company Hacking Team to persist remote access software on some targeted systems.[13]
HiddenWasp uses a rootkit to hook and implement functions on the system.[14]
HIDEDRV is a rootkit that hides certain operating system artifacts.[15]
Hikit is a Rootkit that has been used by Axiom.[16] [17] 
Hildegard has modified /etc/ld.so.preload to overwrite readdir() and readdir64().[18]
HTRAN can install a rootkit to hide network connections from the host OS.[19]
LoJax is a UEFI BIOS rootkit deployed to persist remote access software on some targeted systems.[6]
PoisonIvy starts a rootkit from a malicious file dropped to disk.[20]
Ramsay has included a rootkit to evade defenses.[21] 
Rocke has modified /etc/ld.so.preload to hook libc functions in order to hide the installed dropper and mining software in process lists.[22]
Skidmap is a kernel-mode rootkit that has the ability to hook system calls to hide specific files and fake network and CPU-related statistics to make the CPU load of the infected machine always appear low.[23]
Umbreon hides from defenders by hooking libc function calls, hiding artifacts that would reveal its presence, such as the user account it creates to provide access and undermining strace, a tool often used to identify malware.[24]
Uroburos is a rootkit used by Turla.[25]
Winnti for Linux has used a modified copy of the open-source userland rootkit Azazel, named libxselinux.so, to hide the malware's operations and network activity.[26]
Winnti Group used a rootkit to modify typical server functionality.[27]
Zeroaccess is a kernel-mode rootkit.[28]
/techniques/T1014===========================
ADVSTORESHELL has used rundll32.exe in a Registry value to establish persistence.[3]
APT19 configured its payload to inject into the rundll32.exe.[4]
APT28 executed CHOPSTICK by using rundll32 commands such as rundll32.exe "C:\Windows\twain_64.dll". APT28 also executed a .dll for a first stage dropper using rundll32.exe. An APT28 loader Trojan saved a batch script that uses rundll32 to execute a DLL payload.[5][3][6][7][8]
APT29 has used Rundll32.exe to execute payloads.[9][10][11]
APT3 has a tool that can run DLLs.[12]
APT32 malware has used rundll32.exe to execute an initial infection process.[13]
APT41 has used rundll32.exe to execute a loader.[14]
Attor's installer plugin can schedule rundll32.exe to load the dispatcher.[15]
Bisonal uses rundll32.exe to execute as part of the Registry Run key it adds: HKEY_CURRENT_USER \Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Run\"vert" = "rundll32.exe c:\windows\temp\pvcu.dll , Qszdez".[16]
BLINDINGCAN has used Rundll32 to load a malicious DLL.[17]
Blue Mockingbird has executed custom-compiled XMRIG miner DLLs using rundll32.exe.[18]
Briba uses rundll32 within Registry Run Keys / Startup Folder entries to execute malicious DLLs.[19]
Carbanak installs VNC server software that executes through rundll32.[20]
Comnie uses Rundll32 to load a malicious DLL.[21]
CopyKittens uses rundll32 to load various tools on victims, including a lateral movement tool named Vminst, Cobalt Strike, and shellcode.[22]
CORESHELL is installed via execution of rundll32 with an export named "init" or "InitW."[23]
The CozyCar dropper copies the system file rundll32.exe to the install location for the malware, then uses the copy of rundll32.exe to load and execute the main CozyCar component.[24]
DDKONG uses Rundll32 to ensure only a single instance of itself is running at once.[25]
Egregor has used rundll32 during execution.[26]
After copying itself to a DLL file, a variant of Elise calls the DLL file using rundll32.exe.[27]
Variants of Emissary have used rundll32.exe in Registry values added to establish persistence.[28]
EVILNUM can execute commands and scripts through rundll32.[29] 
FatDuke can execute via rundll32.[30]
FELIXROOT uses Rundll32 for executing the dropper program.[31][32]
Rundll32.exe is used as a way of executing Flame at the command-line.[33]
Gamaredon Group malware has used rundll32 to launch additional malicious components.[34]
A gh0st RAT variant has used rundll32 for execution.[35]
GreyEnergy uses PsExec locally in order to execute rundll32.exe at the highest privileges (NTAUTHORITY\SYSTEM).[32]
HAFNIUM has used rundll32 to load malicious DLLs.[36]
InvisiMole has used rundll32.exe for execution.[37]
JHUHUGIT is executed using rundll32.exe.[38][39]
Koadic can use Rundll32 to execute additional payloads.[40]
KONNI has used Rundll32 to execute its loader for privilege escalation purposes.[41]
Kwampirs uses rundll32.exe in a Registry value added to establish persistence.[42]
Matryoshka uses rundll32.exe in a Registry Run key value for execution as part of its persistence mechanism.[43]
MegaCortex has used rundll32.exe to load a DLL for file encryption.[44]
Mosquito's launcher uses rundll32.exe in a Registry Key value to start the main backdoor capability.[45]
MuddyWater has used malware that leveraged rundll32.exe in a Registry Run key to execute a .dll.[46]
NOKKI has used rundll32 for execution.[47]
NotPetya uses rundll32.exe to install itself on remote systems when accessed via PsExec or wmic.[48]
PolyglotDuke can be executed using rundll32.exe.[30]
PowerDuke uses rundll32.exe to load.[49]
Prikormka uses rundll32.exe to load its DLL.[50]
Pteranodon executes functions using rundll32.exe.[51]
PUNCHBUGGY can load a DLL using Rundll32.[52]
Ragnar Locker has used rundll32.exe to execute components of VirtualBox.[53]
RTM runs its core DLL file using rundll32.exe.[54][55]
Sakula calls cmd.exe to run various DLL files via rundll32.[56]
Sandworm Team used a backdoor which could execute a supplied DLL using rundll32.exe.[57] 
ServHelper contains a module for downloading and executing DLLs that leverages rundll32.exe.[58]
Sibot has executed downloaded DLLs with rundll32.exe.[59]
StreamEx uses rundll32 to call an exported function.[60]
SUNBURST used Rundll32 to execute payloads.[10] 
TA505 has leveraged rundll32.exe to execute malicious DLLs.[61][58]
TA551 has used rundll32.exe to load malicious DLLs.[62]
USBferry can execute rundll32.exe in memory to avoid detection.[63] 
The Winnti for Windows installer loads a DLL using rundll32.[64]
ZxShell has used rundll32.exe to execute other DLLs and named pipes.[65]

Astaroth uses ActiveX objects for file execution and manipulation. [7]
Dark Caracal leveraged a compiled HTML file that contained a command to download and run an executable.[8]
Lazarus Group has used CHM files to move concealed payloads.[9]
OilRig has used a CHM payload to load and execute another malicious file once delivered to a victim.[10]
Silence has weaponized CHM files in their phishing campaigns.[11][12][13][14]

/techniques/T1218/009===========================
APT19 used Regsvr32 to bypass application control techniques.[5]
APT32 created a Scheduled Task/Job that used regsvr32.exe to execute a COM scriptlet that dynamically downloaded a backdoor and injected it into memory. The group has also used regsvr32 to run their backdoor.[6][7][8] 
Astaroth can be loaded through regsvr32.exe.[9]
Blue Mockingbird has executed custom-compiled XMRIG miner DLLs using regsvr32.exe.[10] 
Cobalt Group has used regsvr32.exe to execute scripts.[11][12][13]
Deep Panda has used regsvr32.exe to execute a server variant of Derusbi in victim networks.[14]
Derusbi variants have been seen that use Registry persistence to proxy execution through regsvr32.exe.[15]
Egregor has used regsvr32.exe to execute malicious DLLs.[16]
EVILNUM can run a remote scriptlet that drops a file and executes it via regsvr32.exe.[17] 
Hi-Zor executes using regsvr32.exe called from the Registry Run Keys / Startup Folder persistence mechanism.[18]
Inception has ensured persistence at system boot by setting the value regsvr32 %path%\ctfmonrn.dll /s.[19]
Koadic can use Regsvr32 to execute additional payloads.[20]
Leviathan has used regsvr32 for execution.[21]
More_eggs has used regsvr32.exe to execute the malicious DLL.[22]
Some Orz versions have an embedded DLL known as MockDll that uses Process Hollowing and regsvr32 to execute another payload.[21]
Ragnar Locker has used regsvr32.exe to execute components of VirtualBox.[23]
RogueRobin uses regsvr32.exe to run a .sct file for execution.[24]
TA551 has used regsvr32.exe to load malicious DLLs.[25]
Valak has used regsvr32.exe to launch malicious DLLs.[26][25]
WIRTE has used Regsvr32.exe to trigger the execution of a malicious script.[27]
Xbash can use regsvr32 for executing scripts.[28]

AppleJeus has been installed via MSI installer.[5]
Duqu has used msiexec to execute malicious Windows Installer packages. Additionally, a PROPERTY=VALUE pair containing a 56-bit encryption key has been used to decrypt the main payload from the installer packages.[6]
Grandoreiro can use MSI files to execute DLLs.[7]
IcedID can inject itself into a suspended msiexec.exe process to send beacons to C2 while appearing as a normal msi application. [8]
Javali has used the MSI installer to download and execute malicious payloads.[7]
LoudMiner used an MSI installer to install the virtualization software.[9] 
Machete has used msiexec to install the Machete malware.[10]
Maze has delivered components for its ransomware attacks using MSI files, some of which have been executed from the command-line using msiexec.[11]
Melcoz can use MSI files with embedded VBScript for execution.[7]
Metamorfo has used MsiExec.exe to automatically execute files.[12] 
Molerats has used msiexec.exe to execute an MSI payload.[13] 
Ragnar Locker has been delivered as an unsigned MSI package that was executed with msiexec.exe.[14]
Rancor has used msiexec to download and execute malicious installer files over HTTP.[15]
RemoteUtilities can use Msiexec to install a service.[16]
TA505 has used msiexec to download and execute malicious Windows Installer files.[17][18][19]
ZIRCONIUM has used the msiexec.exe command-line utility to download and execute malicious MSI files.[20]

/techniques/T1553/001===========================
Anchor has been signed with valid certificates to evade detection by security tools.[4]
AppleJeus has used a valid digital signature from Sectigo to appear legitimate.[5] 
APT29 was able to get SUNBURST signed by SolarWinds code signing certificates by injecting the malware into the SolarWinds Orion software lifecycle.[6]
APT41 leveraged code-signing certificates to sign malware when targeting both gaming and non-gaming organizations.[7]
BackConfig has been signed with self signed digital certificates mimicking a legitimate software company.[8]
Bazar has been signed with fake certificates including those appearing to be from VB CORPORATE PTY. LTD.[9]
BLINDINGCAN has been signed with code-signing certificates such as CodeRipper.[10]
BOOSTWRITE has been signed by a valid CA.[11]
ChChes samples were digitally signed with a certificate originally used by Hacking Team that was later leaked and subsequently revoked.[12][13][14]
Cobalt Strike can use self signed Java applets to execute signed applet attacks.[15]
CopyKittens digitally signed an executable with a stolen certificate from legitimate company AI Squared.[16]
CSPY Downloader has come signed with revoked certificates.[17]
Darkhotel has used code-signing certificates on its malware that are either forged due to weak keys or stolen. Darkhotel has also stolen certificates and signed backdoors and downloaders with them.[18][19]
Some Daserf samples were signed with a stolen digital certificate.[20]
Ebury has installed a self-signed RPM package mimicking the original system package on RPM based systems.[21]
Turla has used valid digital certificates from Sysprint AG to sign its Epic dropper.[22]
FIN6 has used Comodo code-signing certificates.[23] 
FIN7 has signed Carbanak payloads with legally purchased code signing certificates. FIN7 has also digitally signed their phishing documents, backdoors and other staging tools to bypass security controls.[24][25]
GALLIUM has used stolen certificates to sign its tools including those from Whizzimo LLC.[26]
Gazer versions are signed with various valid certificates; one was likely faked and issued by Comodo for "Solid Loop Ltd," and another was issued for "Ultimate Computer Support Ltd."[27][28]
GreyEnergy digitally signs the malware with a code-signing certificate.[29]
Helminth samples have been signed with legitimate, compromised code signing certificates owned by software company AI Squared.[30]
Honeybee uses a dropper called MaoCheng that harvests a stolen digital signature from Adobe Systems.[31]
Janicab used a valid AppleDeveloperID to sign the code to get past security restrictions.[32]
Kimsuky has signed files with the name EGIS CO,. Ltd..[33]
Leviathan has used stolen code signing certificates to sign malware.[34][35]
LockerGoga has been signed with stolen certificates in order to make it look more legitimate.[36]
Metamorfo has digitally signed executables using AVAST Software certificates.[37] 
Molerats has used forged Microsoft code-signing certificates on malware.[38]
More_eggs has used a signed binary shellcode loader and a signed Dynamic Link Library (DLL) to create a reverse shell.[23]
Nerex drops a signed Microsoft DLL to disk.[39]
Patchwork has signed malware with self-signed certificates from fictitious and spoofed legitimate software companies.[8]
PipeMon, its installer, and tools are signed with stolen code-signing certificates.[40]
PROMETHIUM has signed code with self-signed certificates.[41]
A QuasarRAT .dll file is digitally signed by a certificate from AirVPN.[42]
RTM samples have been signed with a code-signing certificates.[43]
Silence has used a valid certificate to sign their primary loader Silence.Downloader (aka TrueBot).[44]
StrongPity has been signed with self-signed certificates.[41]
Suckfly has used stolen certificates to sign its malware.[45]
SUNBURST was digitally signed by SolarWinds from March - May 2020.[6]
TA505 has signed payloads with code signing certificates from Thawte and Sectigo.[46][47][48]
TrickBot has come with a signed downloader component.[4]
Winnti Group used stolen certificates to sign its malware.[49]
Wizard Spider has used Digicert code-signing certificates for some of its malware.[50]
/techniques/T1553/002===========================
/techniques/T1553/003===========================
certutil can be used to install browser root certificates as a precursor to performing man-in-the-middle between connections to banking websites. Example command: certutil -addstore -f -user ROOT ProgramData\cert512121.der.[6]
Dok installs a root certificate to aid in man-in-the-middle actions.[7]
Hikit uses certmgr.exe -add GlobalSign.cer -c -s -r localMachine Root and certmgr.exe -add GlobalSign.cer -c -s -r localMachineTrustedPublisher to install a self-generated certificate to the local trust store as a root CA and Trusted Publisher.[8]
RTM can add a certificate to the Windows store.[9][10]
/techniques/T1553/004===========================
APT28 used weaponized Microsoft Word documents abusing the remote template function to retrieve a malicious macro. [8]
DarkHydrus used an open-source tool, Phishery, to inject malicious remote template URLs into Microsoft Word documents and then sent them to victims to enable Forced Authentication.[9]
Dragonfly 2.0 has injected SMB URLs into malicious Word spearphishing attachments to initiate Forced Authentication.[10][11]
Frankenstein has used trojanized documents that retrieve remote templates from an adversary-controlled website.[12]
Gamaredon Group has used DOCX files to download malicious DOT document templates. Gamaredon Group can also inject malicious macros or remote templates into documents already present on compromised systems.[13][14]
Inception has used decoy documents to load malicious remote payloads via HTTP.[15]
Tropic Trooper delivered malicious documents with the XLSX extension, typically used by OpenXML documents, but the file itself was actually an OLE (XLS) document.[16]
/techniques/T1221===========================
Empire can use built-in modules to abuse trusted utilities like MSBuild.exe.[4]
Frankenstein has used MSbuild to execute an actor-created file.[5]
A version of PlugX loads as shellcode within a .NET Framework project using msbuild.exe, presumably to bypass application control techniques.[6]

/techniques/T1535===========================
The APT1 group is known to have used pass the hash.[2]
APT28 has used pass the hash for lateral movement.[3]
APT32 has used pass the hash for lateral movement.[4]
Chimera has dumped password hashes for use in pass the hash authentication attacks.[5]
Cobalt Strike can perform pass the hash.[6]
CrackMapExec can pass the hash to authenticate via SMB.[7]
Empire can perform pass the hash attacks.[8]
GALLIUM used dumped hashes to authenticate to other machines via pass the hash.[9]
HOPLIGHT has been observed loading several APIs associated with Pass the Hash.[10] 
Kimsuky has used pass the hash for authentication to remote access software used in C2.[11]
Mimikatz's SEKURLSA::Pth module can impersonate a user, with only a password hash, to execute arbitrary commands.[12][13]
Night Dragon used pass-the-hash tools to gain usernames and passwords.[14]
Pass-The-Hash Toolkit can perform pass the hash.[2]
PoshC2 has a number of modules that leverage pass the hash for lateral movement.[15]
/techniques/T1550/002===========================
APT29 used Kerberos ticket attacks for lateral movement.[5]
APT32 successfully gained remote access by using pass the ticket.[6]
BRONZE BUTLER has created forged Kerberos Ticket Granting Ticket (TGT) and Ticket Granting Service (TGS) tickets to maintain administrative access.[7]
Mimikatz’s LSADUMP::DCSync and KERBEROS::PTT modules implement the three steps required to extract the krbtgt account hash and create/use Kerberos tickets.[8][9][10][11]
Pupy can also perform pass-the-ticket.[12]
Some SeaDuke samples have a module to use pass the ticket with Kerberos for authentication.[13]
/techniques/T1550/003===========================
APT28 has used several malicious applications that abused OAuth access tokens to gain access to target email accounts, including Gmail and Yahoo Mail.[5]
/techniques/T1550/001===========================
APT29 used a forged duo-sid cookie to bypass MFA set on an email account.[3]
/techniques/T1550/004===========================
Astaroth can check for Windows product ID's used by sandboxes and usernames and disk serial numbers associated with analyst environments.[3]
Attor can detect whether it is executed in some virtualized or emulated environment by searching for specific artifacts, such as communication with I/O ports and using VM-specific instructions.[4]
BadPatch attempts to detect if it is being run in a Virtual Machine (VM) using a WMI query for disk drive name, BIOS, and motherboard information. [5]
CSPY Downloader can search loaded modules, PEB structure, file paths, Registry keys, and memory to determine if it is being debugged or running in a virtual environment.[6]
Darkhotel malware has used a series of checks to determine if it's being analyzed; checks include the length of executable names, if a filename ends with .Md5.exe, and if the program is executed from the root of the C:\ drive, as well as checks for sandbox-related libraries.[7][8]
Denis ran multiple system checks, looking for processor and register characteristics, to evade emulation and analysis.[9]
Dyre can detect sandbox analysis environments by inspecting the process list and Registry.[10][11]
EvilBunny's dropper has checked the number of processes and the length and strings of its own file name to identify if the malware is in a sandbox environment.[12] 
Evilnum has used a component called TerraLoader to check certain hardware and file information to detect sandboxed environments. [13]
FinFisher obtains the hardware device list and checks if the MD5 of the vendor ID is equal to a predefined list in order to check for sandbox/virtualized environments.[14]
Frankenstein has used WMI queries to check if various security applications were running, including VMWare and Virtualbox.[15]
GoldMax will check if it is being run in a virtualized environment by comparing the collected MAC address to c8:27:cc:c2:37:5a.[16][17]
Grandoreiro can detect VMWare via its I/O port and Virtual PC via the vpcext instruction.[18]
GravityRAT uses WMI to check the BIOS and manufacturer information for strings like "VMWare", "Virtual", and "XEN" and another WMI request to get the current temperature of the hardware to determine if it's a virtual machine environment. [19]
InvisiMole can check for artifacts of VirtualBox, Virtual PC and VMware environment, and terminate itself if they are detected.[20]
Lucifer can check for specific usernames, computer names, device drivers, DLL's, and virtual devices associated with sandboxed environments and can enter an infinite loop and stop itself if any are detected.[21]
MegaCortex has checked the number of CPUs in the system to avoid being run in a sandbox or emulator.[22] 
Okrum's loader can check the amount of physical memory and terminates itself if the host has less than 1.5 Gigabytes of physical memory in total.[23]
OopsIE performs several anti-VM and sandbox checks on the victim's machine. One technique the group has used was to perform a WMI query SELECT * FROM MSAcpi_ThermalZoneTemperature to check the temperature to see if it’s running in a virtual environment.[2]
OSX_OCEANLOTUS.D has a variant that checks a number of system parameters to see if it is being run on real hardware or in a virtual machine environment.[24]
PlugX checks if VMware tools is running in the background by searching for any process named "vmtoolsd". [25]
PoetRAT checked the size of the hard drive to determine if it was being run in a sandbox environment. In the event of sandbox detection, it would delete itself by overwriting the malware scripts with the contents of "License.txt" and exiting.[26]
Pupy has a module that checks a number of indicators on the system to determine if its running on a virtual machine.[27]
Remcos searches for Sandboxie and VMware on the system.[28]
RogueRobin uses WMI to check BIOS version for VBOX, bochs, qemu, virtualbox, and vm to check for evidence that the script might be executing within an analysis environment. [29][30]
ROKRAT checks for sandboxing libraries.[31][32]
Smoke Loader scans processes to perform anti-VM checks. [33]
SUNBURST checked the domain name of the compromised host to verify it was running in a real environment.[34]
SynAck checks its directory location in an attempt to avoid launching in a sandbox.[35][36]
ThiefQuest uses a function named is_debugging to perform anti-debugging logic. The function invokes sysctl checking the returned value of P_TRACED. ThiefQuest also calls ptrace with the PTRACE_DENY_ATTACH flag to prevent debugging.  
Trojan.Karagany can detect commonly used and generic virtualization platforms based primarily on drivers and file paths.[37]
UBoatRAT checks for virtualization software such as VMWare, VirtualBox, or QEmu on the compromised machine.[38]
yty has some basic anti-sandbox detection that tries to detect Virtual PC, Sandboxie, and VMware. [39]
/techniques/T1497/001===========================
Darkhotel has used malware that repeatedly checks the mouse cursor position to determine if a real user is on the system.[4]
FIN7 used images embedded into document lures that only activate the payload when a user double clicks to avoid sandboxes.[3]
Okrum loader only executes the payload after the left mouse button has been pressed at least three times, in order to avoid being executed within virtualized or emulated environments.[5] 
Spark has used a splash screen to check whether an user actively clicks on the screen before running malicious code.[6] 
/techniques/T1497/002===========================
AppleJeus has waited a specified time before downloading a second stage payload.[2]
Bazar can use a timer to delay execution of core functionality.[3]
BendyBear can check for analysis environments and signs of debugging using the Windows API kernel32!GetTickCountKernel32 call.[4] 
Egregor can perform a  long sleep (greater than or equal to 3 minutes) to evade detection.[5]
EvilBunny has used time measurements from 3 different APIs before and after performing sleep operations to check and abort if the malware is running in a sandbox.[6]
FatDuke can turn itself on or off at random intervals.[7]
GoldenSpy's installer has delayed installation of GoldenSpy for two hours after it reaches a victim system.[8] 
GoldMax has set an execution trigger date and time, stored as an ASCII Unix/Epoch time value.[9]
Okrum's loader can detect presence of an emulator by using two calls to GetTickCount API, and checking whether the time has been accelerated.[10]
Pony has delayed execution using a built-in function to avoid detection and analysis.[11] 
After initial installation, Raindrop runs a computation to delay execution.[12]
SUNBURST remained dormant after initial access for a period of up to two weeks.[13]
ThiefQuest invokes time call to check the system's time, executes a sleep command, invokes a second time call, and then compares the time difference between the two time calls and the amount of time the system slept to identify the sandbox.[14]
Ursnif has used a 30 minute delay after execution to evade sandbox monitoring tools.[15]

/techniques/T1600/001===========================
/techniques/T1600/002===========================
Astaroth executes embedded JScript or VBScript in an XSL stylesheet located on a remote domain. [7]
Cobalt Group used msxsl.exe to bypass AppLocker and to invoke Jscript code from an XSL file.[8]
Higaisa used an XSL file to run VBScript code.[9]
/techniques/T1220===========================
APT28 has used a brute-force/password-spray tooling that operated in two modes: in brute-force mode it typically sent over 300 authentication attempts per hour per targeted account over the course of several hours or days.[3] 
China Chopper's server component can perform brute force password guessing against authentication portals.[4]
CrackMapExec can brute force passwords for a specified user on a single target system or across an entire network.[5]
Emotet has been observed using a hard coded list of passwords to brute force user accounts. [6][7][8][9][10] 
Lucifer has attempted to brute force TCP ports 135 (RPC) and 1433 (MSSQL) with the default username or list of usernames and    passwords.[11]
P.A.S. Webshell can use predefined users and passwords to execute brute force attacks against SSH, FTP, POP3, MySQL, MSSQL, and PostgreSQL services.[12]
Pony has used a small dictionary of common passwords against a collected list of local accounts.[13] 
SpeakUp can perform brute forcing using a pre-defined list of usernames and passwords in an attempt to log in to administrative panels. [14]
Xbash can obtain a list of weak passwords from the C2 server to use for brute forcing as well as attempt to brute force services with open ports.[15][16]
/techniques/T1110/001===========================
APT3 has been known to brute force password hashes to be able to leverage plain text credentials.[2]
APT41 performed password brute-force attacks on the local admin account.[3]
Dragonfly 2.0 dropped and executed tools used for password cracking, including Hydra and CrackMapExec.[4][5][6]
FIN6 has extracted password hashes from ntds.dit to crack offline.[7]
Net Crawler uses a list of known credentials gathered through credential dumping to guess passwords to accounts as it spreads throughout a network.[8]
/techniques/T1110/002===========================
APT28 has used a brute-force/password-spray tooling that operated in two modes: in password-spraying mode it conducted approximately four authentication attempts per hour per targeted account over the course of several days or weeks.[3][4]
APT33 has used password spraying to gain access to target systems.[5][6]
Chimera has used multiple password spraying attacks against victim's remote services to obtain valid user and administrator accounts.[7]
CrackMapExec can brute force credential authentication by using a supplied list of usernames and a single password.[8]
Lazarus Group malware attempts to connect to Windows shares for lateral movement by using a generated list of usernames, which center around permutations of the username Administrator, and weak passwords.[9][10]
Leafminer used a tool called Total SMB BruteForcer to perform internal password spraying.[11]
Linux Rabbit brute forces SSH passwords in order to attempt to gain access and install its malware onto the server. [12]
MailSniper can be used for password spraying against Exchange and Office 365.[13]
Silent Librarian has used collected lists of names and e-mail accounts to use in password spraying attacks against private sector targets.[14]
/techniques/T1110/003===========================
Chimera has used credential stuffing against victim's remote services to obtain valid accounts.[2]
TrickBot uses brute-force attack against RDP with rdpscanDll module.[3][4]
/techniques/T1110/004===========================
Calisto collects Keychain storage data and copies those passwords/tokens to a file.[3][4]
iKitten collects the keychains on the system.[5]
LaZagne can obtain credentials from macOS Keychains.[6] 
Proton gathers credentials in files for keychains.[5]
/techniques/T1555/001===========================
Keydnap uses the keychaindump project to read securityd memory.[4]
/techniques/T1555/002===========================

/techniques/T1557/002===========================
APT28 deployed the open source tool Responder to conduct NetBIOS Name Service poisoning, which captured usernames and hashed passwords that allowed access to legitimate credentials.[1][2] APT28 close-access teams have used Wi-Fi pineapples to intercept Wi-Fi signals and user credentials.[3]

Impacket can be used to sniff network traffic via an interface or raw socket.[8]
Kimsuky has used the Nirsoft SniffPass network sniffer to obtain passwords sent over non-secure protocols.[9]
MESSAGETAP uses the libpcap library to listen to all traffic and parses network protocols starting with Ethernet and IP layers. It continues parsing protocol layers including SCTP, SCCP, and TCAP and finally extracts SMS message data and routing metadata.  [10]
NBTscan can dump and print whole packet content.[11][12] 
Penquin can sniff network traffic to look for packets matching specific conditions.[13][14]
PoshC2 contains a module for taking packet captures on compromised hosts.[15]
Regin appears to have functionality to sniff for credentials passed over HTTP, SMTP, and SMB.[16]

/techniques/T1003/002===========================
Chimera has gathered the SYSTEM registry and ntds.dit files from target systems.[3] Chimera specifically has used the NtdsAudit tool to dump the password hashes of domain users via cmsadcs.exe "NTDS.dit" -s "SYSTEM" -p RecordedTV_pdmp.txt --users-csv RecordedTV_users.csv and used ntdsutil to copy the Active Directory database.[4]
CrackMapExec can dump hashed passwords associated with Active Directory using Windows' Directory Replication Services API (DRSUAPI), or Volume Shadow Copy.[5]
Dragonfly 2.0 dropped and executed SecretsDump to dump password hashes. They also obtained ntds.dit from domain controllers. [6][7][8]

Fox Kitten has used Volume Shadow Copy to access credential information from NTDS.[13]
HAFNIUM has stolen copies of the Active Directory database (NTDS.DIT).[14]
SecretsDump and Mimikatz modules within Impacket can perform credential dumping to obtain account and password information from NTDS.dit.[15]
Koadic can gather hashed passwords by gathering domain controller hashes from NTDS.[16]
menuPass has used Ntdsutil to dump credentials.[17]
Mustang Panda has used vssadmin to create a volume shadow copy and retrieve the NTDS.dit file. Mustang Panda has also used reg save on the SYSTEM file Registry location to help extract the NTDS.dit file.[18]
Wizard Spider has gained access to credentials via exported copies of the ntds.dit Active Directory database.[19]

Mimikatz performs credential dumping to obtain account and password information useful in gaining access to additional systems and enterprise network resources. It contains functionality to acquire information about credentials in many ways, including from the LSA.[20][21][22][23]
MuddyWater has performed credential dumping with LaZagne.[24][25]
OilRig has used credential dumping tools such as LaZagne to steal credentials to accounts logged into the compromised system and to Outlook Web Access.[26][27][28][29]
Pupy can use Lazagne for harvesting credentials.[30]
Threat Group-3390 actors have used gsecdump to dump credentials. They have also dumped credentials from domain controllers.[31][32]

NETEAGLE allows adversaries to enumerate and modify the infected host's file system. It supports searching for directories, creating directories, listing directory contents, reading and writing to files, retrieving file attributes, and retrieving volume information.[24]
NETWIRE has the ability to search for files on the compromised host.[133]
njRAT can browse file systems using a file manager module.[134]
NotPetya searches for files ending with dozens of different file extensions prior to encryption.[135]
OceanSalt can extract drive information from the endpoint and search files on the system.[136]
Octopus collects information on the Windows directory and searches for compressed RAR files on the host.[137]
Okrum has used DriveLetterView to enumerate drive information.[138]
Operation Wocao has gathered a recursive directory listing to find files and directories of interest.[139]
Orz can gather victim drive information.[140]
OwaAuth has a command to list its directory and logical drives.[90]
P.A.S. Webshell has the ability to list files and file characteristics including extension, size, ownership, and permissions.[141]
Pasam creates a backdoor through which remote attackers can retrieve lists of files.[142]
A Patchwork payload has searched all fixed drives on the victim for files matching a specified list of extensions.[143][25]
Penquin can use the command code do_vslist to send file names, size, and status to C2.[144]
PinchDuke searches for files created within a certain timeframe and whose file extension matches a predefined list.[84]
Pisloader has commands to list drives on the victim machine and to list file information for a given directory.[145]
PLEAD has the ability to list drives and files on the compromised host.[110][146]
PlugX has a module to enumerate drives and find files recursively.[147]
PoetRAT has the ability to list files upon receiving the ls command from C2.[148]
POORAIM can conduct file browsing.[48]
PoshC2 can enumerate files on the local file system and includes a module for enumerating recently accessed files.[149]
PowerDuke has commands to get the current directory name as well as the size of a file. It also has commands to obtain information about logical drives, drive type, and free space.[150]
POWRUNER may enumerate user directories on a victim.[151]
A module in Prikormka collects information about the paths, size, and creation time of files with specific file extensions, but not the actual content of the file.[152]
Proxysvc lists files in directories.[114]
Psylo has commands to enumerate all storage devices and to find all files that start with a particular string.[129]
Pteranodon identifies files matching certain file extension and copies them to subdirectories it created.[153]
Pupy can walk through directories and recursively search for strings in files.[154]
Ramsay can collect directory and file lists.[155][156] 
RARSTONE obtains installer properties from Uninstall Registry Key entries to obtain information about installed applications and how to uninstall certain applications.[157]
RedLeaves can enumerate and search for files and directories.[158][42]
Remcos can search for files on the infected machine.[159]
Remexi searches for files on the system. [160]
RemoteUtilities can enumerate files and directories on a target machine.[161]
Remsec is capable of listing contents of folders on the victim. Remsec also searches for custom network encryption software on victims.[162][163][164]
REvil has the ability to identify specific files and directories that are not to be encrypted.[165][166][167][168][169][170]
Rising Sun can enumerate information about files from the infected system, including file size, attributes, creation time, last access time, and write time. Rising Sun can enumerate the compilation timestamp of Windows executable files.[171] 
ROKRAT has the ability to gather a list of files and directories on the infected system.[172][173]
Rover automatically searches for files on local drives based on a predefined list of file extensions.[174]
RTM can check for specific files and directories associated with virtualization and malware analysis.[175]
Ryuk has called GetLogicalDrives to emumerate all mounted drives, and GetDriveTypeW to determine the drive type.[176]
Sandworm Team has enumerated files on a compromised host.[135] 
SDBbot has the ability to get directory listings or drive information on a compromised host.[177]
Seasalt has the capability to identify the drive type on a victim.[136]
ShimRat can list directories.[178]
SHOTPUT has a command to obtain a directory listing.[179]
Sidewinder has used malware to collect information on files and directories.[180]
Skidmap has checked for the existence of specific files including /usr/sbin/setenforce and  /etc/selinux/config. It also has the ability to monitor the cryptocurrency miner file and process. [181] 
SLOTHFULMEDIA can enumerate files and directories.[182]
Smoke Loader recursively searches through directories for files.[183]
SoreFang has the ability to list directories.[184]
SOUNDBITE is capable of enumerating and manipulating files and directories.[185]
Sowbug identified and extracted all Word documents on a server by using a command containing * .doc and *.docx. The actors also searched for documents based on a specific date range and attempted to identify all installed software on a victim.[186]
SPACESHIP identifies files and directories for collection by searching for specific file extensions or file modification time.[24]
StreamEx has the ability to enumerate drive types.[187]
StrongPity can parse the hard drive on a compromised host to identify specific file extensions.[188]
SUNBURST had commands to enumerate files and directories.[189][190]
SUNSPOT enumerated the Orion software Visual Studio solution directory path.[191]
SynAck checks its directory location in an attempt to avoid launching in a sandbox.[192][193]
TAINTEDSCRIBE can use DirectoryList to enumerate files in a specified directory.[194]
TajMahal has the ability to index files from drives, user profiles, and removable drives.[195]
TINYTYPHON searches through the drive containing the OS, then all drive letters C through to Z, for documents matching certain extensions.[18]
TrickBot searches the system for all of the following file extensions: .avi, .mov, .mkv, .mpeg, .mpeg4, .mp4, .mp3, .wav, .ogg, .jpeg, .jpg, .png, .bmp, .gif, .tiff, .ico, .xlsx, and .zip. It can also obtain browsing history, cookies, and plug-in information.[196][197]
Trojan.Karagany can enumerate files and directories on a compromised host.[198]
Tropic Trooper has monitored files' modified time.[199] 
TSCookie has the ability to discover drive information on the infected host.[200]
Turla surveys a system upon check-in to discover files in specific locations on the hard disk %TEMP% directory, the current user's desktop, the Program Files directory, and Recent.[74][201] Turla RPC backdoors have also searched for files matching the lPH*.dll pattern.[202]
TYPEFRAME can search directories for files on the victim’s machine.[203]
UPPERCUT has the capability to gather the victim's current directory.[204]
USBferry can detect the victim's file or folder list.[199] 
USBStealer searches victim drives for files matching certain extensions (".skr",".pkr" or ".key") or names.[205][206]
Volgmer can list directories on a victim.[207]
WannaCry searches for variety of user files by file extension before encrypting them using RSA and AES, including Office, PDF, image, audio, video, source code, archive/compression format, and key and certificate files.[208][209]
Windigo has used a script to check for the presence of files created by OpenSSH backdoors.[210]
WindTail has the ability to enumerate the users home directory and the path to its own application bundle.[211][212]
WINERACK can enumerate files and directories.[48]
WinMM sets a WH_CBT Windows hook to search for and capture files on the victim.[213]
XAgentOSX contains the readFiles function to return a detailed listing (sometimes recursive) of a specified directory.[214] XAgentOSX contains the showBackupIosFolder function to check for IOS device backups by running ls -la ~/Library/Application\ Support/MobileSync/Backup/.[214]
yty gathers information on victim’s drives and has a plugin for document listing.[215]
Zebrocy searches for files that are 60mb and less and contain the following extensions: .doc, .docx, .xls, .xlsx, .ppt, .pptx, .exe, .zip, and .rar. Zebrocy also runs the echo %APPDATA% command to list the contents of the directory.[216][217][218] Zebrocy can obtain the current execution path as well as perform drive enumeration.[219][220] 
Zeus Panda searches for specific directories on the victim’s machine.[221]
ZLib has the ability to enumerate files and drives.[66]
zwShell can browse the file system.[222]
ZxShell has a command to open a file manager and explorer on the system.[223] 
/techniques/T1083===========================
APT32 performed network scanning on the network to search for open ports, services, OS finger-printing, and other vulnerabilities.[1]
APT39 has used CrackMapExec and a custom port scanner known as BLUETORCH for network scanning. [2][3]
APT41 used a malware variant called WIDETONE to conduct port scans on the specified subnets.[4]
BlackEnergy has conducted port scans on a host.[5]
Caterpillar WebShell has a module to use a port scanner on a system.[6] 
Chimera has used the get -b  -e  -p command for network scanning as well as a custom Python tool  packed into a Windows executable named Get.exe to scan IP ranges for HTTP.[7]
China Chopper's server component can spider authentication portals.[8]
Cobalt Group leveraged an open-source tool called SoftPerfect Network Scanner to perform network scanning.[9][10][11]
Cobalt Strike can perform port scans from an infected host.[12][13]
DarkVishnya performed port scanning to obtain the list of active services.[14]
Empire can perform port scans from an infected host.[15]
FIN6 used publicly available tools (including Microsoft's built-in SQL querying tool, osql.exe) to map the internal network and conduct reconnaissance against Active Directory, Structured Query Language (SQL) servers, and NetBIOS.[16]
Fox Kitten has used tools including NMAP to conduct broad scanning to identify open ports.[17][18]
HDoor scans to identify open ports on the victim.[19]
Hildegard has used masscan to look for kubelets in the internal Kubernetes network.[20]
InvisiMole can scan the network for open ports and vulnerable instances of RDP and SMB protocols.[21]
Koadic can scan for open TCP ports on the target network.[22]
Leafminer scanned network services to search for vulnerabilities in the victim system.[23]
Lucifer can scan for open ports including TCP ports 135 and 1433.[24]
menuPass has used tcping.exe, similar to Ping, to probe port status on systems of interest.[25]
MURKYTOP has the capability to scan for open ports on hosts in a connected network.[8]
NBTscan can be used to scan IP networks.[26][27]
OilRig has used the publicly available tool SoftPerfect Network Scanner as well as a custom tool called GOLDIRONY to conduct network scanning.[28]
Operation Wocao has scanned for open ports and used nbtscan to find NETBIOS nameservers.[29]
P.A.S. Webshell can scan networks for open ports and listening services.[30]
PoshC2 can perform port scans from an infected host.[31]
Pupy has a built-in module for port scanning.[32]
Pysa can perform network reconnaissance using the Advanced Port Scanner tool.[33]
Ramsay can scan for systems that are vulnerable to the EternalBlue exploit.[34][35] 
Remsec has a plugin that can perform ARP scanning as well as port scanning.[36]
Rocke conducted scanning for exposed TCP port 7001 as well as SSH and Redis servers.[37][38]
SpeakUp checks for availability of specific ports on servers.[39]
Suckfly the victim's internal network for hosts with ports 8080, 5900, and 40 open.[40]
Threat Group-3390 actors use the Hunter tool to conduct network service discovery for vulnerable systems.[41][42]
Tropic Trooper used pr and an openly available tool to scan for open ports on target systems.[43][44]
Xbash can perform port scanning of TCP and UDP ports.[45]
XTunnel is capable of probing the network for open ports.[46]
ZxShell can launch port scans.[4][47]

InvisiMole can gather network share information.[17]
Koadic can scan local network for open SMB.[18]

Olympic Destroyer will attempt to enumerate mapped network shares to later attempt to wipe all files on those shares.[22]

OSInfo discovers shares on the network[24]

DustySky can detect connected USB devices.[10]

Zebrocy enumerates information about connected storage devices.[33]

Ryuk has called CreateToolhelp32Snapshot to enumerate all running processes.[158]
Seasalt has a command to perform a process listing.[23]
ShadowPad has collected the PID of a malicious process.[159]
ShimRatReporter listed all running processes on the machine.[160]
SHOTPUT has a command to obtain a process listing.[161]
Sidewinder has used tools to identify running processes on the victim's machine.[162]
Skidmap has monitored critical processes to ensure resiliency.[163] 
SLOTHFULMEDIA has enumerated processes by ID, name, or privileges.[164] 
Socksbot can list all running processes.[165]
SoreFang can enumerate processes on a victim machine through use of Tasklist.[166]
Stealth Falcon malware gathers a list of running processes.[167]
StreamEx has the ability to enumerate processes.[168]
StrongPity can determine if a user is logged in by checking to see if explorer.exe is running.[169]
SUNBURST collected a list of process names that were hashed using a FNV-1a + XOR algorithm to check against similarly-hashed hardcoded blocklists.[170]
SUNSPOT monitored running processes for instances of MsBuild.exe by hashing the name of each running process and comparing it to the corresponding value 0x53D525. It also extracted command-line arguments and individual arguments from the running MsBuild.exe process to identify the directory path of the Orion software Visual Studio solution.[171]
Sykipot may gather a list of running processes by running tasklist /v.[172]
SynAck enumerates all running processes.[173][174]
SYSCON has the ability to use Tasklist to list running processes.[175]
TAINTEDSCRIBE can execute ProcessList for process discovery.[176]
TajMahal has the ability to identify running processes and associated plugins on an infected host.[177]
Tasklist can be used to discover processes running on a system.[178]
ThiefQuest obtains a list of running processes using the function kill_unwanted.[179]
TrickBot uses module networkDll for process list discovery.[180][181]
Trojan.Karagany can use Tasklist to collect a list of running tasks.[18][182]
Tropic Trooper is capable of enumerating the running processes on the system using pslist.[183][184]
TSCookie has the ability to list processes on the infected host.[185]
Turla surveys a system upon check-in to discover running processes using the tasklist /v command.[62] Turla RPC backdoors have also enumerated processes associated with specific open ports or named pipes.[144]
UBoatRAT can list running processes on the system.[186]
Ursnif has gathered information about running processes.[187][188]
USBferry can use tasklist to gather information about the process running on the infected system.[184]

Volgmer can gather a list of processes.[191]

WINERACK can enumerate processes.[138]
WinMM sets a WH_CBT Windows hook to collect information on process creation.[194]
Winnti Group looked for a specific process running on infected servers.[195]
XAgentOSX contains the getProcessList function to run ps aux to get running processes.[196]
yty gets an output of running processes using the tasklist command.[197]

Zeus Panda checks for running processes on the victim’s machine.[201]
ZxShell has a command, ps, to obtain a listing of processes on the system.[202] 
/techniques/T1057===========================
ADVSTORESHELL can enumerate registry keys.[2][3]
APT32's backdoor can query the Windows Registry to gather system information. [4]
APT39 has used various strains of malware to query the Registry.[5]
Attor has opened the registry and performed query searches.[6]
Azorult can check for installed software on the system under the Registry key Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Uninstall.[7]
BabyShark has executed the reg query command for HKEY_CURRENT_USER\Software\Microsoft\Terminal Server Client\Default.[8] 
BACKSPACE is capable of enumerating and making modifications to an infected system's Registry.[9]
Bankshot searches for certain Registry keys to be configured before executing the payload.[10]
Bazar can query Windows\CurrentVersion\Uninstall for installed applications.[11][12]
BendyBear can query the host's Registry key at HKEY_CURRENT_USER\Console\QuickEdit to retrieve data.[13]
BitPaymer can use the RegEnumKeyW to iterate through Registry keys.[14] 
Brave Prince gathers information about the Registry.[15]
Carbanak checks the Registry key HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Internet Settings for proxy configurations information.[16]
Carberp has searched the Image File Execution Options registry key for "Debugger" within every subkey.[17]
Carbon enumerates values in the Registry.[18]
Cardinal RAT contains watchdog functionality that periodically ensures HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows NT\CurrentVersion\Windows\Load is set to point to its executable.[19]
Chimera has queried Registry keys using reg query \\HKU\\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Terminal Server Client\Servers and reg query \\HKU\\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Internet Settings.[20]
CHOPSTICK provides access to the Windows Registry, which can be used to gather information.[21]
Cobalt Strike can query HKEY_CURRENT_USER\Software\Microsoft\Office\\Excel\Security\AccessVBOM\  to determine if the security setting for restricting default programmatic access is enabled.[22]
ComRAT can check the default browser by querying HKCR\http\shell\open\command.[23]
Denis queries the Registry for keys and values.[24]
Derusbi is capable of enumerating Registry keys and values.[25]
DownPaper searches and reads the value of the Windows Update Registry Run key.[26]
Dragonfly 2.0 queried the Registry to identify victim information.[27]
Dtrack can collect the RegisteredOwner, RegisteredOrganization, and InstallDate registry values.[28]
Epic uses the rem reg query command to obtain values from Registry keys.[29]
FatDuke can get user agent strings for the default browser from HKCU\Software\Classes\http\shell\open\command.[30]
FELIXROOT queries the Registry for specific keys for potential privilege escalation and proxy information. FELIXROOT has also used WMI to query the Windows Registry.[31][32]
FinFisher queries Registry values as part of its anti-sandbox checks.[33][34]
Fox Kitten has accessed Registry hives ntuser.dat and UserClass.dat.[35]
gh0st RAT has checked for the existence of a Service key to determine if it has already been installed on the system.[36]
Gold Dragon enumerates registry keys with the command regkeyenum and obtains information for the Registry key HKEY_CURRENT_USER\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Run.[15]
A variant of HOPLIGHT hooks lsass.exe, and lsass.exe then checks the Registry for the data value 'rdpproto' under the key SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Control\Lsa Name.[37]
Hydraq creates a backdoor through which remote attackers can retrieve system information, such as CPU speed, from Registry keys.[38][39]
InvisiMole can enumerate Registry values, keys, and data.[40]
JPIN can enumerate Registry keys.[41]
Lazarus Group malware IndiaIndia checks Registry keys within HKCU and HKLM to determine if certain applications are present, including SecureCRT, Terminal Services, RealVNC, TightVNC, UltraVNC, Radmin, mRemote, TeamViewer, FileZilla, pcAnyware, and Remote Desktop. Another Lazarus Group malware sample checks for the presence of the following Registry key:HKEY_CURRENT_USER\Software\Bitcoin\Bitcoin-Qt.[42][43][44]
Lucifer can check for existing stratum cryptomining information in HKLM\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\spreadCpuXmr – %stratum info%.[45]
njRAT can read specific registry values.[46]
OilRig has used reg query "HKEY_CURRENT_USER\Software\Microsoft\Terminal Server Client\Default" on a victim to query the Registry.[47]
Operation Wocao has queried the registry to detect recent PuTTY sessions.[48]
OSInfo queries the registry to look for information about Terminal Services.[49]
Pillowmint has used shellcode which reads code stored in the registry keys \REGISTRY\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\DRM using the native Windows API as well as read HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\System\CurrentControlSet\Services\Tcpip\Parameters\Interfaces as part of its C2.[50] 
PlugX can enumerate and query for information contained within the Windows Registry.[51][52]
POWERSOURCE queries Registry keys in preparation for setting Run keys to achieve persistence.[53]
PowerSploit contains a collection of Privesc-PowerUp modules that can query Registry keys for potential opportunities.[54][55]
POWRUNER may query the Registry by running reg query on a victim.[56]
Proxysvc gathers product names from the Registry key: HKLM\Software\Microsoft\Windows NT\CurrentVersion ProductName and the processor description from the Registry key HKLM\HARDWARE\DESCRIPTION\System\CentralProcessor\0 ProcessorNameString.[57]
QUADAGENT checks if a value exists within a Registry key in the HKCU hive whose name is the same as the scheduled task it has created.[58]
RATANKBA uses the command reg query "HKCU\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\InternetSettings".[59]
Reaver queries the Registry to determine the correct Startup path to use for persistence.[60]
Reg may be used to gather details from the Windows Registry of a local or remote system at the command-line interface.[61]
REvil can query the Registry to get random file extensions to append to encrypted files.[62]
ROKRAT accesses the HKLM\System\CurrentControlSet\Services\mssmbios\Data\SMBiosData Registry key to obtain the System manufacturer value to identify the machine type.[63]
Shamoon queries several Registry keys to identify hard disk partitions to overwrite.[64]
Sibot has queried the registry for proxy server information.[65]
Stealth Falcon malware attempts to determine the installed version of .NET by querying the Registry.[66]
StoneDrill has looked in the registry to find the default browser path.[67]
SUNBURST collected the registry value HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Cryptography\MachineGuid from compromised hosts.[68]
SynAck enumerates Registry keys associated with event logs.[69]
TEARDROP checked that HKU\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\CTF existed before decoding its embedded payload.[68][70] 
A Threat Group-3390 tool can read and decrypt stored Registry values.[71]
Turla surveys a system upon check-in to discover information in the Windows Registry with the reg query command.[29] Turla has also retrieved PowerShell payloads hidden in Registry keys as well as checking keys associated with null session named pipes .[72]
Ursnif has used Reg to query the Registry for installed programs.[73][74]
Valak can use the Registry for code updates and to collect credentials.[75]
Volgmer checks the system for certain Registry keys.[76]
Waterbear can query the Registry to retrieve data.[77]
WINDSHIELD can gather Registry values.[78]
Zebrocy executes the reg query command to obtain information in the Registry.[79]
Zeus Panda checks for the existence of a Registry key and if it contains certain values.[80]
ZIRCONIUM has used a tool to query the Registry for proxy settings.[81]
ZxShell can query the netsvc group value data located in the svchost group Registry key.[82] 
/techniques/T1012===========================
AdFind has the ability to query Active Directory for computers.[1][2][3]
APT29 has used AdFind to enumerate remote systems.[4]
APT3 has a tool that can detect the existence of remote systems.[5][6]

APT39 has used NBTscan and custom tools to discover remote systems. [8][9][10]
Bazar can enumerate remote systems using  Net View.[11]
BitPaymer can use net view to discover remote systems.[12]
BloodHound can enumerate and collect the properties of domain computers, including domain controllers.[13]
BRONZE BUTLER typically use ping and Net to enumerate systems.[14]
Carbon uses the net view command.[15]
Chimera has utilized various scans and queries to find domain controllers and remote services in the target environment.[16]
Cobalt Strike uses the native Windows Network Enumeration APIs to interrogate and discover targets in a Windows Active Directory network.[17][18]
Comnie runs the net view command
CrackMapExec can discover active IP addresses, along with the machine name, within a targeted network.[19]
Deep Panda has used ping to identify other machines of interest.[20]
Dragonfly 2.0 likely obtained a list of hosts in the victim environment.[21]
Epic uses the net view command on the victim’s machine.[22]
FIN5 has used the open source tool Essential NetTools to map the network and build a list of targets.[23]
FIN6 used publicly available tools (including Microsoft's built-in SQL querying tool, osql.exe) to map the internal network and conduct reconnaissance against Active Directory, Structured Query Language (SQL) servers, and NetBIOS.[24]
FIN8 uses dsquery and other Active Directory utilities to enumerate hosts.[25]
Fox Kitten has used Angry IP Scanner to detect remote systems.[26]
GALLIUM used a modified version of NBTscan to identify available NetBIOS name servers over the network as well as ping to identify remote systems.[27]
Ke3chang has used network scanning and enumeration tools, including Ping.[28]
Kinsing has used a script to parse files like /etc/hosts and SSH known_hosts to discover remote systems.[29]
Kwampirs collects a list of available servers with the command net view.[30]
Leafminer used Microsoft’s Sysinternals tools to gather detailed information about remote systems.[31]
menuPass uses scripts to enumerate IP ranges on the victim network. menuPass has also issued the command net view /domain to a PlugX implant to gather information about remote systems on the network.[32][33]
MURKYTOP has the capability to identify remote hosts on connected networks.[34]
NBTscan can list NetBIOS computer names.[35][36] 
Commands such as net view can be used in Net to gather information about available remote systems.[37]
njRAT can identify remote hosts on connected networks.[38]
Nltest may be used to enumerate remote domain controllers using options such as /dclist and /dsgetdc.[39]
Olympic Destroyer uses Windows Management Instrumentation to enumerate all systems in the network.[40]
Operation Wocao can use the ping command to discover remote systems.[41]
OSInfo performs a connection test to discover remote systems in the network[5]
Ping can be used to identify remote systems within a network.[42]
PoetRAT used Nmap for remote system discovery.[43]
RATANKBA runs the net view /domain and net view commands.[44]
Remsec can ping or traceroute a remote host.[45]
Rocke has looked for IP addresses in the known_hosts file on the infected system and attempted to SSH into them.[46] 
Sandworm Team has used a tool to query Active Directory using LDAP, discovering information about computers listed in AD.[47]
Shamoon scans the C-class subnet of the IPs on the victim's interfaces.[48]
SHOTPUT has a command to list all servers in the domain, as well as one to locate domain controllers on a domain.[49]
Silence has used Nmap to scan the corporate network, build a network topology, and identify vulnerable hosts.[50] 
Sykipot may use net view /domain to display hostnames of available systems on a network.[51]
The TAINTEDSCRIBE command and execution module can perform target system enumeration.[52]
Threat Group-3390 has used the net view command.[53]
TrickBot can enumerate computers and network devices.[54]
Turla surveys a system upon check-in to discover remote systems on a local network using the net view and net view /DOMAIN commands. Turla has also used net group "Domain Computers" /domain, net group "Domain Controllers" /domain, and net group "Exchange Servers" /domain to enumerate domain computers, including the organization's DC and Exchange Server.[22][55]
USBferry can use net view to gather information about remote systems.[56]
WannaCry scans its local network segment for remote systems to try to exploit and copy itself to.[57]
Wizard Spider has used networkdll for network discovery and psfin specifically for financial and point of sale indicators. Wizard Spider has also used AdFind and nltest/dclist to enumerate domain computers, including the domain controller.[3][58][59][1][60]
yty uses the net view command for discovery.[61]

APT3 has a tool that can obtain information about the local system.[17][18]
APT32 has collected the OS version and computer name from victims. One of the group's backdoors can also query the Windows Registry to gather system information, and another macOS backdoor performs a fingerprint of the machine on its first connection to the C&C server. APT32 executed shellcode to identify the name of the infected host.[19][20][21][22]

can collect system information, including computer name, system manufacturer, IsDebuggerPresent state, and execution path.[109]

Hydraq creates a backdoor through which remote attackers can retrieve information such as computer name, OS version, processor speed, memory size, and CPU speed.[117]

Kimsuky has gathered information about the infected computer.[136]
KOMPROGO is capable of retrieving information about the infected system.[137]
KONNI can gather the OS version, architecture information, connected drives, hostname, and computer name from the victim’s machine and has used systeminfo.exe to get a snapshot of the current system state of the target machine.[138][139]
Kwampirs collects OS version information such as registered owner details, manufacturer details, processor type, available storage, installed patches, hostname, version info, system date, and other system information by using the commands systeminfo, net config workstation, hostname, ver, set, and date /t.[140]
Several Lazarus Group malware families collect information on the type and version of the victim OS, as well as the victim computer name and CPU information. A Destover-like variant used by Lazarus Group also collects disk space information and sends it to its C2 server.[141][142][143][144][145].
LightNeuron gathers the victim computer name using the Win32 API call GetComputerName.[146]

Maze has checked the language of the infected system using the "GetUSerDefaultUILanguage" function.[153]

PUNCHBUGGY can gather system information such as computer names.[206] 
Pupy can grab a system’s information including the OS version, architecture, etc.[207]

Ramsay can detect system information--including disk names, total space, and remaining space--to create a hardware profile GUID which acts as a system identifier for operators.[209][210] 
RATANKBA gathers information about the OS architecture, OS name, and OS version/Service pack.[211][212]
Reaver collects system information from the victim, including CPU speed, computer name, volume serial number, ANSI code page, OEM code page identifier for the OS, Microsoft Windows version, and memory information.[213]

SLOTHFULMEDIA has collected system name, OS version, adapter information, memory usage, and disk information from a victim machine.[244]

Trojan.Karagany can capture information regarding the victim's OS, security, and hardware configuration.[265]
Tropic Trooper has detected a target system’s OS version and system volume information.[266][267]

yty gathers the computer name, the serial number of the main disk volume, CPU information, Microsoft Windows version, and runs the command systeminfo.[287]

zwShell can obtain the victim PC name and OS version.[297]
