/techniques/T1082===========================
AdFind can extract subnet information from Active Directory.[1][2][3]
admin@338 actors used the following command after exploiting a machine with LOWBALL malware to acquire information about local networks: ipconfig /all >> %temp%\download[4]
Agent Tesla can collect the IP address of the victim machine and spawn instances of netsh.exe to enumerate wireless settings.[5][6] 
Agent.btz collects the network adapter’s IP and MAC address as well as IP addresses of the network adapter’s default gateway, primary/secondary WINS, DHCP, and DNS servers, and saves them into a log file.[7]
Anchor can determine the public IP and location of a compromised host.[8]
APT1 used the ipconfig /all command to gather network configuration information.[9]
APT19 used an HTTP malware variant and a Port 22 malware variant to collect the MAC address and IP address from the victim’s machine.[10]
A keylogging tool used by APT3 gathers network information from the victim, including the MAC address, IP address, WINS, DHCP server, and gateway.[11][12]
APT32 used the ipconfig /all command to gather the IP address from the system.[13]
APT41 collected MAC addresses from victim machines.[14] 
Aria-body has the ability to identify the location, public IP address, and domain name on a compromised host.[15]
Arp can be used to display ARP configuration information on the host.
Astaroth collects the external IP address from the system. [16]
Avenger can identify the domain of the compromised host.[17]
Azorult can collect host IP information from the victim’s machine.[18]
BabyShark has executed the ipconfig /all command.[19] 
Backdoor.Oldrea collects information about the Internet adapter configuration.[20]
BADCALL collects the network adapter information.[21]
Bazar can collect the IP address and NetBIOS name of an infected machine.[22]
Bisonal can execute ipconfig on the victim’s machine.[23]
BlackEnergy has gathered information about network IP configurations using ipconfig.exe and about routing tables using route.exe.[24][25]
BLINDINGCAN has collected the victim machine's local IP address information and MAC address.[26]
Bonadan can find the external IP address of the infected host.[27]
Brave Prince gathers network configuration information as well as the ARP cache.[28]
Calisto runs the ifconfig command to obtain the IP address from the victim’s machine.[29]
Carbon can collect the IP address of the victims and other computers on the network using the commands: ipconfig -all nbtstat -n, and nbtstat -s.[30][31]
Catchamas gathers the Mac address, IP address, and the network adapter information from the victim’s machine.[32]
Caterpillar WebShell can gather the IP address from the victim's machine using the IP config command.[33] 
Chimera has used ipconfig, Ping, and tracert to enumerate the IP address and network environment and settings of the local host.[34]
Cobalt Strike can determine the IP addresses of domain controllers.[35]
Comnie uses ipconfig /all and route PRINT to identify network adapter and interface information.[36]
Conti can retrieve the ARP cache from the local system by using the GetIpNetTable() API call and check to ensure IP addresses it connects to are for local, non-Internet, systems.[37] 
CrackMapExec can collect DNS information from the targeted system.[38]
Crimson contains a command to collect the victim MAC address and LAN IP.[39]
Darkhotel has collected the IP address and network adapter information from the victim’s machine.[40][41]
Denis uses ipconfig to gather the IP address from the system.[13]
down_new has the ability to identify the MAC address of a compromised host.[17]
Dragonfly 2.0 used batch scripts to enumerate network information, including information about trusts, zones, and the domain.[42]
Dtrack can collect the host's IP addresses using the ipconfig command.[43][44]
The reconnaissance modules used with Duqu can collect information on network configuration.[45]
Dyre has the ability to identify network settings on a compromised host.[46]
Elise executes ipconfig /all after initial communication is made to the remote server.[47][48]
Emissary has the capability to execute the command ipconfig /all.[49]
Empire can acquire network configuration information like DNS servers and network proxies used by a host.[50]
Epic uses the nbtstat -n and nbtstat -s commands on the victim’s machine.[51]
Explosive has collected the MAC address from the victim's machine.[52] 
FALLCHILL collects MAC address and local IP address information from the victim.[53]
FatDuke can identify the MAC address on the target computer.[54]
Felismus collects the victim LAN IP address and sends it to the C2 server.[55]
FELIXROOT collects information about the network including the IP address and DHCP server.[56]
Frankenstein has enumerated hosts, looking for the public IP address of the system.[57]

GeminiDuke collects information on network settings and Internet proxy settings from the victim.[59]
GoldMax retrieved a list of the system's network interface after execution.[60]
Grandoreiro can determine the IP and physical location of the compromised host via IPinfo.[61]
GravityRAT collects the victim IP address, MAC address, as well as the victim account domain name.[62]
Higaisa used ipconfig to gather network configuration information.[63][64]
HotCroissant has the ability to identify the IP address of the compromised machine.[65]
Hydraq creates a backdoor through which remote attackers can retrieve IP addresses of compromised machines.[66][67]
ifconfig can be used to display adapter configuration on Unix systems, including information for TCP/IP, DNS, and DHCP.

zwShell has used RDP for lateral movement.[50]
ZxShell has remote desktop functionality.[51] 
/techniques/T1021/001===========================
Anchor can support windows execution via SMB shares.[4]
APT3 will copy files over to Windows Admin Shares (like ADMIN$) as part of lateral movement.[5]
APT32 used Net to use Windows' hidden network shares to copy their tools to remote machines for execution.[6]
APT39 has used SMB for lateral movement.[7]
APT41 has transferred implant files using Windows Admin Shares.[8]
BlackEnergy has run a plug-in on a victim to spread through the local network by using PsExec and accessing admin shares.[9]
Blue Mockingbird has used Windows Explorer to manually copy malicious files to remote hosts over SMB.[10]
Chimera has used Windows admin shares to move laterally.[11][12]
Cobalt Strike can use Window admin shares (C$ and ADMIN$) for lateral movement.[13]
Conti can spread via SMB and encrypts files on different hosts, potentially compromising an entire network.[14][15]
Deep Panda uses net.exe to connect to network shares using net use commands with compromised credentials.[16]
Adversaries can instruct Duqu to spread laterally by copying itself to shares it has enumerated and for which it has obtained legitimate credentials (via keylogging or other means). The remote host is then infected by using the compromised credentials to schedule a task on remote machines that executes the malware.[17]
Emotet leverages the Admin$ share for lateral movement once the local admin password has been brute forced. [18] 
FIN8 has attempted to map to C$ on enumerated hosts to test the scope of their current credentials/context.[19]
Fox Kitten has used valid accounts to access SMB shares.[20]
Ke3chang actors have been known to copy files to the network shares of other computers to move laterally.[21][22]
Kwampirs copies itself over network shares to move laterally on a victim network.[23]
Lazarus Group malware SierraAlfa accesses the ADMIN$ share via SMB to conduct lateral movement.[24][25]
Lucifer can infect victims by brute forcing SMB.[26]
Lateral movement can be done with Net through net use commands to connect to the on remote systems.[27]
Net Crawler uses Windows admin shares to establish authenticated sessions to remote systems over SMB as part of lateral movement.[28]
NotPetya can use PsExec, which interacts with the ADMIN$ network share to execute commands on remote systems.[29][30][31]
Olympic Destroyer uses PsExec to interact with the ADMIN$ network share to execute commands on remote systems.[32][31]
Operation Wocao has used Impacket's smbexec.py as well as accessing the C$ and IPC$ shares to move laterally.[33]
Orangeworm has copied its backdoor across open network shares, including ADMIN$, C$WINDOWS, D$WINDOWS, and E$WINDOWS.[23]
PsExec, a tool that has been used by adversaries, writes programs to the ADMIN$ network share to execute commands on remote systems.[31]
The Regin malware platform can use Windows admin shares to move laterally.[34]
Ryuk has used the C$ network share for lateral movement.[35]
Shamoon accesses network share(s), enables share access to the target device, copies an executable payload to the target system, and uses a Scheduled Task/Job to execute the malware.[36]
Threat Group-1314 actors mapped network drives using net use.[37]
Turla used net use commands to connect to lateral systems within a network.[38]
Wizard Spider has used SMB to drop Cobalt Strike Beacon on a domain controller for lateral movement.[39][40]
zwShell has been copied over network shares to move laterally.[41]

/techniques/T1560/002===========================
ADVSTORESHELL compresses output data generated by command execution with a custom implementation of the Lempel–Ziv–Welch (LZW) algorithm.[1]
Agent.btz saves system information into an XML file that is then XOR-encoded.[2]
Attor encrypts collected data with a custom implementation of Blowfish and RSA ciphers.[3]
CopyKittens encrypts data with a substitute cipher prior to exfiltration.[4]
Modules can be pushed to and executed by Duqu that copy data to a staging area, compress it, and XOR encrypt it.[5]
FIN6 has encoded data gathered from the victim with a simple substitution cipher and single-byte XOR using the 0xAA key, and Base64 with character permutation.[6][7]
FLASHFLOOD employs the same encoding scheme as SPACESHIP for data it stages. Data is compressed with zlib, and bytes are rotated four times before being XOR'ed with 0x23.[8]
FrameworkPOS can XOR credit card information before exfiltration.[9]
HAWKBALL has encrypted data with XOR before sending it over the C2 channel.[10]
InvisiMole uses a variation of the XOR cipher to encrypt files before exfiltration.[11]
Kimsuky has used RC4 encryption before exfil.[12]
A Lazarus Group malware sample encrypts data using a simple byte based XOR operation prior to exfiltration.[13][14][15][16]
Machete's collected data is encrypted with AES before exfiltration.[17] 
MESSAGETAP has XOR-encrypted and stored contents of SMS messages that matched its target list. [18]
Mustang Panda has encrypted documents with RC4 prior to exfiltration.[19]
NETWIRE has used a custom encryption algorithm to encrypt collected data.[20]
Okrum has used a custom implementation of AES encryption to encrypt collected data.[21]
OopsIE compresses collected files with a simple character replacement scheme before sending them to its C2 server.[22]
OwaAuth DES-encrypts captured credentials using the key 12345678 before writing the credentials to a log file.[23]
Ramsay can store collected documents in a custom container after encrypting and compressing them using RC4 and WinRAR.[24]
RawPOS encodes credit card data it collected from the victim with XOR.[25][26][27]
Reaver encrypts collected data with an incremental XOR key prior to exfiltration.[28]
RGDoor encrypts files with XOR before sending them back to the C2 server.[29]
Rising Sun can archive data using RC4 encryption and Base64 encoding prior to exfiltration.[30] 
Data SPACESHIP copies to the staging area is compressed with zlib. Bytes are rotated by four positions and XOR'ed with 0x23.[8]
StrongPity can compress and encrypt archived files into multiple .sft files with a repeated xor encryption scheme.[31][32]
T9000 encrypts collected data using a single byte XOR key.[33]

/techniques/T1123===========================
APT1 used a batch script to perform a series of discovery techniques and saves it to a text file.[1]
APT28 used a publicly available tool to gather and compress multiple documents on the DCCC and DNC networks.[2]
Attor has automatically collected data about the compromised system.[3]
BADNEWS monitors USB devices and copies files with certain extensions toa predefined directory.[4]
Bankshot recursively generates a list of files within a directory and sends them back to the control server.[5]
Chimera has used custom DLLs for continuous retrieval of data from memory.[6]
Comnie executes a batch script to store discovery information in %TEMP%\info.dat and then uploads the temporarily file to the remote C2 server.[7]
Crutch can automatically monitor removable drives in a loop and copy interesting files.[8]
FIN5 scans processes on all victim systems in the environment and uses automated scripts to pull back the results.[9]
FIN6 has used a script to iterate through a list of compromised PoS systems, copy and remove data to a log file, and to bind to events from the submit payment button.[10][11]
Frankenstein has enumerated hosts via Empire, gathering the username, domain name, machine name, and other system information.[12]
Gamaredon Group has deployed scripts on compromised systems that automatically scan for interesting documents.[13]
GoldFinder logged and stored information related to the route or hops a packet took from a compromised machine to a hardcoded C2 server, including the target C2 URL, HTTP response/status code, HTTP response headers and values, and data received from the C2 node.[14] 
A Helminth VBScript receives a batch script to execute a set of commands in a command prompt.[15]
InvisiMole can sort and collect specific documents as well as generate a list of all files on a newly inserted drive and store them in an encrypted file.[16][17]
LightNeuron can be configured to automatically collect files under a specified directory.[18]
menuPass has used the Csvde tool to collect Active Directory files and data.[19]
MESSAGETAP checks two files, keyword_parm.txt and parm.txt, for instructions on how to target and save data parsed and extracted from SMS message data from the network traffic. If an SMS message contained either a phone number, IMSI number, or keyword that matched the predefined list, it is saved to a CSV file for later theft by the threat actor.[20]
Metamorfo has automatically collected mouse clicks, continuous screenshots on the machine, and set timers to collect the contents of the clipboard and website browsing.[21] 
Micropsia executes an RAR tool to recursively archive files based on a predefined list of file extensions (.xls, .xlsx, .csv, .odt, .doc, .docx, .ppt, .pptx, .pdf, .mdb, .accdb, .accde, *.txt).[22]
Mustang Panda used custom batch scripts to collect files automatically from a targeted system.[23]
NETWIRE can automatically archive collected data.[24]
OilRig has used automated collection.[25]
Operation Wocao has used a script to collect information about the infected system.[26]
Patchwork developed a file stealer to search C:\ and collect files with certain extensions. Patchwork also executed a script to enumerate all drives, store them as a list, and upload generated files to the C2 server.[4]
PoetRAT used file system monitoring to track modification and enable automatic exfiltration.[27]
PoshC2 contains a module for recursively parsing through files and directories to gather valid credit card numbers.[28]
Proxysvc automatically collects data about the victim and sends it to the control server.[29]
Ramsay can conduct an initial scan for Microsoft Word documents on the local system, removable media, and connected network drives, before tagging and collecting them. It can continue tagging documents to collect with follow up scans.[30] 
Rover automatically collects files from the local system and removable drives based on a predefined list of file extensions on a regular timeframe.[31]
RTM monitors browsing activity and automatically captures screenshots if a victim browses to a URL matching one of a list of strings.[32][33]
ShimRatReporter gathered information automatically, without instruction from a C2, related to the user and host machine that is compiled into a report and sent to the operators.[34]
Sidewinder has used tools to automatically collect system and network configuration information.[35]
StrongPity has a file searcher component that can automatically collect and archive files based on a predefined list of file extensions.[36]
T9000 searches removable storage devices for files with a pre-defined list of file extensions (e.g. * .doc, .ppt, .xls, .docx, .pptx, *.xlsx). Any matching files are encrypted and written to a local user directory.[37]
TajMahal has the ability to index and compress files into a send queue for exfiltration.[38]
Threat Group-3390 ran a command to compile an archive of file types of interest from the victim user's directories.[39]
Tropic Trooper has collected information automatically using the adversary's USBferry attack.[40] 
For all non-removable drives on a victim, USBStealer executes automated collection of certain files for later exfiltration.[41]
Valak can download a module to search for and build a report of harvested credential data.[42]
VERMIN saves each collected file with the automatically generated format {{0:dd-MM-yyyy}}.txt .[43]
WindTail can identify and add files that possess specific file extensions to an array for archiving.[44]
Zebrocy scans the system and automatically collects files with the following extensions: .doc, .docx, ,.xls, .xlsx, .pdf, .pptx, .rar, .zip, .jpg, .jpeg, .bmp, .tiff, .kum, .tlg, .sbx, .cr, .hse, .hsf, and .lhz.[45][46]

yty collects files with the following extensions: .ppt, .pptx, .pdf, .doc, .docx, .xls, .xlsx, .docm, .rtf, .inp, .xlsm, .csv, .odt, .pps, .vcf and sends them back to the C2 server.[107]
/techniques/T1005===========================
When it first starts, BADNEWS crawls the victim's mapped drives and collects documents with the following extensions: .doc, .docx, .pdf, .ppt, .pptx, and .txt.[1]
BRONZE BUTLER has exfiltrated files stolen from file shares.[2]
Chimera has collected data of interest from network shares.[3]
CosmicDuke steals user files from network shared drives with file extensions and keywords that match a predefined list.[4]
Egregor can collect any files found in the enumerated drivers before sending it to its C2 channel.[5] 
Fox Kitten has searched network shares to access sensitive documents.[6]
Gamaredon Group malware has collected Microsoft Office documents from mapped network drives.[7]
menuPass has collected data from remote systems by mounting network shares with net use and using Robocopy to transfer data.[8]
Ramsay can collect data from network drives and stage it for exfiltration.[9] 
Sowbug extracted Word documents from a file server on a victim network.[10]
/techniques/T1039===========================
An APT28 backdoor may collect the entire contents of an inserted USB device.[1]
Aria-body has the ability to collect data from USB devices.[2]
BADNEWS copies files with certain extensions from USB devices toa predefined directory.[3]
CosmicDuke steals user files from removable media with file extensions and keywords that match a predefined list.[4]
Crimson contains a module to collect data from removable drives.[5]
Crutch can monitor removable drives and exfiltrate files matching a given extension list.[6]
Explosive can scan all .exe files located in the USB drive.[7] 
FLASHFLOOD searches for interesting files (either a default or customized set of file extensions) on removable media and copies them to a staging area. The default file types copied would include data copied to the drive by SPACESHIP.[8]
A Gamaredon Group file stealer has the capability to steal data from newly connected logical volumes on a system, including USB drives.[9][10]
GravityRAT steals files based on an extension list if a USB drive is connected to the system.[11]
InvisiMole can collect jpeg files from connected MTP devices.[12]
Machete can find, encrypt, and upload files from fixed and removable drives.[13][14] 
Prikormka contains a module that collects documents with certain extensions from removable media or fixed drives connected via USB.[15]
Ramsay can collect data from removable media and stage it for exfiltration.[16] 
Remsec has a package that collects documents from any inserted USB sticks.[17]
Rover searches for files on attached removable drives based on a predefined list of file extensions every five seconds.[18]
TajMahal has the ability to steal written CD images and files of interest from previously connected removable drives when they become available again.[19]
Turla RPC backdoors can collect files from USB thumb drives.[20][21]
Once a removable media device is inserted back into the first victim, USBStealer collects data from it that was exfiltrated from a second victim.[22][23]

ADVSTORESHELL stores output from command execution in a .dat file in the %TEMP% directory.[1]

Machete stores files and logs in a folder on the local drive.[41][42]
menuPass stages data prior to exfiltration in multi-part archives, often saved in the Recycle Bin.[43]
MESSAGETAP stored targeted SMS messages that matched its target list in CSV files on the compromised system.[44]
MoonWind saves information from its keylogging routine as a .zip file in the present working directory.[45]
Mustang Panda has stored collected credential files in c:\windows\temp prior to exfiltration. Mustang Panda has also stored documents for exfiltration in a hidden folder on USB drives.[46][47]

PoisonIvy stages collected data in a text file.[53]
Prikormka creates a directory, %USERPROFILE%\AppData\Local\SKC\, which is used to store collected log files.[54]
Pteranodon creates various subdirectories under %Temp%\reports\% and copies files to those subdirectories. It also creates a folder at C:\Users\\AppData\Roaming\Microsoft\store to store screenshot JPEG files.[55]
PUNCHBUGGY has saved information to a random temp file before exfil.[56]
PUNCHTRACK aggregates collected data in a tmp file.[57]
Ramsay can stage data prior to exfiltration in %APPDATA%\Microsoft\UserSetting and %APPDATA%\Microsoft\UserSetting\MediaCache.[58][59] 
Data captured by RawPOS is placed in a temporary file under a directory named "memdump".[60]

Sidewinder has collected stolen files in a temporary folder in preparation for exfiltration.[62]

/techniques/T1114/001===========================

/techniques/T1114/003===========================
Agent Tesla has the ability to use form-grabbing to extract data from web data forms.[5]

Grandoreiro can monitor browser activity for online banking actions and display full-screen overlay images to block user access to the intended site or present additional data fields.[9][10][11]
IcedID has used web injection attacks to redirect victims to spoofed sites designed to harvest banking and other credentials.  IcedID can use a self signed TLS certificate in connection with the spoofed site and simultaneously maintains a live connection with the legitimate site to display the correct URL and certificates in the browser.[12][13]
Melcoz can monitor the victim's browser for online banking sessions and display an overlay window to manipulate the session in the background.[9]
TrickBot uses web injects and browser redirection to trick the user into providing their login credentials on a fake or modified web page.[14][15][16][17]
Ursnif has injected HTML codes into banking sites to steal sensitive online banking information (ex: usernames and passwords).[18]

/techniques/T1071/004===========================
APT28 uses a tool that captures information from air-gapped computers via an infected USB and transfers it to network-connected computer when the USB is inserted.[1]
Part of APT28's operation involved using CHOPSTICK modules to copy itself to air-gapped machines, using files written to USB sticks to transfer data and command traffic.[2][3][1]
USBStealer drops commands for a second victim onto a removable media drive inserted into the first victim, and commands are executed when the drive is inserted into the second victim.[4]
/techniques/T1092===========================
C2 traffic from ADVSTORESHELL is encrypted, then encoded with Base64 encoding.[3]
An APT19 HTTP malware variant used Base64 to encode communications to the C2 server.[4]
APT33 has used base64 to encode command and control traffic.[5]
Astaroth encodes data using Base64 before sending it to the C2 server. [6]
AutoIt backdoor has sent a C2 response that was base64-encoded.[7]
BabyShark has encoded data using certutil before exfiltration.[8]
Some Backdoor.Oldrea samples use standard Base64 + bzip2, and some use standard Base64 + reverse XOR + RSA-2048 to decrypt data received from C2 servers.[9]
BADNEWS encodes C2 traffic with base64.[7][10][11]
BLINDINGCAN has encoded its C2 traffic with Base64.[12]
Several BRONZE BUTLER tools encode data with base64 when posting it to a C2 server.[13]
BS2005 uses Base64 encoding for communication in the message body of an HTTP request.[14]
Carbanak encodes the message body of HTTP traffic with Base64.[15][16]
ChChes can encode C2 data with a custom technique that utilizes Base64.[17][18] 
Cobian RAT obfuscates communications with the C2 server using Base64 encoding.[19]
CORESHELL C2 messages are Base64-encoded.[20]
Daserf uses custom base64 encoding to obfuscate HTTP traffic.[13]
Denis encodes the data sent to the server in Base64.[21]
Dipsind encodes C2 traffic with base64.[22]
down_new has the ability to base64 encode C2 communications.[23]
Ebury has encoded C2 traffic in hexadecimal format.[24] 
Elise exfiltrates data using cookie values that are Base64-encoded.[25]
Some Felismus samples use a custom method for C2 traffic that utilizes Base64.[26]
Fysbis can use Base64 to encode its C2 traffic.[27]
gh0st RAT has used Zlib to compress C2 communications data before encrypting it.[28]
HAFNIUM has used ASCII encoding for C2 traffic.[29]
For C2 over HTTP, Helminth encodes data with base64 and sends it via the "Cookie" field of HTTP requests. For C2 over DNS, Helminth converts ASCII characters into their hexadecimal values and sends the data in cleartext.[30]
HOPLIGHT has utilized Zlib compression to obfuscate the communications payload. [31] 
Ixeshe uses custom Base64 encoding schemes to obfuscate command and control traffic in the message body of HTTP requests.[32][33]
A JHUHUGIT variant encodes C2 POST data base64.[34]
Kazuar encodes communications to the C2 server in Base64.[35]
Kessel has exfiltrated data via hexadecimal-encoded subdomain fields of DNS queries.[36]
KONNI has used a custom base64 key to encode stolen data before exfiltration.[37]
A Lazarus Group malware sample encodes data with base64.[38]
Machete has used base64 encoding.[39]
MechaFlounder has the ability to use base16 encoded strings in C2.[40]
Mis-Type uses Base64 encoding for C2 traffic.[41]
Misdat network traffic is Base64-encoded plaintext.[41]
More_eggs has used basE91 encoding, along with encryption, for C2 communication.[42]
MuddyWater has used tools to encode C2 communications including Base64 encoding.[43][44]
njRAT uses Base64 encoding for C2 traffic.[45]
Octopus encodes C2 communications in Base64.[46]
Okrum has used base64 to encode C2 communication.[47]

Responses from the Pisloader C2 server are base32-encoded.[50]

POWERSTATS encoded C2 traffic with base64.[53]

Prikormka encodes C2 traffic with Base64.[55]
QUADAGENT encodes C2 communications with base64.[56]
Ramsay has used base64 to encode its C2 traffic.[57]
RDAT can communicate with the C2 via base32-encoded subdomains.[58] 
Revenge RAT uses Base64 to encode information sent to the C2 server.[59]
RogueRobin base64 encodes strings that are sent to the C2 over its DNS tunnel.[60]

SeaDuke C2 traffic is base64-encoded.[62]
Spark has encoded communications with the C2 server with base64.[63] 
SpeakUp encodes C&C communication using Base64. [64]

/techniques/T1132/001===========================
Newer variants of BACKSPACE will encode C2 communications with a custom system.[3]
Bankshot encodes commands from the control server using a range of characters and gzip.[4]
InvisiMole can use a modified base32 encoding to encode data within the subdomain of C2 requests.[5]
OceanSalt can encode data with a NOT operation before sending the data to the control server.[6]
RDAT can communicate with the C2 via subdomains that utilize base64 with character substitutions.[7] 
ShadowPad has encoded data as readable Latin characters.[8]
/techniques/T1132/002===========================
APT28 added "junk data" to each encoded string, preventing trivial decoding without knowledge of the junk removal algorithm. Each implant was given a "junk length" value when created, tracked by the controller software to allow seamless communication but prevent analysis of the command protocol on the wire.[1]
BendyBear has used byte randomization to obscure its behavior.[2]
Downdelph inserts pseudo-random characters between each original character during encoding of C2 network requests, making it difficult to write signatures on them.[3]
GoldMax has used decoy traffic to surround its malicious network traffic to avoid detection.[4]
P2P ZeuS added junk data to outgoing UDP packets to peer implants.[5]
PLEAD samples were found to be highly obfuscated with junk code.[6]
SUNBURST added junk bytes to its C2 over HTTP.[7]
WellMess can use junk data in the Base64 string for additional obfuscation.[8]
/techniques/T1001/001===========================
APT29 has used steganography to hide C2 communications in images.[1]
Some malware that has been used by Axiom also uses steganography to hide communication in PNG image files.[2]
Daserf can use steganography to hide malicious code downloaded to the victim.[3]
When the Duqu command and control is operating over HTTP or HTTPS, Duqu uploads data to its controller by appending it to a blank JPG file.[4]
HAMMERTOSS is controlled via commands that are appended to image files.[5]
LightNeuron is controlled via commands that are embedded into PDFs and JPGs using steganographic methods.[6]
RDAT can process steganographic images attached to email messages to send and receive C2 commands. RDAT can also embed additional messages within BMP images to communicate with the RDAT operator.[7] 
SUNBURST C2 data attempted to appear as benign XML related to .NET assemblies or as a faux JSON blob.[8][9][10]
ZeroT has retrieved stage 2 payloads as Bitmap images that use Least Significant Bit (LSB) steganography.[11][12]
/techniques/T1001/002===========================
BADCALL uses a FakeTLS method during C2.[1]
Bankshot generates a false TLS handshake using a public certificate to disguise C2 network communications.[2]
FakeM C2 traffic attempts to evade detection by resembling data generated by legitimate messenger applications, such as MSN and Yahoo! messengers. Additionally, some variants of FakeM use modified SSL code for communications back to C2 servers, making SSL decryption ineffective.[3]
FALLCHILL uses fake Transport Layer Security (TLS) to communicate with its C2 server.[4]
HARDRAIN uses FakeTLS to communicate with its C2 server.[5]
Higaisa used a FakeTLS session for C2 communications.[6]
InvisiMole can mimic HTTP protocol with custom HTTP "verbs" HIDE, ZVVP, and NOP.[7][8]
KeyBoy uses custom SSL libraries to impersonate SSL in C2 traffic.[9]
Lazarus Group malware also uses a unique form of communication encryption known as FakeTLS that mimics TLS but uses a different encryption method, evading SSL man-in-the-middle decryption attacks.[10][11][12][13]
Okrum mimics HTTP protocol for C2 communication, while hiding the actual messages in the Cookie and Set-Cookie headers of the HTTP requests.[14]
SUNBURST masqueraded its network traffic as the Orion Improvement Program (OIP) protocol.[15]
TAINTEDSCRIBE has used FakeTLS for session authentication.[16]
/techniques/T1001/003===========================
APT41 has used DGAs to change their C2 servers monthly.[8]
Aria-body has the ability to use a DGA for C2 communications.[9]
Astaroth has used a DGA in C2 communications.[10]
Bazar can implement DGA using the current date as a seed variable.[11]
BONDUPDATER uses a DGA to communicate with command and control servers.[12]
CCBkdr can use a DGA for Fallback Channels if communications with the primary command and control server are lost.[4]
CHOPSTICK can use a DGA for Fallback Channels, domains are generated by concatenating words from lists.[7]
Doki has used the DynDNS service and a DGA based on the Dogecoin blockchain to generate C2 domains.[13]
Ebury has used a DGA to generate a domain name for C2.[14][15]
Grandoreiro can use a DGA for hiding C2 addresses, including use of an algorithm with a user-specific key that changes daily.[16][17]
MiniDuke can use DGA to generate new Twitter URLs for C2.[18]
Ngrok can provide DGA for C2 servers through the use of random URL strings that change every 12 hours.[19]
POSHSPY uses a DGA to derive command and control URLs from a word list.[6]
ShadowPad uses a DGA that is based on the day of the month for C2 servers.[20][21][8]
TA551 has used a DGA to generate URLs from executed macros.[22][23]
Ursnif has used a DGA to generate domain names for C2.[24]
/techniques/T1568/002===========================
gh0st RAT    operators have used dynamic DNS to mask the true location of their C2 behind rapidly changing IP addresses.[4]
menuPass has used dynamic DNS service providers to host malicious domains.[5]
njRAT has used a fast flux DNS for C2 IP resolution.[6]
TA505 has used fast flux to mask botnets by distributing payloads across multiple IPs.[7]
/techniques/T1568/001===========================
APT12 has used multiple variants of DNS Calculation including multiplying the first two octets of an IP address and adding the third octet to that value in order to get a resulting command and control port.[1]
/techniques/T1568/003===========================
3PARA RAT command and control commands are encrypted within the HTTP C2 channel using the DES algorithm in CBC mode with a key derived from the MD5 hash of the string HYF54&%9&jkMCXuiS. 3PARA RAT will use an 8-byte XOR key derived from the string HYF54&%9&jkMCXuiS if the DES decoding fails[1]
4H RAT obfuscates C2 communication using a 1-byte XOR with the key 0xBE.[1]
A variant of ADVSTORESHELL encrypts some C2 with 3DES.[2]
APT28 installed a Delphi backdoor that used a custom algorithm for C2 communications.[3]
APT33 has used AES for encryption of command and control traffic.[4]
Attor has encrypted data symmetrically using a randomly generated Blowfish (OFB) key which is encrypted with a public RSA key.[5]
Azorult can encrypt C2 traffic using XOR.[6][7]
BADCALL encrypts C2 traffic using an XOR/ADD cipher.[8]
BADNEWS encrypts C2 data with a ROR by 3 and an XOR by 0x23.[9][10]
Bazar can send C2 communications with XOR encryption.[11]
BBSRAT uses a custom encryption algorithm on data sent back to the C2 server over HTTP.[12]
BendyBear communicates to a C2 server over port 443 using modified RC4 and XOR-encrypted chunks.[13] 
Bisonal variants reported on in 2014 and 2015 used a simple XOR cipher for C2. Some Bisonal samples encrypt C2 communications with RC4.[14]
BLINDINGCAN has encrypted its C2 traffic with RC4.[15]
Bonadan can XOR-encrypt C2 communications.[16]
BRONZE BUTLER has used RC4 encryption (for Datper malware) and AES (for xxmm malware) to obfuscate HTTP traffic. BRONZE BUTLER has also used a tool called RarStar that encodes data with a custom XOR algorithm when posting it to a C2 server.[17]
CallMe uses AES to encrypt C2 traffic.[18]
Carbanak encrypts the message body of HTTP traffic with RC2 (in CBC mode). Carbanak also uses XOR with random keys for its communications.[19][20]
Cardinal RAT uses a secret key with a series of XOR and addition operations to encrypt C2 traffic.[21]
Chaos provides a reverse shell connection on 8338/TCP, encrypted via AES.[22]
ChChes can encrypt C2 traffic with AES or RC4.[23][24]
CHOPSTICK encrypts C2 communications with RC4.[25]
Cobalt Strike has the ability to use AES-256 symmetric encryption in CBC mode with HMAC-SHA-256 to encrypt task commands and XOR to encrypt shell code and configuration data.[26]
Comnie encrypts command and control communications with RC4.[27]
CORESHELL C2 messages are encrypted with custom stream ciphers using six-byte or eight-byte keys.[28]
CosmicDuke contains a custom version of the RC4 algorithm that includes a programming error.[29]
Darkhotel has used AES-256 and 3DES for C2 communications.[30]
Daserf uses RC4 encryption to obfuscate HTTP traffic.[17]
Derusbi obfuscates C2 traffic with variable 4-byte XOR keys.[31]
Dipsind encrypts C2 data with AES256 in ECB mode.[32]
down_new has the ability to AES encrypt C2 communications.[33]
Downdelph uses RC4 to encrypt C2 responses.[34]
Dridex has encrypted traffic with RC4.[35]
The Duqu command and control protocol's data stream can be encrypted with AES-CBC.[36]
Ebury has encrypted C2 traffic using the client IP address, then encoded it as a hexadecimal string.[37]
Elise encrypts exfiltrated data with RC4.[38]
The C2 server response to a beacon sent by a variant of Emissary contains a 36-character GUID value that is used as an encryption key for subsequent network communications. Some variants of Emissary use various XOR operations to encrypt C2 data.[39]
Epic encrypts commands from the C2 server using a hardcoded key.[40]
Explosive has encrypted communications with the RC4 method.[41] 
The original variant of FakeM encrypts C2 traffic using a custom encryption cipher that uses an XOR key of "YHCRA" and bit rotation between each XOR operation. Some variants of FakeM use RC4 to encrypt C2 traffic.[18]
FALLCHILL encrypts C2 data with RC4 encryption.[42][43]
FatDuke can AES encrypt C2 communications.[44]
Some Felismus samples use a custom encryption method for C2 traffic that utilizes AES and multiple keys.[45]
FlawedAmmyy has used SEAL encryption during the initial C2 handshake.[46]
Frankenstein has communicated with a C2 via an encrypted RC4 byte stream and AES-CBC.[47]
Gazer uses custom encryption for C2 that uses 3DES.[48][49]
gh0st RAT uses RC4 and XOR to encrypt C2 traffic.[50]
GreyEnergy encrypts communications using AES256.[51]
H1N1 encrypts C2 traffic using an RC4 key.[52]
Before being appended to image files, HAMMERTOSS commands are encrypted with a key composed of both a hard-coded value and a string contained on that day's tweet. To decrypt the commands, an investigator would need access to the intended malware sample, the day's tweet, and the image file containing the command.[53]
Helminth encrypts data sent to its C2 server over HTTP with RC4.[54]
Hi-Zor encrypts C2 traffic with a double XOR using two distinct single-byte keys.[55]
HiddenWasp uses an RC4-like algorithm with an already computed PRGA generated key-stream for network communication.[56]
Higaisa used AES-128 to encrypt C2 traffic.[57]
Hikit performs XOR encryption.[58]
HotCroissant has compressed network communications and encrypted them with a custom stream cipher.[59][60]
httpclient encrypts C2 content with XOR using a single byte, 0x12.[1]
Hydraq C2 traffic is encrypted using bitwise NOT and XOR operations.[61]
HyperStack has used RSA encryption for C2 communications.[62]
Inception has encrypted network communications with AES.[63]
InvisiMole uses variations of a simple XOR encryption routine for C&C communications.[64]
KEYMARBLE uses a customized XOR algorithm to encrypt C2 communications.[65]
The Komplex C2 channel uses an 11-byte XOR algorithm to hide data.[66]
Several Lazarus Group malware families encrypt C2 traffic using custom code that uses XOR with an ADD operation and XOR with a SUB operation. Another Lazarus Group malware sample XORs C2 traffic. Other Lazarus Group malware uses Caracachs encryption to encrypt C2 payloads.[67][68][69][70]
LightNeuron uses AES to encrypt C2 traffic.[71]
LookBack uses a modified version of RC4 for data transfer.[72]
Lucifer can perform a decremental-xor encryption on the initial C2 request before sending it over the wire.[73]
Lurid performs XOR encryption.[74]
Machete has used AES to exfiltrate documents.[75]
MoonWind encrypts C2 traffic using RC4 with a static key.[76]
More_eggs has used an RC4-based encryption method for its C2 communications.[77]
Mosquito uses a custom encryption algorithm, which consists of XOR and a stream that is similar to the Blum Blum Shub algorithm.[78]
Mustang Panda has encrypted C2 communications with RC4.[79]
NanoCore uses DES to encrypt the C2 traffic.[80]
NDiskMonitor uses AES to encrypt certain information sent over its C2 channel.[10]
NETEAGLE will decrypt resources it downloads with HTTP requests by using RC4 with the key "ScoutEagle."[81]
NETWIRE can use AES encryption for C2 data transferred.[82]
Okrum uses AES to encrypt network traffic. The key can be hardcoded or negotiated with the C2 server in the registration phase. [83]
PipeMon communications are RC4 encrypted.[84]
PLAINTEE encodes C2 beacons using XOR.[85]
PLEAD has used RC4 encryption to download modules.[86]
PoisonIvy uses the Camellia cipher to encrypt communications.[87]
POWERTON has used AES for encrypting C2 traffic.[4]
Prikormka encrypts some C2 traffic with the Blowfish cipher.[88]
QuasarRAT uses AES to encrypt network communication.[89][90]
RDAT has used AES ciphertext to encode C2 communications.[91]
RedLeaves has encrypted C2 traffic with RC4, previously using keys of 88888888 and babybear.[92]
Rifdoor has encrypted command and control (C2) communications with a stream cipher.[59]
APT12 has used the RIPTIDE RAT, which communicates over HTTP with a payload encrypted with RC4.[93]
RTM encrypts C2 traffic with a custom RC4 variant.[94]
Sakula encodes C2 traffic with single-byte XOR keys.[95]
SeaDuke C2 traffic has been encrypted with RC4 and AES.[96][97]
SNUGRIDE encrypts C2 traffic using AES with a static key.[98]
Stealth Falcon malware encrypts C2 traffic using RC4 with a hard-coded key.[99]
SUNBURST encrypted C2 traffic using a single-byte-XOR cipher.[100]
Sys10 uses an XOR 0x1 loop to encrypt its C2 domain.[101]
Taidoor uses RC4 to encrypt the message body of HTTP content.[102]
TAINTEDSCRIBE uses a Linear Feedback Shift Register (LFSR) algorithm for network encryption.[103]
TrickBot uses a custom crypter leveraging Microsoft’s CryptoAPI to encrypt C2 traffic.[104]
TSCookie has encrypted network communications with RC4.[105]
Some versions of UPPERCUT have used the hard-coded string "this is the encrypt key" for Blowfish encryption when communicating with a C2. Later versions have hard-coded keys uniquely for each C2 address.[106]
Volgmer uses a simple XOR cipher to encrypt traffic and files.[107]
WellMess can encrypt HTTP POST data using RC6 and a dynamically generated AES key encrypted with a hard coded RSA public key.[108][109][110]
Winnti for Linux has used a custom TCP protocol with four-byte XOR for command and control (C2).[111]
ZeroT has used RC4 to encrypt C2 traffic.[112][113]
ZIRCONIUM has used AES encrypted communications in C2.[114]
/techniques/T1573/001===========================
adbupd contains a copy of the OpenSSL library to encrypt C2 traffic.[1]
A variant of ADVSTORESHELL encrypts some C2 with RSA.[2]
Attor's Blowfish key is encrypted with a public RSA key.[3]
Bazar can use TLS in C2 communications.[4]
BISCUIT uses SSL for encrypting C2 communications.[5]
Carbon has used RSA encryption for C2 communications.[6]
CHOPSTICK encrypts C2 communications with TLS.[7]
Cobalt Group has used the Plink utility to create SSH tunnels.[8]
Cobalt Strike can use RSA asymmetric encryption with PKCS1 padding to encrypt data sent to the C2 server.[9]
ComRAT can use SSL/TLS encryption for its HTTP-based C2 channel. ComRAT has used public key cryptography with RSA and AES encrypted email attachments for its Gmail C2 channel.[10][11] 
Doki has used the embedTLS library for network communications.[12]
Dridex has encrypted traffic with RSA.[13]
Emotet is known to use RSA keys for encrypting C2 traffic. [14]
Empire can use TLS to encrypt its C2 channel.[15]
FIN6 used the Plink command-line utility to create SSH tunnels to C2 servers.[16]
FIN8 has used the Plink utility to tunnel RDP back to C2 infrastructure.[17]
Gazer uses custom encryption for C2 that uses RSA.[18][19]
GoldMax has RSA-encrypted its communication with the C2 server.[20]
Grandoreiro can use SSL in C2 communication.[21]
GreyEnergy encrypts communications using RSA-2048.[22]
Hi-Zor encrypts C2 traffic with TLS.[23]
IcedID has used SSL and TLS in communications with C2.[24][25]
Koadic can use SSL and TLS for communications.[26]
Machete has used TLS-encrypted FTP to exfiltrate data.[27]
Metamorfo's C2 communication has been encrypted using OpenSSL.[28] 
OilRig used the Plink utility and other tools to create tunnels to C2 servers.[29]
Operation Wocao's proxy implementation "Agent" can upgrade the socket in use to a TLS socket.[30]
Pay2Key has used RSA encrypted communications with C2.[31]
Penquin can encrypt communications using the BlowFish algorithm and a symmetric key exchanged with Diffie Hellman.[32]
PoetRAT used TLS to encrypt command and control (C2) communications.[33]
POSHSPY encrypts C2 traffic with AES and RSA.[34]
POWERSTATS has encrypted C2 traffic with RSA.[35]
Pupy's default encryption for its C2 communication channel is SSL, but it also has transport options for RSA and AES.[36]
REvil has encrypted C2 communications with the ECIES algorithm.[37]
ServHelper may set up a reverse SSH tunnel to give the attacker access to services running on the victim, such as RDP.[38]
StrongPity has encrypted C2 traffic using SSL/TLS.[39]
Sykipot uses SSL for encrypting C2 communications.[40]
Tor encapsulates traffic in multiple layers of encryption, using TLS by default.[41]
Trojan.Karagany can secure C2 communications with SSL and TLS.[42]
Tropic Trooper has used SSL to connect to C2 servers.[43][44]
Some Volgmer variants use SSL to encrypt C2 communications.[45]
WannaCry uses Tor for command and control traffic and routes a custom cryptographic protocol over the Tor circuit.[46]
WellMail can use hard coded client and certificate authority certificates to communicate with C2 over mutual TLS.[47][48]
WellMess can communicate to C2 with mutual TLS where client and server mutually check certificates.[49][50][51][48]
XTunnel uses SSL/TLS and RC4 to encrypt traffic.[52][7]
Zebrocy uses SSL and AES ECB for encrypting C2 communications.[53][54][55] 
/techniques/T1573/002===========================
Anchor can use secondary C2 servers for communication after establishing connectivity and relaying victim information to primary C2 servers.[1]
APT41 used the Steam community page as a fallback mechanism for C2.[2] 
Bazar has the ability to use an alternative C2 server if the primary server fails.[3]
BISCUIT malware contains a secondary fallback command and control server that is contacted after the primary command and control server.[4][5]
BlackEnergy has the capability to communicate over a backup channel via plus.google.com.[6]
Carbanak’s Harpy backdoor malware can use DNS as a backup channel for C2 if HTTP fails. [7]
Cardinal RAT can communicate over multiple C2 host and port combinations.[8]
CHOPSTICK can switch to a new C2 channel if the current one is broken.[9]
Crutch has used a hardcoded GitHub repository as a fallback channel.[10]
Derusbi uses a backup communication method with an HTTP beacon.[11]
DustySky has two hard-coded domains for C2 servers; if the first does not respond, it will try the second.[12]
Ebury has implemented a fallback mechanism to begin using a DGA when the attacker hasn't connected to the infected system for three days.[13]
Exaramel for Linux can attempt to find a new C2 server if it receives an error.[14]
FatDuke has used several C2 servers per targeted organization.[15]
HOPLIGHT has multiple C2 channels in place in case one fails.[16] 
InvisiMole has been configured with several servers available for alternate C2 communications.[17][18]
JHUHUGIT tests if it can reach its C2 server by first attempting a direct connection, and if it fails, obtaining proxy settings and sending the connection through a proxy, and finally injecting code into a running browser if the proxy method fails.[19]
Kazuar can accept multiple URLs for C2 servers.[20]
Kwampirs uses a large list of C2 servers that it cycles through until a successful connection is established.[21]
Lazarus Group malware SierraAlfa sends data to one of the hard-coded C2 servers chosen at random, and if the transmission fails, chooses a new C2 server to attempt the transmission again.[22][23]
Linfo creates a backdoor through which remote attackers can change C2 servers.[24]
Machete has sent data over HTTP if FTP failed, and has also used a fallback server.[25] 
MiniDuke uses Google Search to identify C2 servers if its primary C2 method via Twitter is not working.[26]
Mis-Type first attempts to use a Base64-encoded network protocol over a raw TCP socket for C2, and if that method fails, falls back to a secondary HTTP-based protocol to communicate to an alternate C2 server.[27]
NETEAGLE will attempt to detect if the infected host is configured to a proxy. If so, NETEAGLE will send beacons via an HTTP POST request; otherwise it will send beacons via UDP/6000.[28]
OilRig malware ISMAgent falls back to its DNS tunneling mechanism if it is unable to reach the C2 server over HTTP.[29]
PipeMon can switch to an alternate C2 domain when a particular date has been reached.[30]
QUADAGENT uses multiple protocols (HTTPS, HTTP, DNS) for its C2 server as fallback channels if communication with one is unsuccessful.[31]
RDAT has used HTTP if DNS C2 communications were not functioning.[32] 
S-Type primarily uses port 80 for C2, but falls back to ports 443 or 8080 if initial communication fails.[27]
ShimRat has used a secondary C2 location if the first was unavailable.[33] 
SslMM has a hard-coded primary and backup C2 string.[34]
TAINTEDSCRIBE can randomly pick one of five hard-coded IP addresses for C2 communication; if one of the IP fails, it will wait 60 seconds and then try another IP address.[35]
TrickBot can use secondary C2 servers for communication after establishing connectivity and relaying victim information to primary C2 servers.[1]
Valak can communicate over multiple C2 hosts.[36]
WinMM is usually configured with primary and backup domains for C2 communications.[34]
The C2 server used by XTunnel provides a port number to the victim to use as a fallback in case the connection closes on the currently used port.[9]

/techniques/T1105===========================
An APT3 downloader first establishes a SOCKS5 connection to 192.157.198[.]103 using TCP port 1913; once the server response is verified, it then requests a connection to 192.184.60[.]229 on TCP port 81.[1]
APT41 used the storescyncsvc.dll BEACON backdoor to download a secondary backdoor.[2]
BACKSPACE attempts to avoid detection by checking a first stage command and control server to determine if it should connect to the second stage server, which performs "louder" interactions with the malware.[3]
The Bazar loader is used to download and execute the Bazar backdoor.[4][5]
BLACKCOFFEE uses Microsoft’s TechNet Web portal to obtain an encoded tag containing the IP address of a command and control server and then communicates separately with that IP address for C2. If the C2 server is discovered or shut down, the threat actors can update the encoded IP address on TechNet to maintain control of the victims’ machines.[6]
After initial compromise, Chaos will download a second stage to establish a more permanent presence on the affected system.[7]
MuddyWater has used one C2 to obtain enumeration scripts and monitor web logs, but a different C2 to send data back.[8] 
Valak can download additional modules and malware capable of using separate C2 channels.[9]

Anchor has used ICMP in C2 communications.[4]

FIN6 has used Metasploit Bind and Reverse TCP stagers.[16]

InvisiMole has used TCP to download additional modules.[20]
LookBack uses a custom binary protocol over sockets for C2 communications.[21]
Metamorfo has used raw TCP for C2.[22] 
Mis-Type network traffic can communicate over a raw socket.[23]
Misdat network traffic communicates over a raw socket.[23]
MoonWind completes network communication via raw sockets.[24]
If NETEAGLE does not detect a proxy configured on the infected machine, it will send beacons via UDP/6000. Also, after retrieving a C2 IP address and Port Number, NETEAGLE will initiate a TCP connection to this socket. The ensuing connection is a plaintext C2 channel in which commands are specified by DWORDs.[25]
NETWIRE can use TCP in C2 communications.[26][27]

ShadowPad has used UDP for C2 communications.[42]

Umbreon provides access to the system via SSH or any other protocol that uses PAM to authenticate.[44]

WINDSHIELD C2 traffic can communicate via TCP raw sockets.[32]
Winnti for Linux has used ICMP, custom TCP, and UDP in outbound communications.[46]
/techniques/T1095===========================
APT-C-36 has used port 4050 for C2 communications.[3]
An APT32 backdoor can use HTTP over a non-standard TCP port (e.g 14146) which is specified in the backdoor configuration.[4]
APT33 has used HTTP over TCP ports 808 and 880 for command and control.[1]
BADCALL communicates on ports 443 and 8000 with a FakeTLS method.[5]
Bankshot binds and listens on port 1058 for HTTP traffic while also utilizing a FakeTLS method.[6]
BendyBear has used a custom RC4 and XOR encrypted protocol over port 443 for C2.[7]
DarkVishnya used ports 5190 and 7900 for shellcode listeners, and 4444, 4445, 31337 for shellcode C2.[8]
Derusbi has used unencrypted HTTP on port 443 for C2.[9]
Emotet has used HTTP over ports such as 20, 22, 7080, and 50000, in addition to using ports commonly associated with HTTP/S.[10]
FIN7 has used port-protocol mismatches on ports such as 53, 80, 443, and 8080 during C2.[11]
GoldenSpy has used HTTP over ports 9005 and 9006 for network traffic, 9002 for C2 requests, 33666 as a WebSocket, and 8090 to download files.[12]
GravityRAT has used HTTP over a non-standard port, such as TCP port 46769.[13]
HARDRAIN binds and listens on port 443 with a FakeTLS method.[14]
HOPLIGHT has connected outbound over TCP port 443 with a FakeTLS method.[15]
Some Lazarus Group malware uses a list of ordered port numbers to choose a port for C2 traffic, creating port-protocol mismatches.[16][17]
Magic Hound malware has communicated with its C2 server over TCP port 4443 using HTTP.[18]
Metamorfo has communicated with hosts over raw TCP on port 9999.[19] 
MoonWind communicates over ports 80, 443, 53, and 8080 via raw sockets instead of the protocols usually associated with the ports.[20]
njRAT has used port 1177 for HTTP C2 communications.[21]
PoetRAT used TLS to encrypt communications over port 143[22]
RedLeaves can use HTTP over non-standard ports, such as 995, for C2.[23]
Rocke's miner connects to a C2 server using port 51640.[24] 
RTM used Port 44443 for its VNC module.[25]
Sandworm Team has used port 6789 to accept connections on the group's SSH server.[26]
Silence has used port 444 when sending data about the system from the client to the server.[27] 
StrongPity has used HTTPS over port 1402 in C2 communication.[28]
TEMP.Veles has used port-protocol mismatches on ports such as 443, 4444, 8531, and 50501 during C2.[29]
Some TrickBot samples have used HTTP over ports 447 and 8082 for C2.[30][31][32]
TYPEFRAME has used ports 443, 8080, and 8443 with a FakeTLS method.[33]
WellMail has been observed using TCP port 25, without using SMTP, to leverage an open port for secure command and control communications.[34][35]
/techniques/T1571===========================
Chimera has encapsulated Cobalt Strike's C2 protocol in DNS and HTTPS.[3]
Cobalt Group has used the Plink utility to create SSH tunnels.[4][5][6]
Cobalt Strike uses a custom command and control protocol that is encapsulated in HTTP, HTTPS, or DNS. In addition, it conducts peer-to-peer communication over Windows named pipes encapsulated in the SMB protocol. All protocols use their standard assigned ports.[7]
Duqu uses a custom command and control protocol that communicates over commonly used ports, and is frequently encapsulated by application layer protocols.[8]
FIN6 used the Plink command-line utility to create SSH tunnels to C2 servers.[9]
FLIPSIDE uses RDP to tunnel traffic from a victim environment.[10]
Fox Kitten has used protocol tunneling for communication and RDP activity on compromised hosts through the use of open source tools such as Ngrok and custom tool SSHMinion.[11][12][13]
Ngrok can tunnel RDP and other services securely over internet connections.[14][15][16][17]
OilRig has used the Plink utility and other tools to create tunnels to C2 servers.[18][19][20]
/techniques/T1572===========================
APT29 configured at least one instance of Cobalt Strike to use a network pipe over SMB during the 2020 SolarWinds intrusion.[2]
APT39 used custom tools to create SOCK5 and custom protocol proxies between infected hosts. [3][4]
The "ZJ" variant of BACKSPACE allows "ZJ link" infections with Internet access to relay traffic from "ZJ listen" to a command server.[5]
CHOPSTICK used a proxy server between victims and the C2 server.[6]
Cobalt Strike can be configured to have commands relayed over a peer-to-peer network of infected hosts. This can be used to limit the number of egress points, or provide access to a host without direct internet access.[7]
Drovorub can use a port forwarding rule on its agent module to relay network traffic through the client module to a remote host on the same network.[8]
Duqu can be configured to have commands relayed over a peer-to-peer network of infected hosts if some of the hosts do not have Internet access.[9]
FatDuke can used pipes to connect machines with restricted internet access to remote machines via other infected hosts.[10]
Higaisa discovered system proxy settings and used them if available.[11]
Hikit supports peer connections.[12]
InvisiMole can function as a proxy to create a server that relays communication between the client and C&C server, or between two clients.[13]
Kazuar has used internal nodes on the compromised network for C2 communications.[14]
MiniDuke can can use a named pipe to forward communications from one compromised machine with internet access to other compromised machines.[10]
Operation Wocao can proxy traffic through multiple infected systems.[15]
Pay2Key has designated machines in the compromised network to serve as reverse proxy pivot points to channel communications with C2.[16][17]
Strider has used local servers with both local network and Internet access to act as internal proxy nodes to exfiltrate data from other parts of the network without direct Internet access.[18]
/techniques/T1090/001===========================
APT28 used other victims as proxies to relay command traffic, for instance using a compromised Georgian military email server as a hop point to NATO victims. The group has also used a tool that acts as a proxy to allow C2 even if the victim is behind a router. APT28 has also used a machine to relay and obscure communications between CHOPSTICK and their server.[2][3][4]
An APT3 downloader establishes SOCKS5 connections for its initial C2.[5]
APT39 has used various tools to proxy C2 communications.[6]
FIN5 maintains access to victim environments by using FLIPSIDE to create a proxy for a backup RDP tunnel.[7]
GALLIUM used a modified version of HTRAN to redirect connections between networks.[8]
InvisiMole InvisiMole can identify proxy servers used by the victim and use them for C2 communication.[9][10]
Lazarus Group uses multiple proxies to obfuscate network traffic from victims.[11][12]
menuPass has used a global service provider's IP as a proxy for C2 traffic from a victim.[13][14]
MuddyWater has controlled POWERSTATS from behind a proxy network to obfuscate the C2 location.[15] MuddyWater has used a series of compromised websites that victims connected to randomly to relay information to command and control (C2).[16][17]
Okrum can identify proxy servers configured and used by the victim, and use it to make HTTP requests to C2 its server.[18]
POWERSTATS has connected to C2 servers through proxies.[19]
Regin leveraged several compromised universities as proxies to obscure its origin.[20]
ShimRat can use pre-configured HTTP proxies.[21]
Silence has used ProxyBot, which allows the attacker to redirect traffic from the current node to the backconnect server via Sock4\Socks5.[22] 
/techniques/T1090/002===========================
APT28 has routed traffic over Tor and VPN servers to obfuscate their activities.[2]
A backdoor used by APT29 created a Tor hidden service to forward traffic from the Tor client to local ports 3389 (RDP), 139 (Netbios), and 445 (SMB) enabling full remote access from outside the network.[3]
Attor has used Tor for C2 communication.[4]
Dok downloads and installs Tor via homebrew.[5]
FIN4 has used Tor to log in to victims' email accounts.[6]
GreyEnergy has used Tor relays for Command and Control servers.[7]
Inception used chains of compromised routers to proxy C2 communications between them and cloud service providers.[8]
Keydnap uses a copy of tor2web proxy for HTTPS communications.[9]
MacSpy uses Tor for command and control.[5]
Operation Wocao has executed commands through the installed web shell via Tor exit nodes.[10]
StrongPity can use multiple layers of proxy servers to hide terminal nodes in its infrastructure.[11]
Traffic traversing the Tor network will be forwarded to multiple nodes before exiting the Tor network and continuing on to its intended destination.[12]
Ursnif has used Tor for C2.[13][14]
WannaCry uses Tor for command and control traffic.[15]
/techniques/T1090/003===========================
APT29 has used the meek domain fronting plugin for Tor to hide the destination of C2 traffic.[2]
meek uses Domain Fronting to disguise the destination of network traffic as another server that is hosted in the same Content Delivery Network (CDN) as the intended destination.

PlugX uses Pastebin to store C2 addresses.[13]

RTM has used an RSS feed on Livejournal to update a list of encrypted C2 server names.[15]

/techniques/T1020/001===========================
Carbanak exfiltrates data in compressed chunks if a message is larger than 4096 bytes .[1]
Helminth splits data into chunks up to 23 bytes and sends the data in DNS queries to its C2 server.[2]
Kessel can split the data to be exilftrated into chunks that will fit in subdomains of DNS queries.[3]
OopsIE exfiltrates command output and collected files to its C2 server in 1500-byte blocks.[4]
POSHSPY uploads data in 2048-byte chunks.[5]
RDAT can upload a file via HTTP POST response to the C2 split into 102,400-byte portions. RDAT can also download data from the C2 which is split into 81,920-byte portions.[6] 
Threat Group-3390 actors have split RAR files for exfiltration into parts.[7]

/techniques/T1048/002===========================
Agent Tesla has routines for exfiltration over SMTP, FTP, and HTTP.[1][2][3]

CookieMiner has used the curl --upload-file command to exfiltrate data over HTTP.[10]

CosmicDuke exfiltrates collected files over FTP or WebDAV. Exfiltration servers can be separately configured from C2 servers.[12]

FIN8 has used FTP to exfiltrate collected data.[14]
FTP may be used to exfiltrate data separate from the main command and control protocol.[15]

KONNI has used FTP to exfiltrate reconnaissance data out.[17]

PoetRAT has used FTP for exfiltration.[21]

Thrip has used WinSCP to exfiltrate data from a targeted organization over FTP.[23]

Wizard Spider has exfiltrated victim information using FTP.[25][26]

/techniques/T1531===========================
APT38 has used a custom secure delete function to make deleted files unrecoverable.[9]
BlackEnergy 2 contains a "Destroy" plug-in that destroys data stored on victim hard drives by overwriting file contents.[10][11]
Kazuar can overwrite files with random data before deleting them.[12]
Lazarus Group has used a custom secure delete function to overwrite file contents with data from heap memory.[13]
Olympic Destroyer overwrites files locally and on remote shares.[6][14] 
PowerDuke has a command to write random data across a file and delete it.[15]
Proxysvc can overwrite files indicated by the attacker before deleting them.[16]
RawDisk was used in Shamoon to write to protected system locations such as the MBR and disk partitions in an effort to destroy data.[3][5]
REvil has the capability to destroy files and folders.[17][18][19][19][20][21][22]
Sandworm Team has used the BlackEnergy KillDisk component to overwrite files on Windows-based Human-Machine Interfaces. [23][24]
SDelete deletes data in a way that makes it unrecoverable.[25]
Shamoon attempts to overwrite operating system files and disk structures with image files.[1][2][3] In a later variant, randomly generated data was used for data overwrites.[5][26]
StoneDrill has a disk wiper module that targets files other than those in the Windows directory.[4]
Xbash has destroyed Linux-based databases as part of its ransomware capabilities.[27] 
/techniques/T1485===========================
APT38 has used Hermes ransomware to encrypt files with AES256.[6]
APT41 used a ransomware called Encryptor RaaS to encrypt files on the targeted systems and provide a ransom note to the user.[7]
BitPaymer can import a hard-coded RSA 1024-bit public key, generate a 128-bit RC4 key for each file, and encrypt the file in place, appending .locked to the filename.[8]
Conti can use CreateIoCompletionPort(), PostQueuedCompletionStatus(), and GetQueuedCompletionPort() to rapidly encrypt files, excluding those with the extensions of .exe, .dll, and .lnk. It has used a different AES-256 encryption key per file with a bundled RAS-4096 public encryption key that is unique for each victim. Conti can use "Windows Restart Manager" to ensure files are unlocked and open for encryption.[9][10][11]
Egregor can encrypt all non-system files using a hybrid AES-RSA algorithm prior to displaying a ransom note.[12][13] 
Indrik Spider has encrypted domain-controlled systems using BitPaymer.[8]
JCry has encrypted files and demanded Bitcoin to decrypt those files. [14]
LockerGoga has encrypted files, including core Windows OS files, using RSA-OAEP MGF1 and then demanded Bitcoin be paid for the decryption key.[15][16][17]
Maze has disrupted systems by encrypting files on targeted machines, claiming to decrypt files if a ransom payment is made. Maze has used the ChaCha algorithm, based on Salsa20, and an RSA algorithm to encrypt files.[18]
MegaCortex has used the open-source library, Mbed Crypto, and generated AES keys to carry out the file encryption process.[19][20]
Netwalker can encrypt files on infected machines to extort victims.[21] 
NotPetya encrypts user files and disk structures like the MBR with 2048-bit RSA.[22][3][23]
Pay2Key can encrypt data on victim's machines using RSA and AES algorithms in order to extort a ransom payment for decryption.[24][25]
Pysa has used RSA and AES-CBC encryption algorithm to encrypt a list of targeted file extensions.[26] 
Ragnar Locker encrypts files on the local machine and mapped drives prior to displaying a note demanding a ransom.[27][28]
REvil can encrypt files on victim systems and demands a ransom to decrypt the files.[29][30][31][32][33][34][35][36]
RobbinHood will search for an RSA encryption key and then perform its encryption process on the system files.[37] 
Ryuk has used a combination of symmetric (AES) and asymmetric (RSA) encryption to encrypt files. Files have been encrypted with their own AES key and given a file extension of .RYK. Encrypted directories have had a ransom note of RyukReadMe.txt written to the directory.[38]
SamSam encrypts victim files using RSA-2048 encryption and demands a ransom be paid in Bitcoin to decrypt those files.[39]
Shamoon has an operational mode for encrypting data instead of overwriting it.[40][41]
SynAck encrypts the victims machine followed by asking the victim to pay a ransom. [42]
TA505 has used a wide variety of ransomware, such as Locky, Jaff, Bart, Philadelphia, and GlobeImposter, to encrypt victim files and demand a ransom payment.[43]
ThiefQuest encrypts a set of file extensions on a host, deletes the original files, and provides a ransom note with no contact information.[44]
WannaCry encrypts user files and demands that a ransom be paid in Bitcoin to decrypt those files.[45][2][46]
Xbash has maliciously encrypted victim's database systems and demanded a cryptocurrency ransom be paid.[47]
/techniques/T1486===========================
APT38 has used DYEPACK to create, delete, and alter records in databases used for SWIFT transactions.[1]
FIN4 has created rules in victims' Microsoft Outlook accounts to automatically delete emails containing words such as "hacked," "phish," and "malware" in a likely attempt to prevent organizations from communicating about their activities.[3]
SUNSPOT created a copy of the SolarWinds Orion software source file with a .bk extension to backup the original content, wrote SUNBURST using the same filename but with a .tmp extension, and then moved SUNBURST using MoveFileEx to the original filename with a .cs extension so it could be compiled within Orion software.[4]
/techniques/T1565/001===========================
APT38 has used DYEPACK to manipulate SWIFT messages en route to a printer.[1]

Metamorfo has a function that can watch the contents of the system clipboard for valid bitcoin addresses, which it then overwrites with the attacker's address.[5]

/techniques/T1491/001===========================
Sandworm Team defaced approximately 15,000 websites belonging to Georgian government, non-government, and private sector organizations in 2019.[5][6]
/techniques/T1491/002===========================
Lazarus Group has used malware like WhiskeyAlfa to overwrite the first 64MB of every drive with a mix of static and random buffers. A similar process is then used to wipe content in logical drives and, finally, attempt to wipe every byte of every sector on every drive. WhiskeyBravo can be used to overwrite the first 4.9MB of physical drives. WhiskeyDelta can overwrite the first 132MB or 1.5MB of each drive with random data from heap memory.[2]
MegaCortex can wipe deleted data from all drives using cipher.exe.[4]
RawDisk has been used to directly access the hard disk to help overwrite arbitrarily sized portions of disk content.[2]
StoneDrill can wipe the accessible physical or logical drives of the infected machine.[5] 
/techniques/T1561/001===========================
APT37 has access to destructive malware that is capable of overwriting a machine's Master Boot Record (MBR).[6][7]
APT38 has used a custom MBR wiper named BOOTWRECK to render systems inoperable.[8]
Lazarus Group malware SHARPKNOT overwrites and deletes the Master Boot Record (MBR) on the victim's machine and has possessed MBR wiper malware since at least 2009.[9][10]
RawDisk was used in Shamoon to help overwrite components of disk structure like the MBR and disk partitions.[3][5]
Sandworm Team has used the BlackEnergy KillDisk component to corrupt the infected system's master boot record.[11][12]
Shamoon has been seen overwriting features of disk structure such as the MBR.[1][2][3][5]
StoneDrill can wipe the master boot record of an infected computer.[13]

Netwalker can delete the infected system's Shadow Volumes to prevent recovery.[11][12]

Pysa has the functionality to delete shadow copies.[13]

RobbinHood deletes shadow copies to ensure that all the data cannot be restored easily.[24] 
Ryuk has used vssadmin Delete Shadows /all /quiet to to delete volume shadow copies and vssadmin resize shadowstorage to force deletion of shadow copies created by third-party applications.[25]
WannaCry uses vssadmin, wbadmin, bcdedit, and wmic to delete and disable operating system recovery features.[26][2][27]

/techniques/T1496===========================
Conti can stop up to 146 Windows services related to security, backup, database, and email solutions through the use of net stop.[4]
HotCroissant has the ability to stop services on the infected host.[5]
Lazarus Group has stopped the MSExchangeIS service to render Exchange contents inaccessible to users.[6]
LookBack can kill processes and delete services.[7]
Maze has stopped SQL services to ensure it can encrypt any database.[8] 
MegaCortex can stop and disable services on the system.[9] 
Netwalker can terminate system processes and services, some of which relate to backup software.[10]
Olympic Destroyer uses the API call ChangeServiceConfigW to disable all services on the affected system.[1]
Pay2Key can stop the MS SQL service at the end of the encryption process to release files locked by the service.[11]
Pysa can stop services and processes.[12] 
Ragnar Locker has attempted to stop services associated with business applications and databases to release the lock on files used by these applications so they may be encrypted.[13]
REvil has the capability to stop services and kill processes.[14][15]
RobbinHood stops 181 Windows services on the system before beginning the encryption process.[16] 
Ryuk has called kill.bat for stopping services, disabling services and killing processes.[17]
SLOTHFULMEDIA has the capability to stop processes and services.[18]
WannaCry attempts to kill processes associated with Exchange, Microsoft SQL Server, and MySQL to make it possible to encrypt their data stores.[19][3]
Wizard Spider has used taskkill.exe and net.exe to stop backup, catalog, cloud, and other services prior to network encryption.[20]
/techniques/T1489===========================
APT37 has used malware that will issue the command shutdown /r /t 1 to reboot a system after wiping its MBR.[4]
APT38 has used a custom MBR wiper named BOOTWRECK, which will initiate a system reboot after wiping the victim's MBR.[5]
Lazarus Group has rebooted systems after destroying files and wiping the MBR on infected systems.[6]
LockerGoga has been observed shutting down infected systems.[7]
LookBack can shutdown and reboot the victim machine.[8]
Maze has issued a shutdown command on a victim machine that, upon reboot, will run the ransomware within a VM.[9]
NotPetya will reboot the system one hour after infection.[2][10]
Olympic Destroyer will shut down the compromised system after it is done modifying system configuration settings.[3][10]
Shamoon will reboot the infected system once the wiping functionality has been completed.[11][12]
